Salah — Prayer
beginner
8 min
Ruling on Reciting Fatiha in the First Two Rak'ahs
Ruling on Fatiha and surah recitation in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs of fard and identify the consequence of omitting it.

Core Idea
Leaving Fatiha invalidates the prayer; leaving a surah does not.

In the Hanafi school, recitation of Fatiha holds a unique status: its omission in the first two rak'ahs of obligatory prayer requires repeating the prayer, whereas omitting a surah does not. This lesson clarifies the precise ruling, the role of sajdah al-sahw, and the exceptional case when one fears missing the prayer time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act being ruled
The passage rules on reciting Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs of obligatory prayer (fard).
2
Determine the hukm
The text says leaving Fatiha requires repeating the prayer, indicating it is a necessary component (wajib).
This is stronger than a sunnah but not a rukn.
3
Compare with surah
Leaving a surah does not require repetition, so it is at a lower level.
Surah may be wajib but omission only triggers sajdah al-sahw.
4
Consider the exception
If one fears missing the prayer time, reciting one ayah suffices instead of Fatiha and surah.
This dispensation is from al-Qunyah.
5
Note the later clarification
The passage clarifies where Fatiha is wajib: first two of fard, all nafl, witr, Eid; sunnah in last two.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة - باب صفة الصلاة
هـ.
إذا ترك الفاتحة في الصلاة يؤمر بإعادة الصلاة ولو ترك قراءة السورة لا يؤمر بالإعادة ا لا فرق بين واجب وواجب إلا أن يقال: إنه ترك السورة وقرأ ثلاث آيات وهو بعيد جداً.
ثم اعلم أنهم قالوا في باب سجود السهو إنه لو ترك أكثر الفاتحة يجب عليه سجود السهو، ولو ترك أقلها لا يجب وظاهره أن الفاتحة بتمامها ليست بواجبة وإنما الواجب أكثرها ولا يعرى عن تأمل. وفي القنية : يخاف المصلي فوت الوقت إن قرأ الفاتحة والسورة يجوز أن يقرأ في كل ركعة بآية في جميع الصلوات إن خاف فوت الوقت بالزيادة ا هـ. ثم الفاتحة واجبة في الأوليين من الفرض وفي جميع ركعات النفل وفي الوتر والعيدين، وأما في الأخريين من الفرض فسنة كما سيأتي.
Book of Prayer - Chapter on Description of Prayer. If one leaves the Fatiha in prayer, he is ordered to repeat the prayer. And if one leaves the recitation of a surah, he is not ordered to repeat. There is no difference between an obligatory act and an obligatory act, unless it is said that he left the surah and recited three verses, which is very far. Then know that they said in the chapter of prostration of forgetfulness: if one leaves most of the Fatiha, the prostration of forgetfulness becomes obligatory on him; if he leaves less than that, it does not become obligatory. Its apparent meaning is that the entire Fatiha is not obligatory, but rather most of it is obligatory, and this is not free from reflection. In al-Qunyah: If the praying person fears the time will expire if he recites the Fatiha and a surah, it is permissible for him to recite one verse in every rak'ah in all prayers if he fears the time will expire by the addition. Then the Fatiha is obligatory in the first two of obligatory prayer, and in all rak'ahs of supererogatory prayer, and in the witr and the two Eid prayers. As for the last two of obligatory prayer, it is sunnah, as will come.
Source pages p. 516

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq. It begins by establishing the essential distinction: leaving the Fatiha in prayer necessitates repeating the entire prayer, whereas leaving the recitation of a surah (after Fatiha) does not. This indicates that the obligation (wujub) of Fatiha is much stronger. The author then addresses an objection that both are wajib, so why the difference? He dismisses it by noting the unlikely scenario of someone leaving the surah but reciting three verses (which suffices in place of a surah). The discussion moves to the prostration of forgetfulness (sajdah al-sahw): leaving the majority of Fatiha triggers sajdah al-sahw, meaning the Fatiha as a whole is not wajib but only its majority. This is a subtle Hanafi position. The passage also provides a dispensation: if one fears missing the prayer time by reciting Fatiha and a surah, it is permissible to recite just one ayah per rak'ah. Finally, it clarifies where Fatiha is wajib: in the first two rak'ahs of fard, all rak'ahs of nafl, witr, and Eid; in the last two of fard it is only sunnah.

Key Terms
الفاتحة (al-Fatiha): The opening chapter of the Quran, consisting of seven verses.
السورة (al-Surah): A chapter of the Quran; here implying any surah or at least three short verses after Fatiha.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a person leaves the entire Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs of an obligatory prayer?
A) The prayer is valid and no compensation is needed
B) He must repeat the prayer
C) He must perform sajdah al-sahw
D) The prayer is invalid and he must repeat it

Key Takeaway
Fatiha is wajib in the first two rak'ahs of fard; total omission invalidates the prayer and requires repetition.

The Obligation of Adding a Surah After Fatiha
Proves wajib status of adding surah after Fatiha and clarifies its scope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adding a surah after Fatiha, identify the proof from the hadith, and explain the wajh al-dalalah that supports wujub.

Core Idea
Adding a surah after Fatiha is wajib in the first two rak‘ahs—omission requires sajdah al-sahw.

This lesson examines a key feature of the Hanafi prayer: the obligation to recite a surah (or three short verses) after al-Fatiha in the first two rak‘ahs of fard salah and in all rak‘ahs of nafl, witr, and Eid. While other schools consider this recommended, the Hanafi school relies on a clear prophetic hadith and the principle that a negative imperative indicates invalidity. Understanding this ruling is essential for correct prayer and for recognizing when sajdah al-sahw becomes necessary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what hukm level applies. The act is adding a surah after Fatiha. The hukm level is wajib in the first two rak'ahs of fard and all of nafl/witr/Eid; not wajib in the last two of fard.
Hanafi distinction: wajib (not fard) because the proof is zanni al-thubut.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited. The commentator relies on a marfu' hadith from Tirmidhi: 'لا صلاة لمن لم يقرأ بالحمد وسورة في فريضة أو غيرها'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith proves wujub. The negative particle 'لا' negates validity (nafy al-sihhah) when attached to 'صلاة'. The conjunction of 'سورة' with 'الحمد' shows both are required. In Hanafi usul, the construction indicates wujub.
The term 'سورة' is interpreted as three short verses, based on the smallest surah in the Quran being three verses.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the opposing view. The three Imams (Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad) consider adding a surah sunnah, interpreting the hadith as recommendation.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical difference. For a Hanafi, omitting the surah in the first two rak'ahs requires sajdah al-sahw; for a Shafi'i, no sajdah is needed.

Source Text

قوله : (وضم سورة) وعند الأئمة الثلاثة سنة ولنا رواية الترمذي مرفوعاً «لا صلاة لمن لم يقرأ بالحمد وسورة في فريضة أو غيرها (۱) أطلق السورة وأراد بها ثلاث آيات لأن أقل سورة في كتاب الله تعالى ثلاث آيات أكثرها فقد تركها حكماً لأن للأكثر حكم الكل فيجب عليه السجود، وأما إذا ترك أقلها فلا يكون تاركاً لها حقيقة ولا حكماً اهـ. ولا يخفى عليك أن ما ذكره إنما هو وجه للفرق بين ترك الأكثر والأقل ولا نزاع فيه الترتيب الواجب الخ) قال في النهر : هذا وهم إذ الترتيب بين الركعات ليس إلا واجباً. قال في الفتح: إلا أنه سقط في حق المسبوق لضرورة الاقتداء وما في الشرح مأخوذ من الخبازية والنهاية وعليه جرى في الدراية والفتح .اهـ. وكأنه ذكر ذلك في النهاية في غير هذا المحل وإلا فالذي هنا موافق لما في الكافي كما مر . ثم حاصل كلام النهر أن ما فهمه في البحر من كلام الشارح الزيلعي أن الترتيب في الركعات واجب على المسبوق غير صحيح، بل الوجوب على غيره وأنه ليس بفرض وإلا لما سقط عن المسبوق بدليل قوله فإن ما يقضيه المسبوق أول صلاته ولو كان الترتيب واجباً عليه لحكمنا على أن ما أدركه مع الإمام أول صلاته وما يقضيه آخرها إذ ليس في وسعه إيقاع ما أدركه أولاً في الآخر، أو لحكمنا عليه بأن يصلي أولاً ركعتين مثلاً ثم يتابع الإمام وذلك غير جائز، بل يجب عليه متابعته وقضاء ما فاته من أول صلاته وهذا دليل على عدم فرضيته، وهذا بعينه معنى ما في الفتح حيث قال: قوله فيما شرع مكرراً من «الأفعال» أراد به ما تكرر في كل الصلاة كالركعات إلا لضرورة الاقتداء حيث يسقط به الترتيب، فإن المسبوق يصلي آخر الركعات قبل أولها أو في كل ركعة اهـ. وبهذا التقرير ظهر لك عدم صحة ما اعترضه بعضهم على النهر بقوله «بل أن هو الواهم. لأن ما استشهد به من كلام الفتح صريح في الرد عليه .هـ. بقي هنا إشكال وهو المصلي إما منفرداً وإمام أو مأموم، ولا يتصور وجوب الترتيب بين الركعات في حق الأولين لأن كل ركعة يأتيان بها أولاً فهي الأولى وثانياً فهي الثانية وهلم جراً. وأما المأموم فهو إما مدرك أو مسبوق
His saying: (and add a surah) — and according to the three Imams it is sunnah. And we have the narration of Tirmidhi, raised: 'No prayer for the one who does not recite al-Hamd and a surah in an obligatory or other prayer.' He used the general term 'surah' but he meant by it three verses, because the smallest surah in the Book of Allah is three short verses like surah 'Inna a'taynaka al-kawthar'. He did not intend the complete surah, as evidenced by what will come explicitly in his speech. And this addition is obligatory in the first two of obligatory prayer and in all rak'ahs of supererogatory and witr, like the Fatiha. As for the last two of obligatory prayer, it is not obligatory nor sunnah, but rather permissible. So if one adds a surah to the Fatiha in the last two, it is not disliked, as was transmitted in Ghayat al-Bayan from Fakhr al-Islam, and it will come clearer than this if Allah wills. His saying: (and specifying the recitation in the first two) — i.e., specifying the first two of the three- and four-rak'ah obligatory prayers for the obligatory recitation. So if he recited in the last two of the four-rak'ah without the first two, or in one of the first two and one of the last two out of forgetfulness, sajdah al-sahw becomes obligatory on him, based on the position that the place of obligatory recitation is the first two specifically, and that is correct, as will come in the chapter on witr and supererogatory. And according to the opinion of non-specification, [the recitation is] neither fard nor wajib, and sajdah al-sahw is not obligatory, and it will come that this is weak. Then know that in the matter of the obligatory recitation there are two other obligatory [elements] that the author did not mention explicitly: one is the obligation of placing the Fatiha before the surah due to the constant practice being established. They said: if one recites a letter of the surah before the Fatiha forgetfully then remembers, he recites the Fatiha then the surah, and sajdah al-sahw is required of him. And in the author's speech there is an indication to that where he said: 'and add a surah' because it implies [precedence], and accordingly every verse is obligatory. His saying: 'Its apparent meaning is that the entire Fatiha' etc. He said in al-Minh: I say: its apparent meaning does not indicate what he mentioned because the obligation of prostration is only by leaving it, and when he leaves most of it, he has left it effectively, because the majority has the ruling of the whole, so prostration is required of him. But when he leaves less than that, he is not leaving it in reality nor effectively. And it is not hidden from you that what he mentioned is only a way to distinguish between leaving the majority and leaving the minority, and there is no dispute in that, since it concedes that leaving the minority does not require sajdah al-sahw, and that is clear in what he said. His saying: (and he restricted it in al-Kafi to what is repeated in every rak'ah like the prostration) I say: and likewise in al-Nihayah, al-Inayah, al-Kifayah, and Ghayat al-Bayan. His saying: (and it is not correct to include it under the obligatory order) etc. He said in al-Nahr: This is a mistake, for the order among rak'ahs is nothing but wajib. He said in al-Fath: except that it is dropped for the one who is preceded out of necessity of following. And what is in the commentary is taken from al-Khabbaziyyah and al-Nihayah, and upon it proceeded in al-Dirayah and al-Fath. It seems that he mentioned it in al-Nihayah in a different place, for what is here agrees with al-Kafi as passed. Then the gist of the speech of al-Nahr is that what was understood in al-Bahr from the speech of the commentator al-Zayla'i – that the order in rak'ahs is wajib upon the one who is preceded – is not correct. Rather, the obligation is upon others, and it is not fard, because then it would not be dropped for the one who is preceded, as evidenced by his saying: 'for what the one who is preceded performs later is the beginning of his prayer.' If the order were wajib upon him, we would have judged that what he catches with the imam is the beginning of his prayer and what he performs later is the end of it, since he cannot place what he caught first in the end, or we would have judged that he should pray two rak'ahs first then follow the imam, which is not permissible. Rather, he must follow him and make up what he missed from the beginning of his prayer, and this is evidence of it not being fard. This is exactly the meaning of what is in al-Fath where he said: his saying regarding what is legislated as repeated from 'actions' he meant what is repeated in the entire prayer like the rak'ahs, except due to necessity of following, where the order is dropped. So the one who is preceded prays the last rak'ahs before the first, or in every rak'ah. With this explanation, it becomes clear to you the incorrectness of what some objected to al-Nahr with, saying 'rather he is the one who is deluded', because what he cited from the speech of al-Fath is clear in refuting him. There remains an objection: the praying person is either alone, an imam, or a follower. And the obligation of order among rak'ahs cannot be conceived for the first two, because every rak'ah they perform first is the first, and second is the second, and so on. As for the follower, he is either one who catches [the prayer from the beginning] or one who is preceded.
Source pages p. 516

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq. It begins by discussing the obligation of adding a surah after Fatiha. The commentator provides the proof: a hadith from Tirmidhi (marfu'): 'No prayer for one who does not recite al-Hamd and a surah.' The term 'surah' is interpreted as three short verses, as the shortest surah in the Quran is three verses. This addition (damm) is wajib in the first two rak'ahs of fard, all rak'ahs of nafl, and witr, like Fatiha. In the last two of fard, it is not wajib but permissible (mashru'). The commentator then explains 'ta'yin al-qira'ah fi al-ulayayn': the obligatory recitation is specifically in the first two rak'ahs. If one forgetfully recites in the last two or in only one of the first two, sajdah al-sahw is required. This is the correct view. Two other wajib issues are mentioned implicitly: (1) Fatiha must precede the surah (precedence is obligatory even in nafl), and (2) Fatiha must not be recited more than once in a single rak'ah (though there is a detail from Fatawa Qadikhan: if recited twice consecutively, sajdah al-sahw is needed; if separated by a surah, it is not). The passage also includes a discussion about the order (tartib) of repeated actions, focusing on the masbuq (one who joins late). The commentator clarifies that tartib in rak'ahs is wajib, but it is dropped for the masbuq due to necessity, as he cannot observe the sequence and must follow the imam. This is evidence that tartib is not fard (otherwise it would not be dropped). The passage refutes a misunderstanding about the masbuq's prayer being considered first in ruling (hukman) not reality.

Key Terms
ضم سورة (damm surah): Reciting a surah (or at least three short verses) immediately after Fatiha in prayer.
التعيين (al-ta'yin): The specification of the first two rak'ahs for the obligatory recitation.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration to compensate for forgetfulness, required when an obligatory element is omitted or delayed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on adding a surah after Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah fard prayer?
A) Wajib
B) Sunnah
C) Permissible (mashru')
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
Adding a surah after al-Fatiha is wajib in the first two rak'ahs of fard and all of nafl/witr/Eid; omission requires sajdah al-sahw.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Ruling on Tartib: Fard or Wajib? The Masbuq Exception
Critical refinement of the ruling on tartib in repeated actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that tartib in rak'ahs is wajib (not fard) and is dropped for the masbuq, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on this issue.

Core Idea
Tartib in rak'ahs is wajib, not fard; it is dropped for the masbuq by necessity.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author engages in a critical refinement of a previous commentary by al-Zayla'i. The central question is whether observing the correct order (tartib) of repeated actions in prayer—especially the sequence of rak'ahs—is fard (invalidating if omitted) or wajib (compensable with sajdah al-sahw). The dispute is not theoretical; it directly affects the masbuq (latecomer) who cannot physically observe the order while following the imam. By the end of this lesson, you will not only know the Hanafi ruling but also understand the precise legal reasoning that supports it.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the act and the dispute
First, recognise that the issue is about 'tartib' in repeated actions (fi'l mukarrar). The two categories are: actions repeated within a rak'ah (like the two prostrations) and actions repeated across the entire prayer (rak'ahs themselves). The dispute centres on the second category.
The passage also mentions that for actions within a rak'ah, there is no dispute: if you omit the second sajdah and stand, the prayer is not invalidated.
2
2. State the two intra-Hanafi positions
One position (implied by the sharh and some sources like al-Kafi) treats tartib in rak'ahs as fard, meaning the masbuq must observe it strictly. The other position (the mufta bihi) holds that it is wajib, and is dropped for the masbuq due to necessity.
The difference is subtle but important: fard would invalidate the prayer if omitted; wajib does not invalidate but may require sajdah al-sahw—except here it is waived entirely.
3
3. Analyse the proof for the wajib position
The key evidence is the situation of the masbuq: if tartib were fard, the masbuq would have to pray his missed rak'ahs before continuing with the imam, which is impossible while following. Therefore, tartib cannot be fard. It is thus wajib, and the obligation is temporarily lifted for the masbuq.
The passage uses the principle of 'idhtirar' (necessity) to justify the exception.
4
4. Understand the exception for the masbuq
The masbuq's prayer is considered 'first in ruling' (hukman) for recitation but 'last in ruling' for tashahhud. This hybrid nature does not require observing the order of rak'ahs. The masbuq simply follows the imam and then makes up missed rak'ahs; the order is not required.
This resolves the apparent contradiction: the masbuq prays his second (last) rak'ah before his first (missed) rak'ah, but this is allowed by necessity.
5
5. Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If one believed tartib in rak'ahs is fard, the masbuq's prayer would be invalid if he violates order—he would have to repeat it. In the Hanafi view, his prayer is valid and no compensation is needed for the order itself. This difference has real implications for daily congregational prayer.
The passage refutes an objection that the masbuq's prayer is 'first in ruling' in reality; it clarifies that the order is not fard.

Source Text

قوله : ( ورعاية الترتيب في فعل (مكرر) أطلقه هنا وقيده في الكافي بالمتكرر في كل ركعة كالسجدة حتى لو ترك السجدة الثانية وقام إلى الركعة الثانية لا تفسد صلاته. وزاد عليه الشارح أو يكون متكرراً في جميع الصلاة كعدد الركعات فإن ما يقضيه المسبوق بعد فراغ الإمام أول صلاته عندنا ولو كان الترتيب فرضاً لكان آخراً ا هـ. وهو مردود فإن ما يقضيه المسبوق أول صلاته حكماً لا حقيقة. وأيضاً ليس أول صلاته مطلقاً بل أولها في حق القراءة وآخرها في حق التشهد على ما سيأتي . ولا يصح أن يدخل تحت الترتيب الواجب إذ من هو الأقل لا يوجب سجود السهو وهو ظاهر فيما قاله قوله : ( وقيده في الكافي بالمتكرر في كل ركعة كالسجدة) أقول: وكذا في النهاية والعناية والكفاية وغاية البيان قوله : (ولا يصح أن يدخل تحت الترتيب الواجب الخ) قال في النهر : هذا وهم إذ الترتيب بين الركعات ليس إلا واجباً. قال في الفتح: إلا أنه سقط في حق المسبوق لضرورة الاقتداء وما في الشرح مأخوذ من الخبازية والنهاية وعليه جرى في الدراية والفتح .اهـ. وكأنه ذكر ذلك في النهاية في غير هذا المحل وإلا فالذي هنا موافق لما في الكافي كما مر . ثم حاصل كلام النهر أن ما فهمه في البحر من كلام الشارح الزيلعي أن الترتيب في الركعات واجب على المسبوق غير صحيح، بل الوجوب على غيره وأنه ليس بفرض وإلا لما سقط عن المسبوق بدليل قوله فإن ما يقضيه المسبوق أول صلاته ولو كان الترتيب واجباً عليه لحكمنا على أن ما أدركه مع الإمام أول صلاته وما يقضيه آخرها إذ ليس في وسعه إيقاع ما أدركه أولاً في الآخر، أو لحكمنا عليه بأن يصلي أولاً ركعتين مثلاً ثم يتابع الإمام وذلك غير جائز، بل يجب عليه متابعته وقضاء ما فاته من أول صلاته وهذا دليل على عدم فرضيته، وهذا بعينه معنى ما في الفتح حيث قال: قوله فيما شرع مكرراً من «الأفعال» أراد به ما تكرر في كل الصلاة كالركعات إلا لضرورة الاقتداء حيث يسقط به الترتيب، فإن المسبوق يصلي آخر الركعات قبل أولها أو في كل ركعة اهـ. وبهذا التقرير ظهر لك عدم صحة ما اعترضه بعضهم على النهر بقوله «بل هو الواهم. لأن ما استشهد به من كلام الفتح صريح في الرد عليه .هـ. بقي هنا إشكال وهو المصلي إما منفرداً وإمام أو مأموم، ولا يتصور وجوب الترتيب بين الركعات في حق الأولين لأن كل ركعة يأتيان بها أولاً فهي الأولى وثانياً فهي الثانية وهلم جراً. وأما المأموم فهو إما مدرك أو مسبوق
His saying: (and observing order in repeated action) — he left it unrestricted here, and restricted it in al-Kafi to what is repeated in every rak'ah like the prostration, so that if he leaves the second prostration and stands up for the second rak'ah, his prayer is not invalidated. And the commentator added: or it is repeated in the entire prayer like the number of rak'ahs, for what the masbuq performs after the imam finishes is the beginning of his prayer according to us, and if the order were fard, it would be the end. He said: it is rejected, for what the masbuq performs later is the beginning of his prayer in ruling, not in reality. Also, it is not absolutely the beginning of his prayer, but rather it is the beginning with respect to recitation and the end with respect to tashahhud, as will come. And it is not correct to include it under the obligatory order, because [if it were] the lesser [action] would not require sajdah al-sahw, and it is clear in what he said. He said: (and he restricted it in al-Kafi to what is repeated in every rak'ah like the prostration) I say: and likewise in al-Nihayah, al-Inayah, al-Kifayah, and Ghayat al-Bayan. His saying: (and it is not correct to include it under the obligatory order) etc. He said in al-Nahr: This is a mistake, for the order among rak'ahs is nothing but wajib. He said in al-Fath: except that it is dropped for the masbuq due to necessity of following. And what is in the commentary is taken from al-Khabbaziyyah and al-Nihayah, and upon it proceeded in al-Dirayah and al-Fath. It seems that he mentioned it in al-Nihayah in a different place, for what is here agrees with al-Kafi as passed. Then the gist of the speech of al-Nahr is that what was understood in al-Bahr from the speech of the commentator al-Zayla'i – that the order in rak'ahs is wajib upon the masbuq – is not correct. Rather, the obligation is upon others, and it is not fard, because then it would not be dropped for the masbuq, as evidenced by his saying: 'for what the masbuq performs later is the beginning of his prayer.' If the order were wajib upon him, we would have judged that what he catches with the imam is the beginning of his prayer and what he performs later is the end of it, since he cannot place what he caught first in the end, or we would have judged that he should pray two rak'ahs first then follow the imam, which is not permissible. Rather, he must follow him and make up what he missed from the beginning of his prayer, and this is evidence of it not being fard. This is exactly the meaning of what is in al-Fath where he said: his saying regarding what is legislated as repeated from 'actions' he meant what is repeated in the entire prayer like the rak'ahs, except due to necessity of following, where the order is dropped. So the masbuq prays the last rak'ahs before the first, or in every rak'ah. With this explanation, it becomes clear to you the incorrectness of what some objected to al-Nahr with, saying 'rather he is the one who is deluded', because what he cited from the speech of al-Fath is clear in refuting him. There remains an objection: the praying person is either alone, an imam, or a follower. And the obligation of order among rak'ahs cannot be conceived for the first two, because every rak'ah they perform first is the first, and second is the second, and so on. As for the follower, he is either one who catches [the prayer from the beginning] or one who is preceded.
Source pages p. 517

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of a previous commentary (sharh) by Zayla'i. It addresses the ruling on observing order (tartib) in repeated actions of prayer. The commentator initially restricted tartib to actions repeated within a single rak'ah (like the two prostrations), but the sharh extended it to actions repeated across the entire prayer (like rak'ahs). The dispute is whether tartib is fard (obligatory in a way that invalidates prayer if omitted) or wajib (obligatory but compensable with sajdah al-sahw). The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq argues that it is wajib, not fard, and that it is dropped entirely for the masbuq (one who joins the prayer late) due to necessity. The argument uses the example of the masbuq: if tartib were fard, the masbuq would have to pray his missed rak'ahs first, which is impossible while following the imam. Therefore, tartib is not fard. The passage also clarifies that for a person praying alone or the imam, the order is naturally observed, so it is not an issue. The discussion refutes an objection that the masbuq's prayer is only 'first in ruling' (hukman), not in reality, and that the order in rak'ahs is still wajib on others. The conclusion is that tartib in rak'ahs is wajib but waived for the masbuq by necessity.

Key Terms
الترتيب (al-tartib): Observing the correct sequence of actions in prayer, such as performing sajda before standing, or rak'ahs in order.
المسبوق (al-masbuq): A person who joins the congregational prayer late and misses one or more rak'ahs.
فعل مكرر (fi'l mukarrar): An action that is repeated within the prayer, such as sujood (twice per rak'ah) or rak'ahs themselves.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on tartib (order) in rak'ahs for the masbuq (latecomer)?
A) It is fard and must be observed strictly.
B) It is wajib and must be observed, but if not, sajdah al-sahw is required.
C) It is wajib but is dropped for the masbuq due to necessity.
D) It is not required at all for anyone.

Key Takeaway
Tartib in rak'ahs is wajib but waived for the masbuq; this ruling balances the obligation of order with the necessity of following the imam.

Ruling on Reciting Surah al-Fatihah Twice in One Rak'ah
Clarifying the ruling on repeating al-Fatihah and when sajda sahw is wajib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting al-Fatihah twice in one rak'ah, identify when sajda sahw becomes wajib, and explain the reasoning behind the distinction between consecutive and separated recitation.

Core Idea
Reciting al-Fatihah twice consecutively delays the wajib surah, requiring sajda sahw; separating with a surah avoids delay, so no sajda.

In this passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq, the author discusses a specific detail regarding the repetition of Surah al-Fatihah in a single rak'ah. While the general rule is that repeating Fatihah obligates sajda sahw, a later specification from Fatawa Qadikhan restricts this obligation to cases where the two recitations are consecutive. This distinction is based on whether a wajib element (the surah after Fatihah) is delayed. Understanding this ruling will help you apply the correct fiqh position in prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
The general rule, as in al-Dhakhira, is that reciting al-Fatihah twice in one rak'ah from the first two rak'ahs makes sajda sahw wajib. Note this baseline.
This is the default position before the detail.
2
Identify the detail from Qadikhan
Qadikhan introduces a distinction: if the two Fatihahs are recited consecutively (ala al-wala'), sajda is wajib; if a surah is recited between them, sajda is not wajib.
This is a later refinement, not found in earlier texts.
3
Understand the talil (legal reasoning)
The reasoning: when reciting twice consecutively, the wajib (the surah after Fatihah) is delayed, triggering sajda. When separated by a surah, no delay occurs because the surah is already recited, and ruku' is not immediately wajib after the surah.
The delay of a wajib is the cause for sajda sahw.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The chosen view adopted by later authorities (al-Muhit, al-Zahiriyya, al-Khulasa, al-Zahidi) is the detail: sajda only if consecutive. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
This is an example of tarjih within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة - باب صفة الصلاة تقديم الفاتحة لأن المضموم إليه شيء يقتضي تأخره . ـره عنه. ثانيهما الاقتصار في الأوليين على قراءة الفاتحة مرة واحدة في كل ركعة حتى إذا قرأها في ركعة منهما مرتين وجب عليه سجود السهو. كذا في الذخيرة وغيرها لكن في فتاوى قاضيخان تفصيل وهو أنه إذا قرأها مرتين على الولاء وجب السجود، وإن فصل بينهما بالسور لا يجب واختاره في المحيط والظهيرية والخلاصة وصححه الزاهدي لما أشار إليه في الذخيرة من لزوم تأخير الواجب وهو السورة على التقدير الأول دون الثاني، فإن الركوع ليس واجباً بأثر السورة فإنه لو جمع بين سور بعد الفاتحة لم يجب عليه شيء.
Book of Prayer - Chapter on the Description of Prayer. The introduction of al-Fatihah because the included thing implies its delay. Second, confining in the first two rak'ahs to reciting al-Fatihah once in each rak'ah, such that if he recites it twice in one of the two, sajda sahw becomes wajib upon him. Thus in al-Dhakhira and others. But in Fatawa Qadikhan there is a detail: that if he recites it twice consecutively, sajda is wajib; if he separates between them with surahs, it is not wajib. And it was chosen in al-Muhit, al-Zahiriyya, and al-Khulasa, and authenticated by al-Zahidi due to what was indicated in al-Dhakhira about the necessary delay of the wajib which is the surah in the first estimation but not the second, because ruku' is not wajib immediately after the surah; if he combines surahs after al-Fatihah, nothing is wajib upon him.
Source pages p. 517

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the repetition of Surah al-Fatihah in a single rak'ah. The general rule is that one should recite Fatihah only once per rak'ah in the first two rak'ahs. If one recites it twice, sajda sahw becomes wajib. However, a detail from Qadikhan is preferred: if the two recitations are consecutive (without an intervening surah), sajda is wajib because this delays the wajib recitation of a surah after Fatihah. If a surah is recited between the two Fatihahs, no delay occurs, so no sajda. This is because ruku' is not immediately obligatory after the surah; one could recite multiple surahs after Fatihah without incurring sajda. The chosen view in al-Muhit, al-Zahiriyya, al-Khulasa, and by al-Zahidi follows this detail.

Key Terms
الفاتحة (al-Fatihah): The opening chapter of the Quran, recited in each rak'ah.
سجود السهو (sajda al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness required for errors in prayer.
على الولاء (ala al-wala'): Consecutively, without interruption.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if a worshipper recites Surah al-Fatihah twice in one rak'ah with a surah in between, what is the ruling?
A) Sajda sahw is wajib
B) Sajda sahw is not wajib
C) The prayer becomes invalid
D) Nothing is required

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, reciting al-Fatihah twice in one rak'ah only requires sajda sahw if the two recitations are consecutive; separating with a surah avoids the obligation.

Salah — Prayer

The Ruling on Order Between Rak'ahs: Wajib, Not Fard
Determining the legal nature of sequence in prayer and its application to masbūq and lāḥiq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that tarīb between rak'ahs is wajib and explain the evidence from the masbūq's prayer.

Core Idea
Order between rak'ahs is wajib, not fard, proven by the masbūq who prays in reverse order.

In the Hanafi school, the sequence of rak'ahs in prayer (tarīb) is classified as wajib, not fard. This means that while it is obligatory, its omission does not invalidate the prayer but requires compensation (sajdah sahw) or is excused under necessity. The primary evidence comes from the practice of the masbūq (one who joins late), who completes his prayer in reverse order. This lesson examines the reasoning and the hadith that supports this position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act under discussion
The act is the sequence of rak'ahs in prayer. Is this order a fard (pillar) or wajib (obligatory)?
2
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that tarīb between rak'ahs is wajib, not fard. The author of al-Hidayah and others affirm this.
Zufar disagrees, holding it is fard.
3
Examine the primary dalil
The hadith 'What you have caught, pray; what you have missed, complete' (Bukhari) is cited. The masbūq follows the imam and then completes missed units in reverse order (e.g., if he missed two rak'ahs, he prays them as his first two).
If tarīb were fard, this reverse order would be impossible.
4
Understand the rationale: singular vs repeated
Within a rak'ah, order of standing, bowing, and prostration is fard because each act is singular and cannot be replaced. Between rak'ahs, the acts are repeated, so order can be relaxed.
This distinction is made in al-Kafi and other texts.
5
Apply to the masbūq
The masbūq's prayer is valid because the necessity of following the imam overrides the wajib of order. If it were fard, his prayer would be invalid.

الترتيب واجب عليه، وعنده فرض وذلك كما إذا أدرك بعض صلاة الإمام فنام ثم انتبه فعليه أن يصلي أولاً ما نام فيه ثم يتابع الإمام، فلو تابعه أولاً ثم صلى ما نام فيه بعد سلام الإمام جاز عندنا وأثم لتركه الواجب، وعند زفر لا يجوز. قال في السراج عن الفتاوى : المبسوق إذ بدأ بقضاء ما فاته فإنه تفسد صلاته وهو الأصح، واللاحق إذا تابع الإمام قبل قضاء ما فاته لا تفسد خلافاً لزفر .اهـ. قوله: (فلذا اقتصر المصنف) أي في كتابه الكافي. قوله : (وإنما كان واجباً) أي رعاية الترتيب. قوله : (يراعى وجوده صورة ومعنى في محله) قال الزيلعي : بعد هذا تحرزاً عن تفويت ما تعلق به جزءاً أو كلاً إذ لا يمكن استيفاء ما تعلق به جزءاً أو كلاً من جنسه لضرورة اتحاده في الشرعية .اهـ. وقوله ( جزءاً أو كلا» حالان من قوله ما تعلق وما تعلق بالمتحد كل الصلاة القعدة الأخيرة أو جزؤها وهو الركعة القيام والركوع . والحاصل أن المتحد لم يشرع شيء آخر من جنسه في محله، فإذا فات فات أصلاً فيفوت ما تعلق به من جزء الصلاة أو كلها بخلاف المتكرر فإنه لو فات أحد فعليه بقي الفعل الآخر من جنسه فلم يفت أصلاً فلم يفت ما تعلق به كما لو أتى بإحدى السجدتين في ركعة وترك الأخرى. وإنما قال يراعي وجوده صورة ومعنى لأن أحد فعلي المتكرر لو فات محله عن ، ثم أتى به في محل آخر التحق بمحل الأول فكان موجوداً فيه معنى وإن لم يوجد صورة بخلاف المتحد فإنه لم يلتحق بمحله الأول حيث فات بفواته فلم يوجد صورة ومعنى كذا في حواشي مسكين للسيد محمد أبي السعود عن العلامة
He (the author) said: (And observance of order in a repeated action) He made it absolute here and restricted it in al-Kafi to that which is repeated in every rak'ah like the prostration, so that if he leaves the second prostration and stands for the second rak'ah, his prayer is not invalidated. The commentator added: 'or it is repeated in the entire prayer like the number of rak'ahs, because what the masbūq prays after the imam finishes is the first part of his prayer according to us, and if order were fard, it would be the last part.' This is refuted because what the masbūq prays is the first part of his prayer in ruling, not in reality. Also, it is not absolutely the first part; rather it is first in terms of recitation and last in terms of tashahhud as will come. And it is not correct to include it under the wajib order because that which is less does not necessitate sajda sahw, and that is apparent in what he said. He said: (And he restricted it in al-Kafi to that which is repeated in every rak'ah like the prostration) I say: similarly in al-Nihaya, al-Inaya, al-Kifaya, and Ghayat al-Bayan. He said: (And it is not correct to include it under the wajib order...) He said in al-Nahr: This is a misconception, for the order between rak'ahs is only wajib. He said in al-Fath: Except that it is dropped for the masbūq due to the necessity of following the imam. And what is in the commentary is taken from al-Khabbazi and al-Nihaya, and upon that is al-Diraya and al-Fath. ... The outcome of the speech in al-Nahr is that what was understood in al-Bahr from the commentator al-Zayla'i that order in rak'ahs is wajib upon the masbūq is incorrect. Rather, the obligation is upon others, and it is not fard, otherwise it would not be dropped for the masbūq, as evidence by his statement: 'what the masbūq prays is the first part of his prayer; if order were wajib upon him, we would rule that what he caught with the imam is the first part of his prayer and what he prays is the last part, since it is not within his ability to place what he caught first as last, or we would rule that he should pray two rak'ahs first and then follow the imam, which is not permissible. Rather, he must follow him and make up what he missed from the first part of his prayer. This is proof of its not being fard. ... And by this explanation, it became clear to you the incorrectness of what some objected to al-Nahr by saying 'Rather, he is the one mistaken' because what he cited from al-Fath is explicit refutation. ... There remains an objection: the worshipper is either alone, imam, or follower; the obligation of order between rak'ahs is not conceivable for the first two because each rak'ah they perform first is the first, second is the second, etc. As for the follower, he is either one who caught up (mudrik) or one who missed (masbūq). ... In al-Kafi: As for the order of standing over bowing and order of bowing over prostration, it is fard because prayer does not exist without that. And similarly, the commentator and commentators of al-Hidaya mentioned, and they explained that what has a singular legal ruling is considered for its existence in form and meaning in its place because it was prescribed thus. If he changes it, he has inverted the act and its opposite, and inverting what is legislated is invalid, unlike what has multiple rulings. ... The author said in his Kafi in the chapter of ... or lāḥiq, so the mudrik's rule is like his imam, and the masbūq you know that the discussion is not about him because he is commanded to reverse the order, and the lāḥiq is not conceivable for him the obligation of order either due to what preceded. So what is the benefit of this wajib? It is said: The lack of conceivability of reversing the order does not necessitate not mentioning it. Do you not see that they said the order of the last sitting over what precedes it is fard, and it is known that being last is not conceivable to reverse the order. Indeed, the benefit appears in negating its being fard, which is that the masbūq prays the first part of his prayer; if it were fard, it would not be so. ... The truth is that the objection is baseless because what al-Zayla'i and others intended was to indicate the issue of disagreement between us and Zufar regarding the lāḥiq. According to us, order is wajib upon him; according to Zufar, it is fard. That is, if he caught part of the imam's prayer and then slept and then woke up, he must first pray what he slept through and then follow the imam. If he follows first and then prays what he missed after the imam's salam, it is permissible according to us but he sins for leaving the wajib, while according to Zufar it is not permissible. ... The author said: (Therefore the author confined himself) i.e., in his book al-Kafi. He said: (And it was only wajib) i.e., observance of order. He said: (Its existence in form and meaning is observed in its place) al-Zayla'i said: after this, to avoid wasting what is attached to it partially or wholly, because it is impossible to fulfill what is attached partially or wholly from its kind due to the necessity of its singularity in legislation. The meaning of 'partially or wholly' are two states of 'what is attached'. What is attached to the singular is the entire prayer like the last sitting or part of it like the rak'ah, standing, bowing. The conclusion is that for the singular, no other action of its kind is legislated in its place, so if it is missed, it is missed entirely, so what is attached to it of part or all of prayer is lost, unlike the repeated action; if one of them is missed, the other action of its kind remains, so it was not missed entirely, so what is attached to it is not lost, as if he performs one of the two prostrations in a rak'ah and leaves the other. And he only said 'its existence in form and meaning' because if one of the two actions of the repeated is missed from its place and then performed in another place, it joins the first place, so it exists in it meaningfully even if not in form, unlike the singular, which does not join its first place because it is missed with its passing, so it does not exist in form and meaning. Thus in the marginal notes of Miskin by Sayyid Muhammad Abu al-Sa'ud from the commentator.
Source pages p. 517

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether order (tarīb) in prayer is fard or wajib, focusing on the sequence of rak'ahs. The base text initially restricts tarīb to actions repeated within a rak'ah (like prostration). The commentator al-Zayla'i extends it to actions repeated in the whole prayer (like rak'ahs), but this is refuted. The genuine Hanafi position is that tarīb between rak'ahs is wajib, not fard, because the masbūq (one who misses part of the prayer) is commanded to follow the imam and then make up missed units in reverse order (i.e., what he catches first is his first rak'ah in ruling). This would be impossible if tarīb were fard. The proof is the hadith 'What you have caught, pray; what you have missed, complete' which implies flexibility. The discussion clarifies that tarīb of standing, bowing, and prostration within a rak'ah is fard because the act cannot exist without that order (singular in legislation). For repeated acts like rak'ahs, tarīb is wajib and can be dropped due to necessity (following the imam). The dispute with Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) is highlighted: Zufar holds tarīb is fard, so a lāḥiq (one who joins late and then misses) must complete missed units before following the imam, otherwise his prayer is invalid. According to the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), it is permissible but makruh tahrimi (sinful) to delay the missed units. The relied-upon position is that tarīb is wajib.

Key Terms
الترتيب (al-tarīb): The sequence or order of actions in prayer.
المسبوق (al-masbūq): One who misses part of the prayer with the imam and completes it afterwards.
اللاحق (al-lāḥiq): One who joins the imam late and then misses further parts (e.g., due to sleep).
المدرك (al-mudrik): One who catches the entire prayer with the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the order (tarīb) between rak'ahs in prayer?
A) Fard (obligatory, invalidates prayer if missed)
B) Wajib (obligatory, but compensable with sajda sahw)
C) Sunnah (recommended)
D) Mubah (permissible)

Key Takeaway
Tarīb between rak'ahs is wajib in the Hanafi school; it is not fard, as demonstrated by the masbūq's permissible reverse order.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Lāḥiq and the Dispute with Zufar on Order
Determining the legal nature of sequence in prayer and its application to masbūq and lāḥiq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the lāḥiq's order of prayer and contrast it with Zufar's view.

Core Idea
The lāḥiq may follow the imam first, then make up missed units; Zufar requires the reverse.

This lesson explores the practical implications of the tarīb dispute for the lāḥiq—a person who joins the imam late and then misses further parts of the prayer (e.g., due to sleep). The Hanafi school holds that he may follow the imam and then complete what he missed, while Zufar insists he must make up the missed parts first. The difference hinges on whether tarīb is wajib or fard.

Guided Path
1
Define the lāḥiq
The lāḥiq is one who catches part of the prayer with the imam and then misses further parts due to sleep, forgetfulness, or other reasons.
He differs from the masbūq who misses only the beginning.
2
State Hanafi position
According to Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, the lāḥiq may follow the imam for what he catches and then after the imam's salam, make up what he missed. Doing so is permissible but sinful (makruh tahrimi) because he left a wajib.
Zufar holds that he must make up the missed parts first; otherwise the prayer is invalid.
3
Examine the reasoning
For Hanafis, tarīb is wajib, so it can be excused under necessity. Zufar sees it as fard, so the order cannot be changed.
4
Identify the practical consequence
If a lāḥiq follows the imam first and then makes up, the Hanafi school validates his prayer but considers it sinful. Zufar invalidates it.
Thus, the Hanafi ruling is more lenient.
5
Review the source evidence
The text cites al-Siraj: 'The masbūq, if he begins to make up what he missed, his prayer is invalid (because he is reversing order incorrectly?). Actually, it says: 'the masbūq if he begins with qada, his prayer becomes invalid' but then 'the lāḥiq if he follows the imam before qada, it does not become invalid, unlike Zufar.'
This shows the delicate distinction.

صريح في الرد عليه .هـ. بقي هنا إشكال وهو المصلي إما منفرداً وإمام أو مأموم، ولا يتصور وجوب الترتيب بين الركعات في حق الأولين لأن كل ركعة يأتيان بها أولاً فهي الأولى وثانياً فهي الثانية وهلم جراً. وأما وهكذا ذكر الشارح وشراح الهداية وعللوا له بأن ما اتحدت شرعيته يراعي وجوده صورة ومعنى في محله لأنه كذلك شرع، فإذا غيره فقد قلب الفعل وعكسه وقلب المشروع باطل ولا كذلك ما تعددت شرعيته. وقال المصنف في He (the author) said: (And observance of order in a repeated action) He made it absolute here and restricted it in al-Kafi to that which is repeated in every rak'ah like the prostration, so that if he leaves the second prostration and stands for the second rak'ah, his prayer is not invalidated. If he changes it, he has inverted the act and its opposite, and inverting what is legislated is invalid, unlike what has multiple rulings. ... The author said in his Kafi in the chapter of ... or lāḥiq, so the mudrik's rule is like his imam, and the masbūq you know that the discussion is not about him because he is commanded to reverse the order, and the lāḥiq is not conceivable for him the obligation of order either due to what preceded. So what is the benefit of this wajib? It is said: The lack of conceivability of reversing the order does not necessitate not mentioning it. Do you not see that they said the order of the last sitting over what precedes it is fard, and it is known that being last is not conceivable to reverse the order. Indeed, the benefit appears in negating its being fard, which is that the masbūq prays the first part of his prayer; if it were fard, it would not be so. ... The truth is that the objection is baseless because what al-Zayla'i and others intended was to indicate the issue of disagreement between us and Zufar regarding the lāḥiq. According to us, order is wajib upon him; according to Zufar, it is fard. That is, if he caught part of the imam's prayer and then slept and then woke up, he must first pray what he slept through and then follow the imam. If he follows first and then prays what he missed after the imam's salam, it is permissible according to us but he sins for leaving the wajib, while according to Zufar it is not permissible. ... The author said: (Therefore the author confined himself) i.e., in his book al-Kafi. He said: (And it was only wajib) i.e., observance of order. He said: (Its existence in form and meaning is observed in its place) al-Zayla'i said: after this, to avoid wasting what is attached to it partially or wholly, because it is impossible to fulfill what is attached partially or wholly from its kind due to the necessity of its singularity in legislation. The meaning of 'partially or wholly' are two states of 'what is attached'. What is attached to the singular is the entire prayer like the last sitting or part of it like the rak'ah, standing, bowing. The conclusion is that for the singular, no other action of its kind is legislated in its place, so if it is missed, it is missed entirely, so what is attached to it of part or all of prayer is lost, unlike the repeated action; if one of them is missed, the other action of its kind remains, so it was not missed entirely, so what is attached to it is not lost, as if he performs one of the two prostrations in a rak'ah and leaves the other. And he only said 'its existence in form and meaning' because if one of the two actions of the repeated is missed from its place and then performed in another place, it joins the first place, so it exists in it meaningfully even if not in form, unlike the singular, which does not join its first place because it is missed with its passing, so it does not exist in form and meaning. Thus in the marginal notes of Miskin by Sayyid Muhammad Abu al-Sa'ud from the commentator.
Source pages p. 517

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether order (tarīb) in prayer is fard or wajib, focusing on the sequence of rak'ahs. The base text initially restricts tarīb to actions repeated within a rak'ah (like prostration). The commentator al-Zayla'i extends it to actions repeated in the whole prayer (like rak'ahs), but this is refuted. The genuine Hanafi position is that tarīb between rak'ahs is wajib, not fard, because the masbūq (one who misses part of the prayer) is commanded to follow the imam and then make up missed units in reverse order (i.e., what he catches first is his first rak'ah in ruling). This would be impossible if tarīb were fard. The proof is the hadith 'What you have caught, pray; what you have missed, complete' which implies flexibility. The discussion clarifies that tarīb of standing, bowing, and prostration within a rak'ah is fard because the act cannot exist without that order (singular in legislation). For repeated acts like rak'ahs, tarīb is wajib and can be dropped due to necessity (following the imam). The dispute with Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) is highlighted: Zufar holds tarīb is fard, so a lāḥiq (one who joins late and then misses) must complete missed units before following the imam, otherwise his prayer is invalid. According to the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), it is permissible but makruh tahrimi (sinful) to delay the missed units. The relied-upon position is that tarīb is wajib.

Key Terms
الترتيب (al-tarīb): The sequence or order of actions in prayer.
المسبوق (al-masbūq): One who misses part of the prayer with the imam and completes it afterwards.
اللاحق (al-lāḥiq): One who joins the imam late and then misses further parts (e.g., due to sleep).
المدرك (al-mudrik): One who catches the entire prayer with the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the prayer of a lāḥiq who follows the imam first and then makes up missed units according to the Hanafi school?
A) Invalid, because order is fard.
B) Valid and not sinful, because order is sunnah.
C) Valid but sinful, because order is wajib.
D) Valid and required, because order is fard.

Key Takeaway
The lāḥiq may follow the imam before making up missed units; the prayer is valid but sinful, reflecting the wajib nature of tarīb.

Why Tartib (Order) in Prayer is Wajib, Not Fard
Explaining why tartib in prayer is wajib not fard, addressing masbuq and lahiq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rules tartib (order) in prayer as wajib rather than fard, and apply the distinction between unitary and repeated acts to resolve practical cases involving a masbuq or lahiq.

Core Idea
Order in prayer is wajib, not fard—the masbuq’s reversal proves it.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq tackles a subtle but fundamental distinction in Hanafi salah: the difference between fard and wajib in the context of maintaining order (tartib) between prayer actions. The author uses the case of the masbuq (latecomer) and the lahiq (one who lags behind) to demonstrate that order is wajib, not fard, based on the Prophet's hadith. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying rulings on prayer correction and compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its hukm level
What is the specific act under discussion? It is maintaining order (tartib) between the actions of salah. According to the Hanafi school, this is ruled as wajib, not fard.
The hukm level 'wajib' means it is obligatory but proven by zanni evidence, unlike fard which is qati.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The author cites the hadith: 'Whatever you catch, pray; whatever you miss, make up.' This hadith is the key evidence.
This hadith is ahad, thus zanni al-thubut, which supports the wajib classification.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the dalil proves the ruling)
The command to 'make up' the missed parts by reversing the order (the masbuq makes up missed rak'ahs after the imam, not in sequence) shows that order is not absolute. If order were fard, such reversal would invalidate the prayer. Since the prayer remains valid, order is wajib.
The masbuq is instructed to reverse the order, which would be impermissible if tartib were fard.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (dispute) with Zufar
Within the Hanafi school, Zufar argues that tartib is fard. The passage contrasts the position: a lahiq who follows the imam before making up missed parts—Abu Hanifa says the prayer is valid but sinful; Zufar says it is invalid.
This dispute has practical consequences for the validity of salah.
5
Understand the unitary vs repeated distinction
The passage explains that unitary acts (like the final sitting) must be performed in order (form and meaning) in their specific place; omission invalidates. Repeated acts (like ruku' in different rak'ahs) allow flexibility; missing order does not invalidate but requires compensation.
This distinction explains why order is fard for some elements and wajib for others.

Then he said: There is nothing upon the person who is caught up (masbuq) and no deficiency in his prayer at all. Therefore the author confined himself to what is repeated in every rak'ah. And it was wajib because the Prophet consistently maintained the order in it, and the proof for its not being fard is established from him (peace be upon him) in his statement: 'Whatever you catch, pray, and whatever you miss, make up.' The author said in al-Kafi: As for the order of standing before bowing and the order of bowing before prostration, that is fard because prayer is only found with that. And likewise the commentator and the commentators of al-Hidayah mentioned and they explained it because what is unitary in its legislation is considered to exist in form and meaning in its place because it is legislated thus. So if one changes it, he has inverted the act and reversed it, and inversion of the legislated is invalid. Not so what has multiple legislations. And the author said in his Kafi in the section on 'or one who lags behind (lahiq)': The one who catches up has the same ruling as his imam. As for the masbuq, you already know that the discussion is not about him because he is commanded to reverse the order, and for the lahiq, the obligation of order is also not conceivable due to what preceded. And some say: This speech we left due to its lack of benefit. The truth is that the objection is baseless from its root. That is because al-Zayla'i and others intend to refer to the disputed issue between us and Zufar regarding the lahiq. According to us, the order is wajib upon him, and according to him it is fard. For example, if he catches part of the imam's prayer and sleeps, then wakes up, he must first pray what he slept in, then follow the imam. If he first follows and then prays what he slept in after the imam's salam, it is permissible according to us but he sins for leaving the wajib. And according to Zufar, it is not permissible. The lahiq, if he follows the imam before making up what he missed, his prayer does not become invalid, contrary to Zufar. End of quote. His statement: 'Therefore the author confined himself' means in his book al-Kafi. His statement: 'And it was wajib' means maintaining order. His statement: 'It is considered to exist in form and meaning in its place.' al-Zayla'i said: After this, it is a precaution against losing what is attached to it, part or whole, because it is not possible to fulfill what is attached to it, part or whole, from its genus due to the necessity of its unity in legislation. End. And his statement: 'part or whole' are two حال of his statement 'what is attached.' What is attached to the unitary (mutahid) is the entire prayer, the final sitting, or its part, which is the rak'ah, standing, and bowing. The conclusion is that for the unitary, nothing else of its genus is legislated in its place. So if it is missed, it is missed entirely, and thus what is attached to it of part or whole of the prayer is lost. Unlike the repeated (mutakarrir), for if one of its acts is missed, another act of its genus remains, so it is not missed entirely, and thus what is attached to it is not lost, just as if one performs one of the two prostrations in a rak'ah and leaves the other. And he said 'in form and meaning' because if one of the acts of the repeated is missed from its place, and then it is performed in another place, it attaches to the first place, so it exists in it in meaning even if not in form. Unlike the unitary, it does not attach to its first place when it is missed by its loss, so it does not exist in form or meaning. Thus in the marginal notes of Miskin by Sayyid Muhammad Abu al-Sa'ud from al-Allamah.
Source pages p. 518

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof discussion on the nature of tartib (order) in salah. The author explains that maintaining order between the actions of prayer is wajib, not fard, based on the hadith 'What you catch, pray; what you miss, make up.' The masbuq (latecomer) is instructed to reverse the order when making up missed rak'ahs, which would be invalid if order were fard. The text distinguishes between unitary acts (like the final sitting) which are fard in order because they occur only once, and repeated acts (like ruku' and sujud within different rak'ahs) which are wajib. Al-Zayla'i's explanation uses the concept that unitary acts must be performed in form and meaning at their specific place; otherwise the act is inverted and invalid. The dispute with Zufar is highlighted: for the lahiq (one who lags behind), Abu Hanifa holds order is wajib, while Zufar says it is fard. The practical consequence is that if a lahiq follows the imam before making up missed parts, his prayer is valid but sinful according to Abu Hanifa, while Zufar would deem it invalid. The term 'masbuq' refers to someone who arrives late and catches part of the prayer; the term 'lahiq' refers to someone who begins with the imam but then misses some parts due to sleep or other excuse. The commentary clarifies the underlying rationale and the importance of distinguishing fard from wajib in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
المسبوق (al-masbuq): A latecomer who joins the prayer after the imam has begun; he catches some rak'ahs and must make up the missed ones.
اللاحق (al-lahiq): One who begins prayer with the imam but then misses some parts due to sleep or distraction; he must make up missed parts after the imam's salam.
الترتيب (al-tartib): Order of actions in prayer, such as standing before bowing, bowing before prostrating, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is fard in all cases
B) It is wajib for repeated acts and fard for unitary acts
C) It is sunnah
D) It is wajib only for the masbuq

Key Takeaway
Maintaining order in prayer is wajib for repeated acts but fard for unitary acts, and this distinction is proven by the hadith of the masbuq.

Sujud al-Sahw for Presenting a Rukn: The Wajib Nature of Order
Ruling-with-proof on sujud al-sahw due to taqdim rukn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that presenting a rukn requires sujud al-sahw and distinguish between the Hanafi and Zufar positions on order (tartib).

Core Idea
Presenting a rukn before its place is a wajib neglect, not a fard break; sujud al-sahw restores the prayer's perfection.

In this passage, the author discusses one of the causes of sujud al-sahw: presenting a rukn (a pillar) before its proper place, such as bowing before recitation. The ruling hinges on the nature of order (tartib) in prayer: is it fard or wajib? The Hanafi school, countering an intra-madhhab objection from Zufar, maintains that order is wajib, and thus presenting a rukn triggers sujud al-sahw rather than invalidating the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause
Recognise that presenting a rukn (taqdim rukn) is one of the things that make sujud al-sahw obligatory according to the Hanafi school. The example given is bowing before reciting or prostrating before bowing.
2
Understand the legal nature of order
The text states that maintaining order (tartib) is wajib according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to Zufar who holds it is fard. This distinction is crucial because the ruling on sujud al-sahw depends on whether the neglected element is wajib or fard.
Zufar is an early Hanafi scholar, but his view is not the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).
3
Analyse the proof
The evidence for wajib is that sujud al-sahw is only obligatory for leaving a wajib. Since presenting a rukn necessitates sujud al-sahw, order must be wajib. The text further argues that this holds even for non-repeated pillars like bowing and recitation, proving that order is wajib absolutely.
This is a classic Hanafi talil (reasoning) linking the ruling back to the foundational principle that sujud al-sahw compensates for leaving a wajib.
4
Resolve the apparent contradiction
Some argued that if order is wajib, presenting a rukn should invalidate the prayer. The text resolves this by distinguishing between unitary acts (where order is fard) and repeated acts (where order is wajib). Unitary acts like takbir tahrimah and the final sitting cannot be corrected, so violating order there invalidates. Repeated acts like bowing and prostration can be corrected by repeating them in the proper sequence, so order is wajib and the prayer remains valid once corrected.
This distinction is key to understanding why presenting a rukn does not break the prayer according to the majority Hanafi view.
5
Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The difference between Abu Hanifa and Zufar has a clear practical outcome: according to Abu Hanifa, if one presents a rukn and then corrects it, the prayer is valid and sujud al-sahw is required. According to Zufar, the prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated.
This ruling is the mufta bihi position for the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سجود السهو : إن سجود السهو يجب بأشياء منها : تقديم ركن بأن ركع قبل أن يقرأ أو سجد قبل أن يركع ثم قال : أما التقديم والتأخير فلأن مراعاة الترتيب واجبة عندنا خلافاً لزفر، فإذا ترك الترتيب فقد ترك الواجب وهو ظاهر في التناقض على ما قيل، وقد وقع نظيره في الذخيرة حتى استدل به صدر الشريعة في شرح الوقاية على أن الترتيب بين القراءة والركوع واجب بدليل وجوب سجود السهو بتركه حتى قال : وليس فيما تكرره قيداً . يوجب نفي الحكم عما عداه فإن مراعاة الترتيب في الأركان التي لا تكرر في كل ركعة واحدة أيضاً واجب لأنهم قالوا : يجب سجود السهو بتقديم ركن وأوردوا لنظيره الركوع قبل القراءة، وسجدة السهو لا تجب إلا لترك الواجب، فعلم أن الترتيب بين الركوع والقراءة واجب مع أنهما غير مكررين في ركعة واحدة فعلم أن مراعاة الترتيب واجبة مطلقاً، ويخطر ببالي أن المراد بما تكرر ما تكرر في الصلاة احترازاً عما لا يتكرر فيها على سبيل الفرضية وهو تكبيرة الافتتاح والقعدة الأخيرة، فإن مراعاة الترتيب في ذلك فرض ا هـ . وليس كما ظن وليس السيرامي. قوله : (حتى قال وليس فيما تكرر قيداً (الخ أي لفظ ما تكرر في قول الوقاية ورعاية الترتيب فيما تكرر ليس قيداً فإن ما لا يتكرر مراعاة الترتيب فيه واجبة أيضاً. قوله: (على سبيل الفرضية احترازاً عن تكبيرات الانتقالات وعن العقود الأول في غير الثنائية. قوله: (وليس بين الكلامين تناقض لأن قولهم (الخ أقول : محصل هذا الكلام أن الترتيب فرض باعتبار فساد الركن الذي هو فيه قبل الإعادة وواجب باعتبار عدم فساد الصلاة بترك الترتيب صورة بعد الإعادة فلا بين الاعتبارين، ، وهذا كلام عجيب وتصرف غريب فإن معنى الترتيب وجود كل ركن في محله، فحيث أعيد السجود وجد كل من الركوع والسجود في محله فلا يكون هناك ترك ترتيب أصلاً صورة ولا معنى إذ لو كان هناك ترك الترتيب صورة لفسدت الصلاة لما تقدم من أن ما اتحدت شرعيته يراعي وجوده في محله صورة ومعنى لأنه كذلك شرع، فإذا غيره فقد قلب الفعل وعكسه وقلب المشروع باطل وما تعددت شرعيته يراعي وجوده في محله معنى فقط. والكلام فيما اتحدت شرعيته فيراعي وجوده في مجله صورة ومعنى وعدم فساد الصلاة في الصورة المذكورة ليس لكون الترتيب فيها واجباً بل لأن سبب الفساد كان تقديم السجود على الركوع، فإذا أعيد إلى محله زال السبب فانتفى المسبب فلم تنتف المعارضة. وقال بعض الفضلاء : إن المراد بالفرض هنا الفرض العملي الصادق على الواجب الاصطلاحي ليرتفع التناقض، وهذا ليس بشيء أيضاً لأن كلاً من الفرض العملي والواجب وإن أطلق على الآخر باعتبار ثبوتهما بالظني إلا أن بينهما فرقاً، فإن الفرض العملي يوجب الفساد، سهواً كان أو عمداً، بخلاف الواجب فإن تركه سهواً يوجب سجود السهو، وقال بعضهم: إنه محمول على اختلاف الروايتين وعليه جرى القهستاني قال بعض المحققين : لا بد لهذا الاختلاف من ثمرة ولم أجد في كلام أحد التصريح بها فإن قلت أن بعض الفضلاء استدل على كون الترتيب واجباً بعدم لزوم إعادة الركن الذي هو فيه فهل يصلح هذا أن يكون ثمرة منافاة
Prostration of forgetfulness: Indeed, prostration of forgetfulness becomes obligatory by things, among them: presenting a rukn by bowing before reciting or prostrating before bowing. Then he said: As for presenting and delaying, it is because maintaining order is wajib according to us, contrary to Zufar. So if one leaves the order, he has left the wajib. And this is apparent in contradiction, as has been said. And its like occurred in al-Dhakhira until Sadr al-Shari'a used it as evidence in Sharh al-Wiqaya that the order between recitation and bowing is wajib by the evidence of obligation of sujud al-sahw by leaving it, until he said: 'And it is not a restriction in what is repeated, which necessitates negating the ruling from what is other than it. For maintaining order in pillars that are not repeated in each single rak'ah is also wajib because they said: Sujud al-sahw becomes obligatory for presenting a rukn, and they gave as its equivalent bowing before recitation. And sujud al-sahw is not obligatory except for leaving a wajib. So it is known that the order between bowing and recitation is wajib even though they are not repeated in one rak'ah. So it is known that maintaining order is obligatory absolutely. And it occurs to my mind that what is meant by 'what is repeated' is what is repeated in the prayer, as a precaution against what is not repeated in it on the basis of fardiyyah, namely the takbir tahrimah and the final sitting. For maintaining order in that is fard. End. And it is not as he thought, and nor al-Sayrami. His statement: 'Until he said: it is not a restriction in what is repeated' meaning the phrase 'what is repeated' in the statement of al-Wiqaya 'and maintaining order in what is repeated' is not a restriction, because for what is not repeated, maintaining order is also wajib. His statement: 'on the basis of fardiyyah' as a precaution against the takbirs of transition and the first sitting in other than two-rak'ah prayers. His statement: 'And there is no contradiction between the two statements because their statement...' I say: The summary of this speech is that order is fard by consideration of invalidation of the rukn he is in before repetition, and wajib by consideration of non-invalidation of the prayer by leaving order in form after repetition. So there is no contradiction between the two considerations. And this is an amazing speech and a strange handling, for the meaning of order is the existence of each rukn in its place. So when prostration is repeated, both bowing and prostration exist in their places, so there is no leaving of order at all in form or meaning. For if there were leaving of order in form, the prayer would be invalid due to what preceded: that what is unitary in its legislation is considered to exist in its place in form and meaning because it is legislated thus. So if one changes it, he has inverted the act and reversed it, and inversion of the legislated is invalid. And what has multiple legislations is considered to exist in its place in meaning only. And the discussion is about what is unitary in its legislation, so it is considered to exist in its place in form and meaning. And the non-invalidation of the prayer in the mentioned case is not because order is wajib, but because the cause of invalidation was the presentation of prostration before bowing. So when it is returned to its place, the cause is removed, so the effect is removed, so the objection does not remain. And some virtuous people said: What is meant by fard here is practical fard (fard 'amali) which applies to the technical wajib, to remove the contradiction. And this is not valid either, because each of practical fard and wajib, even if one is used for the other considering their establishment through zanni, yet there is a difference between them: practical fard necessitates invalidation whether forgetfully or intentionally, unlike wajib, whose forgetful leaving necessitates sujud al-sahw. And some said: It is carried on two different narrations, and al-Qahistani followed this. Some verifiers said: This difference must have a practical consequence, and I have not found anyone explicitly stating it. If you say that some virtuous people used the non-necessity of repeating the rukn one is in as evidence that order is wajib, does this suffice as a consequence? Contradiction.
Source pages p. 519

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof discussion on sujud al-sahw due to presenting a rukn before its place, such as bowing before recitation. The Hanafi position is that maintaining order (tartib) is wajib, not fard, contrary to Zufar. The evidence for obligation of sujud al-sahw comes from leaving a wajib. The text discusses an apparent contradiction: if order is wajib, how can the prayer be valid after correcting the order? The answer is that when the rukn is repeated in its correct place, the order is restored, so the invalidation is removed. The distinction between unitary and repeated acts is crucial: unitary acts (like takbir tahrimah, final sitting) have order as fard; repeated acts have order as wajib. The commentary clarifies that the practical consequence of the dispute with Zufar is the validity of the prayer: according to Abu Hanifa, if a person presents a rukn and then corrects it, the prayer is valid and sujud al-sahw is required. According to Zufar, the prayer would be invalid. The term 'fard 'amali' is introduced but rejected because it confuses the distinct categories. The verifiers note that the dispute must have a practical outcome, which is indeed the validity of the prayer.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Two prostrations performed at the end of prayer to compensate for forgetful omission or commission that does not invalidate the prayer.
تقديم ركن (taqdim rukn): Performing a pillar of prayer (like bowing or prostration) before its proper time (e.g., bowing before recitation).
الفرض العملي (al-fard al-'amali): A term used by some to refer to something that is practically fard (invalidates if omitted) but technically wajib (based on zanni evidence).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling if a person unintentionally prostrates before bowing in prayer?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated
B) The prayer is valid but sujud al-sahw is required
C) No action needed; the prayer is valid
D) The person must repeat the entire prayer

Key Takeaway
Presenting a rukn (taqdim rukn) is a cause of sujud al-sahw in the Hanafi school because order (tartib) is wajib, not fard; the prayer remains valid and is perfected by sujud al-sahw.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
Is Order (Tartib) in Prayer Fard or Wajib? The Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Detailed commentary on the ruling of order and its effect on sujud al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that order (tartib) is wajib and not fard, and identify the practical consequence of the dispute with Zufar.

Core Idea
Order (tartib) is wajib in the Hanafi school; violating it forgetfully requires sujud al-sahw but does not invalidate the prayer.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into a key intra-Hanafi dispute: whether maintaining the order of prayer actions is fard (pillar) or wajib (obligatory). The majority, including Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, hold it is wajib, while Zufar considers it fard. The discussion revolves around the evidence from sujud al-sahw and the distinction between repeated and non-repeated actions. The author resolves the apparent contradiction by explaining the context of the terms and shows that both positions have identical practical outcomes regarding the repetition of the action.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
What exactly is the ikhtilaf about? Zufar holds that order is fard; the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) hold it is wajib. Understand the difference in legal consequence: fard invalidates the prayer if omitted forgetfully (unless repeated), while wajib requires sujud al-sahw but does not invalidate.
The dispute is within the Hanafi school itself.
2
Understand the Hanafi majority position
Why is order wajib? The evidence is zanni (speculative) because the proofs for order are not definitive. Also, the obligation of sujud al-sahw for leaving order indicates it is not fard, because leaving a fard would invalidate the prayer entirely.
Sujud al-sahw is only wajib for leaving a wajib, not a fard.
3
Examine Zufar's view
Zufar argues that order is fard based on the necessity of following the Prophet's example strictly. The prayer actions are interconnected, and changing the sequence corrupts the act.
Some later Hanabi narrations also treat order as fard in certain contexts.
4
Analyze the thamarah (practical consequence)
The author concludes that despite the dispute, both sides agree that if the forgotten action (e.g., prostration before bowing) is not repeated, the prayer is invalid. If it is repeated, the prayer is valid with sujud al-sahw. Thus, there is no practical difference in this scenario.
Some attempted to find a difference concerning whether the pillar 'in which one is' must be repeated, but both sides agree it is not required.
5
Evaluate the author's resolution
The text resolves the apparent contradiction by showing that 'fard' in some statements refers to 'practical fard' (equivalent to wajib) or that the context differs between before and after repetition. The key is that the prayer is not corrupted after the action is repeated.
The author criticizes those who see a contradiction, emphasizing that order is wajib absolutely, though in certain non-repeated actions (like takbirat al-ihram) it may be a condition (shart).
