الفرض العملي يوجب الفساد، سهواً كان أو عمداً، بخلاف الواجب فإن تركه سهواً يوجب سجود السهو، وقال بعضهم: إنه محمول على اختلاف الروايتين وعليه جرى القهستاني قال بعض المحققين : لا بد لهذا الاختلاف من ثمرة ولم أجد في كلام أحد التصريح بها فإن قلت أن بعض الفضلاء استدل على كون الترتيب واجباً بعدم لزوم إعادة الركن الذي هو فيه فهل يصلح هذا أن يكون ثمرة
للاختلاف؟ قلت: لا يصلح أن يكون دليلاً على الوجوب ولا ثمرة للاختلاف لأن القائلين بالفرضية، والقائلين بالوجوب متفقون على لزوم إعادة الركن الذي أتى به وفساد الصلاة إن لم يعده وعلى عدم لزوم إعادة الركن الذي هو فيه ولو قال القائلون بالوجوب بعدم لزوم إعادة الركن الذي أتى به لكان لهذا الاختلاف ثمرة .اهـ. وسيأتي من الشارح التنبيه على نفي ما في السؤال مما استدل به بعض الفضلاء حيث يقول : فعلم أن الاختلاف في الإعادة الخ. قوله : (معناه أن الركن الخ) أي الركن الذي قدمه على غيره كالسجود الذي قدمه على الركوع في المثال المذكور يفسد هو أي الركن المذكور ولا يقع معتداً به بسبب ترك الترتيب أي بسبب تقديمه على محله فيلزمه إعادته. قوله : (فالحاصل أن المشروع هذا أول عبارة الفتح الآتي الغزو إليها. قوله: (فالترتيب شرط بين الخ) اعلم أن الأنواع التي ذكرها أربع هي ما يتحد في كل الصلاة وما يتعدد في كلها، وما يتعدد في كل ركعة، وما يتحد في كل ركعة وكل واحد منها له أفراد ؛ فالأول أفراده التحريمة والقعدة، والثاني الركعات، والثالث السجدتان، والرابع القراءة في الثنائية أو غيرها إذا اقتصر على القراءة في الأخريين والقيام والركوع والصور العقلية في الترتيب بين نوع ونوع آخر ستة بأن تعتبر ترتيب كل نوع ما يليه، والصور بين ترتيب فرد من نوع وفرد آخر من ذلك النوع خمس بأن تعتبر الترتيب بين التحريمة والقعدة وبين أول الركعات ،وآخرها وبين السجدة والسجدة وبين القراءة والقيام والركوع، وكذا بين القيام والركوع وهذا الترتيب في هذه الصور منه شرط ومنه واجب. وحاصله أن الترتيب شرط في شيئين : أحدهما فيما بين النوع الأول وبين بقية الأنواع الثلاثة فيشترط الترتيب بين الأول أعني ما يتحد في كل الصلاة كالقعدة ومن ما يتعدد في كلها كالركعات، ومثل له في
Book of Prayer - Chapter on Description of Prayer. Sujud al-Sahw: Sujud al-Sahw becomes obligatory due to things including: advancing a pillar, such as bowing before reciting or prostrating before bowing. Then he said: As for advancing and delaying, because observing order is obligatory in our school, contrary to Zufar. So if one leaves order, he has left an obligatory act, and this is apparent contradiction as has been said. Its analogue occurred in al-Dhakhira, such that Sadr al-Shari'ah used it as evidence in Sharh al-Wiqayah that order between recitation and bowing is obligatory due to the obligation of sujud al-sahw for leaving it, until he said: And it is not a restriction on what is repeated. It necessitates negating the ruling for other than it, for observing order in pillars that are not repeated in each rak'ah is also obligatory because they said: Sujud al-Sahw is obligatory for advancing a pillar, and they gave its analogue bowing before recitation. And sujud al-sahw is not obligatory except for leaving an obligatory act. So it is known that order between bowing and recitation is obligatory despite them not being repeated in one rak'ah. Thus it is known that observing order is obligatory absolutely. It occurs to me that what is meant by 'what is repeated' is what is repeated in the prayer, as a precaution against what is not repeated in it as a fard, such as the takbir of opening and the final sitting, for observing order in that is fard. End. It is not as he thought, and not al-Sayrami. His saying: (until he said: and it is not a restriction on 'what is repeated' etc.) means the phrase 'what is repeated' in the saying of al-Wiqayah 'and observing order in what is repeated' is not a restriction, for observing order in what is not repeated is also obligatory. His saying: (as a fard precaution against the takbirs of transitions and the first sitting in non-two-rak'ah prayers). His saying: (and there is no contradiction between the two statements because their saying etc.) I say: The gist of this speech is that order is fard in terms of the corruption of the pillar in which one is before repetition, and obligatory in terms of the prayer not being corrupted by leaving order in form after repetition, so there is no contradiction between the two considerations. This is strange speech and a strange approach, for the meaning of order is the existence of every pillar in its place. So when the prostration is repeated, both bowing and prostration exist in their places, so there is no leaving of order at all, neither in form nor meaning. For if there was leaving of order in form, the prayer would be corrupted because of what preceded: that what is unified in its legal basis requires its existence in its place in form and meaning, because it is legislated as such. So if one changes it, he has inverted the act and reversed it, and the reversal of the legislated act is invalid. What is multiple in its legal basis requires its existence in its place in meaning only. The discussion is about what is unified in its legal basis, so its existence is considered in its place in form and meaning. And the non-corruption of the prayer in the mentioned form is not because order is obligatory there, but because the cause of corruption was the advancing of prostration before bowing. So when it is repeated in its place, the cause is removed, so the effect is removed, so the objection is not removed. Some virtuous scholars said: What is meant by fard here is practical fard, which applies to the technical wajib, to remove the contradiction. This is also nothing, because each of practical fard and wajib, although they are applied to the other due to their being established by zanni evidence, there is a difference between them. For practical fard necessitates corruption, whether forgetfully or intentionally, unlike wajib, for leaving it forgetfully necessitates sujud al-sahw. Some said: It is carried on the difference of the two narrations, and al-Qahistani proceeded upon it. Some investigators said: There must be some practical consequence for this difference, and I have not found in anyone's speech an explicit statement of it. For if you say that some virtuous scholars inferred that order is wajib from the non-necessity of repeating the pillar in which one is, is this suitable to be a practical consequence of the difference? I say: It is not suitable to be evidence for obligation, nor a practical consequence, because those who say it is fard and those who say it is wajib agree on the necessity of repeating the pillar that was performed and the corruption of the prayer if he does not repeat it, and on the non-necessity of repeating the pillar in which he is. If those who say wajib had said that repeating the pillar that was performed is not necessary, then this difference would have a practical consequence. End. The commentator will later point out the negation of what is in the question from what some virtuous scholars used as evidence, where he says: So it is known that the difference is in repeating etc. His saying: (meaning that the pillar etc.) meaning the pillar that he advanced over another, like prostration that he advanced before bowing in the mentioned example, becomes invalid, i.e., the mentioned pillar, and it does not count as valid due to leaving order, i.e., due to its advancement from its place, so he must repeat it. His saying: (So the gist is that the legislated) this is the beginning of the expression from al-Fath that is to be referred to later. His saying: (so order is a condition between etc.) Know that the types he mentioned are four: what is unified in the entire prayer, what is multiple in the entire prayer, what is multiple in each rak'ah, and what is unified in each rak'ah, and each has its instances. The first has instances: the opening takbir and the final sitting. The second: the rak'ahs. The third: the two prostrations. The fourth: recitation in the two-rak'ah or other prayer if he limits recitation to the last two rak'ahs, and standing, and bowing. The rational pictures of order between one type and another are six, by considering the order of each type with what follows it. The pictures of order between an instance of one type and another instance of that type are five, by considering order between the opening takbir and the final sitting, between the first and last of the rak'ahs, between one prostration and another, between recitation and standing and bowing, and likewise between standing and bowing. This order in these pictures is partially a condition and partially obligatory. Its gist is that order is a condition in two things: one of them is between the first type and the remaining three types. So order is a condition between the first, i.e., what is unified in the entire prayer like the final sitting, and what is multiple in the entire prayer like the rak'ahs, and he gave an example for it.
Source pages p. 519

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the topic of Sujud al-Sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) and specifically the ruling on order (tartib) between the actions of prayer. The author explains that in the Hanafi school, arranging actions in their proper sequence is wajib (obligatory, but not fard), contrary to Zufar who held it as fard. The discussion centers on the distinction between actions that are repeated in each rak'ah (like sujud) and those that are not (like the opening takbir). The author argues that even for non-repeated actions, order is still wajib, and leaving it intentionally or forgetfully requires sujud al-sahw, but does not invalidate the prayer if the missed action is repeated. A potential contradiction is addressed: if order is wajib, why do some texts call it fard? The author resolves this by explaining that 'fard' here means practical fard (which includes wajib in common parlance). He further clarifies that the disagreement among later Hanafi scholars (whether order is fard or wajib) has no practical effect in this case, because both groups agree that the forgotten action must be repeated and that the prayer is invalid if not repeated. The passage then categorizes the types of prayer actions and specifies where order is a condition (shart) versus wajib, concluding that between the first type (non-repeated actions like qa'dah) and others, order is a condition.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Two prostrations performed at the end of prayer to compensate for forgetfulness that occurs during the prayer.
ترتيب (tartib): The specific order of actions in prayer, such as reciting before bowing, bowing before prostrating, etc.
فرض (fard): A definitive obligation proven by qati' evidence; leaving it intentionally or forgetfully invalidates the prayer if not repeated.
واجب (wajib): An obligation proven by zanni evidence; leaving it forgetfully requires sujud al-sahw but does not invalidate the prayer if compensated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the status of order (tartib) between prayer actions?
A) Fard, because it is a pillar of prayer.
B) Wajib, because the evidence is zanni and sujud al-sahw is required for forgetful violation.
C) Sunnah, because it is recommended but not obligatory.
D) Makruh, because it is disliked to change order.

Key Takeaway
Order (tartib) is wajib in the Hanafi school; forgetful violation requires sujud al-sahw and repetition of the action, but the prayer remains valid.

The Four Types of Prayer Actions and the Ruling on Order (Tartib)
Ruling statement with expansion on tartib categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the four types of prescribed actions in prayer and determine when tartib is a condition (shart) versus an obligation (wajib) in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Order (tartib) is a condition between some actions, but only wajib between others—know which to save your prayer.

Understanding when violating the order of actions invalidates prayer versus when it only requires compensation is a key Hanafi distinction. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents the four categories of prayer actions and clarifies when tartib is a condition (shart) and when it is wajib. We will walk through each category and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four types of actions
List the four categories: (1) single in whole prayer, (2) single in each rak‘ah, (3) multiple in whole (rak‘ahs), (4) multiple in each rak‘ah (sajdah). Recognize examples: final sitting (type 1), standing/bowing (type 2), rak‘ahs (type 3), prostrations (type 4).
This classification is unique to the Hanafi school.
2
Determine the ruling on tartib between each combination
State which pairs of categories require tartib as shart and which as wajib. Tartib is shart between type 1 and types 2/3/4, and between type 2 and type 4 when they belong to the same rak‘ah. Otherwise, tartib is wajib.
Wajib omission requires sajda sahw but does not invalidate.
3
Work through the scenario of remembering a missed action
Analyze the case: if one remembers after final sitting, he performs the missed act, repeats sitting, and does sajda sahw. If he remembers a missed bowing while in a later bowing (same type), he performs it and continues; order between repeated actions is only wajib.
The text provides specific examples; memorize the rules.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on repetition
Contrast al-Hidayah (repetition mustahabb, not obligatory) with Qadikhan (repetition obligatory because current action is nullified). The difference hinges on whether returning to a previous action nullifies the current pillar.
The preferred view is from al-Hidayah for fatwa, though both are valid.
5
Apply to a new scenario
Given a scenario (e.g., forgetting a prostration and remembering in the next rak‘ah’s bowing), determine whether to repeat the bowing according to the mufta bihi view (no repetition).
Ensure the student distinguishes between shart and wajib cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالحاصل أن المشروع فرضاً في الصلاة أربعة أنواع : ما يتحد في كل الصلاة كالقعدة أو في كل ركعة كالقيام، والركوع وما يتعدد في كلها كالركعات أو في كل ركعة كالسجود، فالترتيب شرط بين المتحد في كل الصلاة ما وجميع سواه مما يتعدد في كلها كالركعات أو في كل ركعة وما يتحد في كل ركعة حتى لو تذكر بعد القعدة قبل السلام أو بعده قبل أن يأتي بمفسد ركعة أو سجدة صلبية أو للتلاوة فعلها وأعاد القعدة وسجد للسهو، ولو تذكر كرر ركوعاً قضاه وقضى ما بعده من السجود أو قياماً أو قراءة صلى ركعة تامة، وكذا يشترط الترتيب بين ما يتحد في كل ركعة كالقيام والركوع، ولذا قلنا آنفاً في ترك القيام والركوع إنه يصلي ركعة تامة وإذا عرف ما رف هذا فقوله في النهاية الترتيب ليس بشرط بين يتعدد في كل الصلاة يعني الركعات أو يتحد في كل ركعة وبين ما يتعدد في كل ركعة ليس على إطلاقه، بل بين السجود والمتحد في كل ركعة تفصيل إن كان سجود ذلك الركوع بأن يكون ركوعاً وسجوداً من ركعة واحدة فالترتيب شرط، وإن كان ركوعاً من ركعة وسجوداً من أخرى بأن تذكر في سجدة ركوع ركعة قبل ركوع هذه السجدة قضى الركوع وسجدتيه، وإن تذكر على القلب بأن تذكر في ركوع أنه لم يسجد في الركعة قبلها سجدها وهل يعيد الركوع والسجود المتذكر فيه؟ ففي الهداية إنه لا تجب الإعادة بل تستحب معللاً بأن الترتيب ليس بفرض بين ما يتكرر في الأفعال والذي في فتاوى قاضيخان وغيره، أنه يعيد معللاً بأنه ارتفض بالعود إلى ما قبله من الأركان لأنه قبل الرفع منه يقبل الرفض، ولهذا ذكر هو فيما لو تذكر سجدة بعد ما رفع من الركوع أنه يقضيها ولا يعيد الركوع لأنه بعد ما تم بالرفع لا يقبل الرفض، فعلم أن الاختلاف في الإعادة ليس بناء على اشتراط الترتيب وعدمه بل عن أن الركن المتذكر فيه هل يرتفض بالعود إلى ما قبله من الأركان أو لا.
The conclusion is that what is prescribed as fard in prayer are four types: what is single in the whole prayer like the sitting, or in each rak'ah like standing and bowing, and what is multiple in the whole like rak'ahs, or in each rak'ah like prostration. Thus, order is a condition between the single in the whole prayer and all others that are multiple in the whole like rak'ahs or in each rak'ah, and what is single in each rak'ah, such that if one remembers after the final sitting before or after salām before doing something that invalidates, a rak'ah or a prostration (either integral or for recitation), he performs it, repeats the sitting, and prostrates for forgetfulness. If he remembers a repeated bowing, he performs it and what follows it of prostration or standing or recitation, he prays a full rak'ah. Likewise, order is a condition between what is single in each rak'ah like standing and bowing. Hence we said earlier regarding omitting standing and bowing that he prays a full rak'ah. When you know this, then the statement in al-Nihāyah that order is not a condition between what is multiple in the whole prayer (meaning the rak'ahs) or what is single in each rak'ah and what is multiple in each rak'ah is not absolute. Rather, between prostration and what is single in each rak'ah there is detail: if the prostration is for that bowing, i.e., bowing and prostration from one rak'ah, then order is a condition. If it is bowing from one rak'ah and prostration from another (e.g., one remembers in the prostration the bowing of a rak'ah before the bowing of this prostration), he performs the bowing and its two prostrations. If one remembers the opposite, i.e., in bowing that he did not prostrate in the preceding rak'ah, he prostrates now. Should he repeat the bowing and the prostration in which he remembered? In al-Hidāyah, repetition is not obligatory but recommended, reasoned that order is not fard between repeating actions. In the Fatāwā of Qādīkhān and others, he must repeat, reasoned that it is nullified by returning to previous pillars because before raising from it, it can be nullified. For this reason, he mentioned that if one remembers a prostration after raising from bowing, he performs it without repeating bowing because after completion by raising, it cannot be nullified. Thus, the difference on repetition is not based on requiring order or not, but on whether the pillar in which one remembers is nullified by returning to previous pillars or not.
Source pages p. 520

Commentary
This passage is an expanded ruling on the order (tartib) of actions in prayer. The author first categorizes the prescribed (fard) actions into four types: (1) what is single in the whole prayer (e.g., the final sitting and the opening takbir), (2) what is single in each rak'ah (e.g., standing, bowing), (3) what is multiple in the whole prayer (the rak'ahs themselves), and (4) what is multiple in each rak'ah (the two prostrations). He then states that order is a condition (shart) between the first type (single in whole prayer) and all others; if you miss a rak'ah and remember after the final sitting, you must perform that rak'ah, repeat the sitting, and do prostration of forgetfulness. Similarly, order is a condition between single-in-each-rak'ah actions (e.g., standing before bowing) within the same rak'ah. However, order is not a condition but wajib between multiple actions like rak'ahs and prostrations when they are not from the same rak'ah. The passage then discusses cases where one remembers a missed action while in another action: if you are in prostration and remember missing a bowing from a previous rak'ah, you make up the bowing and its two prostrations. If you are in bowing and remember missing prostrations from a previous rak'ah, there is a difference of opinion: according to al-Hidāyah, you do not need to repeat the bowing, but according to Fatāwā Qādīkhān, you must. The core of the dispute is not about order being a condition, but whether the current action is nullified by going back. The Hanafi position is that order is a condition in the specific cases mentioned and wajib in others, and the relied-upon view for fatwa is what is in al-Hidāyah and al-Nihāyah, though the fatwa of Qādīkhān is also considered.

Key Terms
الترتيب (al-tartīb): The prescribed sequence of actions in prayer; a condition (shart) or obligation (wajib) depending on the types of actions involved.
الفرض (al-farḍ): An obligatory action established by definitive (qat'i) evidence; omission invalidates the prayer.
الواجب (al-wājib): An obligatory action established by speculative (zanni) evidence; omission requires sajda sahw but does not invalidate the prayer.
الشرط (al-sharṭ): A condition that must be present for validity; if omitted, the act is invalid.
المتحد (al-muttaḥid): What is single or repeated once (e.g., one sitting, one bowing per rak'ah).
المتعدد (al-mutaʿaddid): What is multiple or repeated (e.g., rak'ahs, prostrations).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on order (tartib) between the actions that are single in each rak'ah (like standing and bowing) and the actions that are multiple in each rak'ah (like prostrations) when they belong to the same rak'ah?
A) Order is a condition (shart); violation invalidates the prayer.
B) Order is wajib; violation requires sajda sahw but prayer is valid.
C) Order is sunnah; no compensation needed.
D) Order is not required at all.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, tartib is a condition only between single actions and all others; between repeated actions it is wajib, and the preferred view is that returning to a missed action does not nullify the current action.

Order of Actions and Ruling on Missed Parts in Prayer
Commentary on order and irtifad in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of tartib to determine whether to repeat a current action after remembering a missed prior action in prayer, and distinguish between the rulings of Al-Hidayah and Fatawa Qadikhan.

Core Idea
In Hanafi prayer, order is a condition only within the same rak'ah; irtifad determines if a current action is invalidated by returning to a missed one.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on the sequence (tartib) of actions in prayer. When a worshipper remembers a missed obligatory action while in the midst of another action, the key question is whether the current action is invalidated by returning to the missed one. The classical sources reveal a nuanced dispute within the Hanafi school itself, turning on the concept of irtifad (invalidation of a pillar before completion). Understanding this dispute prepares you to apply the correct ruling in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the remembered action and its position
Determine which action was missed and whether it belongs to the same rak'ah as the current action or a previous one. This distinction is crucial because tartib is a condition only within the same rak'ah.
For example, remembering a missed sujud (prostration) while in ruku' (bowing) of the same rak'ah vs. remembering a missed sujud from a previous rak'ah.
2
Determine the current action's completion status
Check whether the current action (e.g., ruku' or sujud) has been completed by raising (raf') from it. If it has not yet been completed, it is susceptible to irtifad (invalidation).
Completion status is the key factor in the dispute between Al-Hidayah and Fatawa Qadikhan.
3
Apply the basic rule of tartib
If the missed action belongs to the same rak'ah, tartib is a condition (shart) and the current action must be repeated after making up the missed action. If from a different rak'ah, tartib is not a condition and repetition is not obligatory.
This rule is agreed upon in the Hanafi school.
4
Analyse the disagreement via irtifad
When the current action is not yet completed, Fatawa Qadikhan holds that returning to the missed action invalidates (irtifad) the current action, necessitating its repetition. Al-Hidayah holds that the current action is not invalidated and repetition is only recommended.
The difference stems from whether a pillar that has not been completed can be invalidated by a return.
5
Derive the practical ruling
If the current action is less than a complete rak'ah's addition, the prayer remains valid. If it results in an extra complete rak'ah (e.g., an extra ruku' and two sujud), the prayer becomes corrupt (batil).
This final ruling accounts for the possibility of an extra rak'ah being added.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصلاة يعني الركعات أو يتحد في كل ركعة وبين ما يتعدد في كل ركعة ليس على إطلاقه، بل بين السجود والمتحد في كل ركعة تفصيل إن كان سجود ذلك الركوع بأن يكون ركوعاً وسجوداً من ركعة واحدة فالترتيب شرط، وإن كان ركوعاً من ركعة وسجوداً من أخرى بأن تذكر في سجدة ركوع ركعة قبل ركوع هذه السجدة قضى الركوع وسجدتيه، وإن تذكر على القلب بأن تذكر في ركوع أنه لم يسجد في الركعة قبلها سجدها وهل يعيد الركوع والسجود المتذكر فيه؟ ففي الهداية إنه لا تجب الإعادة بل تستحب معللاً بأن الترتيب ليس بفرض بين ما يتكرر في الأفعال والذي في فتاوى قاضيخان وغيره ، أنه يعيد معللاً بأنه ارتفض بالعود إلى ما قبله من الأركان لأنه قبل الرفع منه يقبل الرفض، ولهذا ذكر هو فيما لو تذكر سجدة بعد ما رفع من الركوع أنه يقضيها ولا يعيد الركوع لأنه بعد ما تم بالرفع لا يقبل الرفض، فعلم أن الاختلاف في الإعادة ليس بناء على اشتراط الترتيب وعدمه بل عن أن الركن المتذكر فيه هل يرتفض بالعود إلى ما قبله من الأركان أو لا، وفي الكافي للحاكم: رجل افتتح الصلاة وقرأ وركع ولم يسجد ثم قام فقرأ وسجد ولم يركع، فهذا قد صلى ركعة، وكذلك إن ركع أولاً ثم قرأ وركع وسجد فإنما صلى ركعة واحدة، وكذلك إن سجد أولاً سجدتين ثم قام فقرأ في الثانية وركع ولم يسجد ثم قام فقرأ وسجد في الثالثة ولم يركع فإنما صلى ركعة واحدة، وكذلك إن ركع في الأولى ولم يسجد وركع في الثانية ولم يسجد ثم سجد في الثالثة ولم يركع فإنما صلى واحدة .ا.هـ. كذا في فتح القدير. ثم اعلم أن في كل موضع يشترط فيه الترتيب، وقلنا يفسد بتركه الركن الذي فيه كما قدمنا هل تفسد الصلاة بالكلية ينظر؛ إن كانت الزيادة ركعة تامة تفسد لما أن الركعة لا تقبل الرفض حتى يراعي الترتيب المشروط برفضها، وأما إن كانت الزيادة ما دون الركعة فلا تفسد إليه أشار في النهاية.
[The passage discusses] the prayer meaning the rak'ahs or what is single in each rak'ah and between what is multiple in each rak'ah not absolutely, but between the prostration and what is single in each rak'ah there is detail: if the prostration is of that bowing, meaning there is bowing and prostration from one rak'ah, then order is a condition; and if it is bowing from one rak'ah and prostration from another, like one remembers in a prostration the bowing of a rak'ah before the bowing of this prostration, he performs the bowing and its two prostrations; and if he remembers in reverse, like he remembers in bowing that he did not prostrate in the previous rak'ah, he prostrates it, and is the bowing and the prostration in which he remembered repeated? In al-Hidayah it is said that repetition is not obligatory but recommended, justified by that order is not an obligation between repeated actions; and in Fatawa Qadikhan and others it is said that he repeats, justified by that it has been invalidated by returning to the preceding pillars, because before rising from it it can be invalidated; and for this he mentioned regarding one who remembers a prostration after raising from bowing that he makes it up and does not repeat the bowing because after it is completed by raising it cannot be invalidated. So it is known that the difference in repetition is not based on stipulating order and its absence, but on whether the pillar remembered in it is invalidated by returning to the preceding pillars or not. And in al-Kafi by al-Hakim: a man began the prayer, recited and bowed and did not prostrate, then stood and recited and prostrated and did not bow; so this has prayed one rak'ah. Similarly if he bowed first, then recited and bowed and prostrated, he has only prayed one rak'ah. Similarly if he prostrated first two prostrations, then stood and recited in the second and bowed and did not prostrate, then stood and recited and prostrated in the third and did not bow, he has only prayed one rak'ah. Similarly if he bowed in the first and did not prostrate, and bowed in the second and did not prostrate, then prostrated in the third and did not bow, he has only prayed one. End quote. So in Fath al-Qadir. Then know that in every place where order is stipulated, and we said the prayer becomes corrupt by leaving the pillar that is in it as we presented, it is considered whether the entire prayer becomes corrupt: if the increase is a complete rak'ah it becomes corrupt because the rak'ah cannot be invalidated such that the stipulated order is observed by invalidating it; but if the increase is less than a rak'ah then it does not become corrupt, as indicated in al-Nihayah.
Source pages p. 521

Commentary
This is a commentary (sharh) on Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifying the rules of order (tartib) between actions in prayer. The author explains that order is a condition (shart) only between actions that belong to the same rak'ah—for example, the sujud specific to a particular ruku'. If one remembers a missed ruku' while in sujud of another rak'ah, he performs that ruku' along with its associated sujud. However, if he remembers a missed sujud while in ruku', there is a dispute among Hanafi authorities: al-Hidayah advises that it is not obligatory to repeat the current ruku', while Fatawa Qadikhan requires repetition, based on whether the current pillar is invalidated by returning to the missed one. The text then cites al-Kafi to illustrate how missing actions affect counting rak'ahs: if one performs a bowing and a prostration in the same sequence, it counts as one rak'ah regardless of order. Finally, it rules that if the forgotten element leads to an extra complete rak'ah, the prayer becomes null; if the addition is less than a rak'ah, the prayer remains valid. This lesson relies on rational reasoning (istihsan and analysis of irtifad).

Key Terms
ترتيب (tartib): The prescribed sequential order between actions of prayer.
قضاء (qada'): Making up a missed obligatory part of prayer after remembering it.
رفض (irtifad): Invalidation or rejection of a pillar by returning to a previous action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the underlying reason for the disagreement between al-Hidayah and Fatawa Qadikhan regarding whether to repeat the ruku' after remembering a missed sujud?
A) Whether tartib is a condition
B) Whether the current pillar is invalidated by returning to the earlier one
C) Whether the prayer is valid
D) Whether the missed sujud is fard

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi prayer, order (tartib) is only a condition within the same rak'ah; between different rak'ahs, the current action's invalidation depends on whether it has been completed, leading to an intra-madhhab dispute on repetition.

Ta'dil al-Arkan: Wajib, Fard, or Sunnah?
Commentary on the ruling of settling the limbs in bowing and prostration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi ruling on ta'dil al-arkan, identify the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf, and explain the Hanafi proof that distinguishes wajib from fard.

Core Idea
Ta'dil al-arkan is wajib in the Hanafi school — omitting it renders the prayer deficient but not invalid.

The obligation to settle the limbs in bowing and prostration (ta'dil al-arkan) is a key element of prayer whose legal status has been debated within the Hanafi school. This passage from Bahru al-Ra'iq clarifies the three opinions — fard, wajib, and sunnah — and presents the evidence that leads the majority of later Hanafis to adopt the wajib view. Understanding this distinction is crucial for proper prayer practice and for appreciating how Hanafi usul balances Quranic texts with hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its definition
Read the opening definition of ta'dil al-arkan: calming the limbs in ruku' and sujud until the joints settle. Note the minimum duration (one tasbih).
This is the practical baseline.
2
Map the three Hanafi views
Identify the three positions: fard (Abu Yusuf), wajib (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), and sunnah (al-Jurjani). Recognize that the passage argues for wajib as the correct view.
This is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
3
Analyse the proof for fard (Abu Yusuf)
Examine Abu Yusuf's dalil: the hadith of al-musi' salatuh, where the Prophet commands the man to repeat his prayer because he lacked tranquility. The command to repeat implies the prayer was invalid, making tranquility fard.
This is a straightforward reading of the hadith.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response (wajib view)
Follow Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's rebuttal: the Quranic verse ('Bow and prostrate') is specific and cannot be added to by a solitary hadith. The command to repeat is interpreted as wajib (not fard), and the negation of prayer is interpreted as negation of perfection. The Prophet's approval of the man continuing after the first rak'ah shows the prayer was not invalid.
This is a subtle usul-based argument.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Note that the text declares the wajib view as 'as-sahih' (correct) and cites al-Karkhi and Sharh al-Munyah. Al-Jurjani's sunnah view is weakened. The mufta bihi today is wajib.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وتعديل الأركان) وهو تسكين الجوارح في الركوع والسجود حتى تطمئن مفاصله. وأدناه مقدار تسبيحة، وهو واجب على تخريج الكرخي وهو الصحيح كما في شرح المنية، وسنة على تخريج الجرجاني، وفرض على ما نقله الحاوي عن الثلاثة. والذي نقله الجم الغفير أنه واجب عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد فرض عند أبي يوسف مستدلين له ولمن وافقه بحديث المسيء صلاته حيث قال: ارجع فصل فإنك لم تصل ثلاث مرات، وأمره له بالطمأنينة، فالأمر بالإعادة لا يجب إلا عند فساد الصلاة ومطلق الأمر يفيد الافتراض. وبما أخرجه أصحاب السنن الأربعة مرفوعاً لا تجزئ صلاة لا يقيم الرجل فيها صلبه في الركوع والسجود ولهما قوله تعالى اركعوا واسجدوا ﴾ [الحج : ٧٧] واللفظان خاصان معلوم معناهما فلا تجوز الزيادة عليهما بخبر الواحد لأنه لا يصلح ناسخاً للكتاب ويصلح مكملاً، فيحمل أمره بالإعادة والطمأنينة على الوجوب ونفيه للصلاة على نفي كمالها كنفي الإجزاء في الحديث الثاني على نفي الإجزاء الكامل ويدل عليه آخر حديث المسيء صلاته فإنه قال فيه : فإذا فعلت ذلك فقد تمت صلاتك، وإن انتقصت منه شيئاً انتقصت صلاتك. فقد سماها صلاة والباطلة ليست صلاة ولأنه تركه عليه السلام بعد أول ركعة حتى أتم، ولو كان عدمها مفسداً لفسدت بأول ركعة وبعد الفساد لا يحل المضي في الصلاة، وتقريره عليه السلام من الأدلة الشرعية ويدل على وجوبها المواظبة عليها، وبهذا يضعف قول الجرجاني ولهذا سئل محمد عن تركها فقال : أني أخاف أن لا تجوز. وعن السرخسي: من
His statement: (And ta'dil al-arkan) which is calming the limbs in bowing and prostration until his joints settle. Its minimum is the duration of one tasbih. It is wajib according to the derivation of al-Karkhi, and it is correct as in Sharh al-Munyah, and sunnah according to the derivation of al-Jurjani, and fard according to what al-Hawi reported from the three. And what the great multitude reported is that it is wajib according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, fard according to Abu Yusuf. They adduce for him and those who agree with him the hadith of the man who prayed badly: 'Return and pray, for you have not prayed' three times, and he ordered him to have tranquility. So the command to repeat is only necessary upon corruption of prayer, and an absolute command indicates obligation. And by what the authors of the four Sunan narrated as marfu': 'A prayer in which a man does not straighten his back in bowing and prostration is not valid.' And for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is His statement: 'Bow and prostrate' (Qur'an 22:77). The two wordings are specific, their meanings are known, so it is not permissible to add to them via a solitary hadith because it cannot abrogate the Book but can complete it. So His command to repeat and the tranquility is interpreted as obligation, and His negation of the prayer is interpreted as negation of its perfection. Similarly, the negation in the second hadith is interpreted as negation of complete validity. And evidence for this is the end of the hadith of the man who prayed badly: 'When you do that, then your prayer is complete; and if you omit from it anything, your prayer is deficient.' So he called it prayer, and the invalid is not prayer. And because the Prophet peace be upon him left him to continue after the first rak'ah until he finished; had its omission been corrupting, it would have been corrupted from the first rak'ah, and after corruption it is not permissible to continue in prayer. And the Prophet's approval is one of the legal proofs. And it indicates its obligation that he adhered to it continuously. And by this the statement of al-Jurjani is weakened. And for this Muhammad was asked about leaving it and he said: 'I fear that it is not permissible.' And from al-Sarakhsi: 'Whoever...'
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This is a commentary (sharh) explaining the ruling of 'ta'dil al-arkan', defined as calming the limbs in ruku' and sujud until the joints are at rest. The minimal time is the duration of one tasbih. The author presents three views within the Hanafi school: it is wajib according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the correct view as per al-Karkhi), fard according to Abu Yusuf, and sunnah according to al-Jurjani. Proofs are given for the fard view: the hadith of the man who prayed badly (musi' salatuh) where the Prophet ordered him to repeat his prayer and specifically mentioned tranquility (tuma'ninah), and another hadith stating that a prayer without straightening the back is not valid. The opponents (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) argue that these proofs indicate obligation (wujub) rather than strict obligation (fard), because the Quranic verse ('Bow and prostrate') is specific and cannot be added to by a solitary hadith—so the command for tranquility is interpreted as wajib, and the negation of prayer is interpreted as negation of perfection. The text also notes that the Prophet allowed the man to continue his prayer after the first rak'ah, which would not be permissible if the omission were corrupting (mufsid). Therefore, the relied-upon position is that ta'dil al-arkan is wajib.

Key Terms
تعديل الأركان (ta'dil al-arkan): Settling the limbs in ruku' and sujud so that the joints are at rest.
طمأنينة (tuma'ninah): Tranquility and stillness of the body during prayer.
المسيء صلاته (al-musi' salatuh): The man who performed his prayer poorly as described in the hadith, who was taught by the Prophet the correct manner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling of ta'dil al-arkan?
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that ta'dil al-arkan is wajib; omitting it makes the prayer deficient but not invalid.

Missing a Rukn and Its Effect on Prayer Validity
Explains when missing a rukn invalidates the entire prayer versus just the rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for when missing a rukn invalidates the entire prayer versus just the rak'ah, and identify whether an extra action constitutes a complete rak'ah.

Core Idea
Missing a rukn invalidates the whole prayer only if it creates an extra complete rak'ah.

In prayer, maintaining the proper sequence (tartib) within each rak'ah is essential. However, not every mistake nullifies the entire prayer. The Hanafi school distinguishes between errors that can be remedied within the same rak'ah and those that create an extra, unwanted rak'ah. This lesson unpacks that distinction using examples from Fath al-Qadir and al-Nihayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the missing rukn
Determine which pillar (rukn) was omitted—such as ruku' or sujud. In the examples, the person omits either bowing or prostrating in a particular rak'ah.
The missing rukn is the key to the analysis.
2
Check whether the subsequent actions form a complete rak'ah
Examine if the actions performed after the omission, when combined with other actions, create a full unit (both ruku' and sujud in proper order). A rak'ah requires both ruku' and sujud in sequence.
A complete rak'ah = ruku' followed by sujud, or vice versa? Actually the text implies order matters: if you bow then prostrate later without bowing again, it's not a full rak'ah.
3
Apply the ruling: complete extra rak'ah → prayer invalid
If the omission and later actions produce a complete extra rak'ah, the entire prayer becomes invalid because a rak'ah cannot be discarded to restore order.
The reasoning: the extra rak'ah is a confirmed entity and cannot be nullified, so the prayer is corrupted.
4
Apply the ruling: less than a rak'ah → prayer valid
If the extra actions are less than a full rak'ah, the prayer remains valid and the mistake is corrected by performing the missing rukn later.
In this case, the missing rukn is effectively compensated within the same prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصلاة وقرأ وركع ولم يسجد ثم قام فقرأ وسجد ولم يركع، فهذا قد صلى ركعة، وكذلك إن ركع أولاً ثم قرأ وركع وسجد فإنما صلى ركعة واحدة، وكذلك إن سجد أولاً سجدتين ثم قام فقرأ في الثانية وركع ولم يسجد ثم قام فقرأ وسجد في الثالثة ولم يركع فإنما صلى ركعة واحدة، وكذلك إن ركع في الأولى ولم يسجد وركع في الثانية ولم يسجد ثم سجد في الثالثة ولم يركع فإنما صلى واحدة .ا.هـ. كذا في فتح القدير. ثم اعلم أن في كل موضع يشترط فيه الترتيب، وقلنا يفسد بتركه الركن الذي فيه كما قدمنا هل تفسد الصلاة بالكلية ينظر؛ إن كانت الزيادة ركعة تامة تفسد لما أن الركعة لا تقبل الرفض حتى يراعي الترتيب المشروط برفضها، وأما إن كانت الزيادة ما دون الركعة فلا تفسد إليه أشار في النهاية .
He prayed and recited and bowed but did not prostrate, then stood and recited and prostrated but did not bow; this person has prayed one rak'ah. Similarly, if he bowed first, then recited and bowed and prostrated, he has only prayed one rak'ah. Similarly, if he first prostrated two prostrations, then stood and in the second [rak'ah] recited and bowed but did not prostrate, then stood and in the third recited and prostrated but did not bow, he has only prayed one rak'ah. Similarly, if he bowed in the first but did not prostrate, and bowed in the second but did not prostrate, then prostrated in the third but did not bow, he has only prayed one. End quote from Fath al-Qadir. Then know that wherever order is required, and we said it becomes invalid by leaving the pillar (rukn) in it, as we presented: does the entire prayer become invalid? It is considered: if the increase is a complete rak'ah, it invalidates because a rak'ah is not subject to being discarded until the required order is observed by discarding it. But if the increase is less than a rak'ah, it does not invalidate; this is indicated in al-Nihayah.
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This is a ruling from Fath al-Qadir and al-Nihayah about the effect of missing a rukn on the validity of the prayer. The rule is: if a person omits a rukn (like sujud) and then later performs it in a way that creates an extra rak'ah, the whole prayer becomes invalid if the extra is a full rak'ah. But if it is less than a rak'ah, the prayer is still valid. The examples show what constitutes a rak'ah: the combination of ruku' and sujud in a particular order. The key principle is that the prayer requires sequence (tartib) within each rak'ah, and if a rukn is missed and later performed, it may create an extra partial rak'ah. The ruling depends on whether the extra amounts to a complete rak'ah.

Key Terms
ركعة (rak'ah): A unit of prayer consisting of standing, bowing, and prostration in a specific sequence; in this context, a complete set of actions that when performed after a missed rukn may constitute an extra unit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example where a person bows in the first [rak'ah] but does not prostrate, bows in the second but does not prostrate, then prostrates in the third but does not bow, how many rak'ahs has he prayed?
A) None
B) One
C) Two
D) Three

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that missing a rukn invalidates the entire prayer only when it creates an extra complete rak'ah; otherwise the prayer remains valid.

The Legal Status of Ta'dil al-Arkan: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Proper Posture in Prayer
Intra-Hanafi dispute over ta'dil al-arkan with usul-based proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ikhtilaf on ta'dil al-arkan, apply the madhhab's usul principle that khabar wahid cannot add to a nass, and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Ta'dil al-arkan is wajib (not fard or sunnah) per Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, resolved by interpreting Abu Yusuf's 'fard' as 'fard 'amali'.

In this passage, the author of al-Bahr al-Raiq navigates an intra-Hanafi dispute over the legal status of ta'dil al-arkan—the stillness and proper posture during bowing and prostration. At stake is whether the Quranic command 'Bow and prostrate' can be augmented by a solitary hadith to make stillness an independent obligation. The discussion reveals how the Hanafi school applies its usul principle that a khabar wahid cannot abrogate or add to a specified Quranic command, but can clarify wajib status. You will learn the three positions within the school, the proofs each cites, and how later scholars reconciled them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
From the passage, extract the three views: (1) Abu Hanifa & Muhammad say wajib, (2) Abu Yusuf says fard, (3) al-Jirjani says sunnah. Note that the majority hold the wajib view.
The passage calls al-Jirjani's view weak.
2
Understand the proof of Abu Hanifa & Muhammad
They rely on the Quranic verse 'Bow and prostrate' which is specific (khass). They argue that a khabar wahid (solitary hadith) cannot add a new obligation to a known Quranic command. The Prophet's command to repeat is interpreted as wujub, not to indicate fardiyyah.
This is a key usul principle: khabar wahid can complement but not abrogate a nass.
3
Examine Abu Yusuf's proof
He uses the hadith of the man who prayed badly (musi' salatahu) where the Prophet ordered repetition and mentioned tranquility. He argues that the command to repeat implies the prayer was invalid, and the absolute command to be tranquil indicates obligation (fard).
Abu Yusuf also cites the hadith 'No prayer is valid for one who does not straighten his back.'
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to Abu Yusuf
The Hanafi response is that the Prophet's command to repeat indicates wujub, not fard, because the end of the hadith calls it 'prayer' and says it is 'complete.' The negation is of perfection, not validity. Constant practice (mudawamah) also indicates wujub.
The passage notes the Prophet's approval as a legal proof.
5
Resolve the dispute and apply the mufta bihi
Ibn al-Humam interprets Abu Yusuf's 'fard' as 'fard 'amali' (practical obligation) which is effectively wajib. This reconciles the views. The authoritative (mufta bihi) position is that ta'dil is wajib, meaning if omitted deliberately, the prayer is valid but makruh tahriman and must be repeated.
This resolution shows how later scholars harmonize ikhtilaf within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وتعديل الأركان) وهو تسكين الجوارح في الركوع والسجود حتى تطمئن مفاصله. وأدناه مقدار تسبيحة، وهو واجب على تخريج الكرخي وهو الصحيح كما في شرح المنية، وسنة على تخريج الجرجاني، وفرض على ما نقله الحاوي عن الثلاثة. والذي نقله الجم الغفير أنه واجب عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد فرض عند أبي يوسف مستدلين له ولمن وافقه بحديث المسيء صلاته حيث قال: ارجع فصل فإنك لم تصل ثلاث مرات، وأمره له بالطمأنينة، فالأمر بالإعادة لا يجب إلا عند فساد الصلاة ومطلق الأمر يفيد الافتراض. وبما أخرجه أصحاب السنن الأربعة مرفوعاً لا تجزئ صلاة لا يقيم الرجل فيها صلبه في الركوع والسجود ولهما قوله تعالى اركعوا واسجدوا ﴾ [الحج : الحديث الثاني على نفي الإجزاء الكامل ويدل عليه آخر حديث المسيء صلاته فإنه قال فيه : فإذا فعلت ذلك فقد تمت صلاتك، وإن انتقصت منه شيئاً انتقصت صلاتك. فقد سماها صلاة والباطلة ليست صلاة ولأنه تركه عليه السلام بعد أول ركعة حتى أتم، ولو كان عدمها مفسداً لفسدت بأول ركعة وبعد الفساد لا يحل المضي في الصلاة، وتقريره عليه السلام من الأدلة الشرعية ويدل على وجوبها المواظبة عليها، وبهذا يضعف قول الجرجاني ولهذا سئل محمد عن تركها فقال : أني أخاف أن لا تجوز. وعن السرخسي: من ترك الاعتدال تلزمه الإعادة. ومن المشايخ من قال : تلزمه ويكون الفرض هو الثاني ولا إشكال في وجوب الإعادة إذ هو الحكم في كل صلاة أديت مع كراهة التحريم ويكون جابراً للأول لأن الفرض لا يتكرر، وجعله الثاني يقتضي عدم سقوطه بالأول وهو لازم ترك الركن لا الواجب إلا أن يقال : المراد أن ذلك امتنان من الله تعالى إذ يحتسب الكامل وإن تأخر عن الفرض لما علم سبحانه أنه سيوقعه كذا في فتح القدير. وقد يقال: إن قول أبي يوسف بالفرضية مشكل لأنه وافقهما في الأصول أن الزيادة على الخاص بخبر الواحد لا تجوز فكيف استقام له القول بالجواز ،هنا ولهذا والله أعلم قال المحقق ابن الهمام: ويحمل قول أبي يوسف بالفرضية على الفرض العملي وهو الواجب فيرتفع الخلاف ا هـ. ويؤيده أن هذا الخلاف لم يذكر في ظاهر الرواية على ما قالوا كما في شرح منية المصلي، ولهذا لم يذكر صاحب الأسرار خلاف أبي يوسف وإنما قال قال علماؤنا : الطمأنينة في الركوع والسجود، وفي الانتقال من ركن إلى ركن ليس بركن وكذلك الاستواء بين السجدتين وبين الركوع والسجود ا.هـ. وينبغي أن يحمل ما ذهب إليه الطحاوي من الافتراض على الفرض العملي كما قررناه ليوافق أصول أهل المذهب وإلا فالإشكال أشد قيد بالطمأنينة في الأركان أي الركوع والسجود لأن الطمأنينة في القومة والجلسة سنة عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد بالاتفاق، وعند أبي يوسف فرض كما تقدم، وفي شرح الزاهدي ما يدل على وجوبها عندهما كوجوبها في الأركان فإنه قال : وذكر صدر القضاة وإتمام الركوع وإكمال كل ركن واجب عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد، وعند أبي يوسف والشافعي فرض. وكذا رفع الرأس من الركوع والانتصاب والقيام والطمأنينة فيه فيجب أن يكمل الركوع حتى يطمئن كل عضو منه ويرفع رأسه من الركوع قائماً ويطمئن كل عضو منه، وكذا في السجود، ولو ترك شيئاً من ذلك ناسياً يلزمه سجدتا السهو، ولو تركها عمداً يكره أشد الكراهة ويلزمه أن يعيد الصلاة ا هـ. وهو يدل على وجوب القومة والجلسة وسيأتي التصريح بسنينهما ومقتضى الدليل وجوب الطمأنينة في الأربعة ووجوب نفس الرفع من الركوع والجلوس بين السجدتين للمواظبة على حتى ينتصب أي جعل بعض المشايخ الفرض هو الثاني يلزم منه أنه ركن قوله : فيرتفع الخلاف) قال في النهر : أنت خبير بأن صحة رفع الخلاف موقوفة على أن يراد بالواجب على قولهما أقوى نوعيه وهو ما يفوت الجواز بفوته لكنه لا يفوت على قولهما ويفوت على قونه فأنى يرتفع» وقد صرح في السهو بذلك حيث قال : لو ترا القومة والجلسة فسدت صلاته عند أبي يوسف خلافاً لهما اهـ. وعلى هذا فالإشكال باقي لكن قال بعض الفضلاء يمكن الجواب بأن الركوع والسجود ذكراً في الآية الشريفة مطلقين فانصرفا إلى الكامل وهو ما كان بصفة التعديل، وحينئذ لا يرد عليه لزوم الزيادة بخبر الواحد اهـ. وفي حواشي الدرر للعلامة نوح أفندي بعد ما قرر نحو ما في النهر : وإن المذكور في عامة
His statement: (And ta'dil al-arkan) it is the stillness of the limbs in bowing and prostration until his joints are at rest. Its minimum is the amount of one tasbih. It is wajib according to the derivation of al-Karkhi, and this is the correct view as in Sharh al-Munyah; sunnah according to the derivation of al-Jirjani; and fard according to what al-Hawi narrated from the three [imams]. The vast majority have narrated that it is wajib according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, fard according to Abu Yusuf, providing evidence for himself and those who agree with him by the hadith of the man who prayed badly where he [the Prophet] said: 'Go back and pray, for you have not prayed' three times, and his command to him of tranquility (tuma'ninah). The command to repeat only becomes obligatory when the prayer is invalid, and an absolute command indicates obligation. And by what the four Sunan compilers narrated as a marfu' hadith: 'The prayer of a man who does not straighten his back in bowing and prostration is not valid.' And for the two Sahibs [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] there is the saying of Allah: 'Bow and prostrate' [al-Hajj:77]. The two expressions are specific, their meaning is known, so it is not permissible to add to them by a solitary report (khabar wahid) because it is not suitable to abrogate the Book but is suitable to complete. So his command to repeat and to [have] tranquility is interpreted as obligation, and his negation of prayer is interpreted as negation of its perfection, like the negation of acceptability in the second hadith is interpreted as negation of perfect acceptability. This is supported by the end of the hadith of the man who prayed badly, for he said in it: 'When you do that, your prayer is complete, and if you diminish anything from it, your prayer is diminished.' So he called it prayer (salah), and an invalid prayer is not [called] prayer. And because he [the Prophet] left him [the man] after the first rak'ah until he completed [the prayer]; if its absence were invalidating, it would have been invalidated from the first rak'ah, and after invalidation it is not permissible to continue in the prayer. The Prophet's approval is among the legal proofs, and it indicates its obligation through constant practice. Thus the saying of al-Jirjani is weakened. For this reason, when Muhammad was asked about leaving it, he said: 'I fear that it may not be valid.' And from al-Sarakhsi: Whoever leaves i'tidal (standing upright) must repeat. And among the mashayikh is one who said: He must repeat, and the fard is the second one, and there is no problem in the obligation of repetition because that is the ruling in every prayer performed with karahah tahrirman, and it serves as a compensator for the first because the fard does not repeat. Making it the second implies that it is not dropped by the first, and that is the necessary consequence of leaving a rukn, not a wajib. But it may be said that the meaning is that this is a favor from Allah Almighty, for He counts the perfect [prayer] even if it occurs after the fard because He knows that he will perform it; as in Fath al-Qadir. And it may be said: Indeed the statement of Abu Yusuf that it is fard is problematic because he agrees with them in principles that adding to a specific [text] by a solitary report is not permissible, so how can he allow it here? For this reason, and Allah knows best, al-Muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam said: Abu Yusuf's saying of fard is interpreted as 'fard 'amali' (practical obligation) which is wajib, so the disagreement is resolved. It is supported by the fact that this disagreement is not mentioned in the zahir al-riwayah, as they said in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli. For this reason, the author of al-Asrar did not mention the disagreement of Abu Yusuf; rather he said: 'Our scholars said: Tranquility in bowing and prostration and in moving from one pillar to another is not a pillar, similarly the leveling between the two prostrations and between bowing and prostration.' It is appropriate to interpret what al-Tahawi went to of obligation (iftirad) as 'fard 'amali' as we have established, to agree with the principles of the school, otherwise the problem is more severe. The restriction of tranquility is to the pillars, i.e., bowing and prostration, because tranquility in the standing (qawma) and sitting (jalsa) is sunnah according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad by agreement, and according to Abu Yusuf it is fard as previously. In Sharh al-Zahidi there is something indicating its obligation according to them both like its obligation in the pillars, for he said: 'And Sadr al-Qudah mentioned: Completing the bowing and completing every pillar is wajib according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and according to Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i it is fard. Similarly, raising the head from bowing and standing straight and standing and tranquility in it; so one must complete the bowing until every limb is still, and raise his head from bowing standing and make every limb still, similarly in prostration. If one leaves anything of that forgetfully, sajdat al-sahw are necessary; if one leaves it deliberately, it is severely disliked and he must repeat the prayer.' This indicates the obligation of qawma and jalsa, and the explicit statement of their being sunnah will come. The requirement of the evidence is the obligation of tranquility in all four [positions] and the obligation of the very act of raising from bowing and of sitting between the two prostrations due to constant practice. Until he stands straight. Meaning: Some mashayikh made the fard the second which necessitates that it is a rukn. His saying: 'so the dispute is resolved' – in al-Nahr he said: 'You are aware that the validity of resolving the dispute depends on intending by 'wajib' according to them the stronger of its two types, which is that which makes permissibility lost if it is lost; but it is not lost according to them while it is lost according to him – so how can it be resolved?' And he explicitly stated in the chapter on forgetfulness: 'If one leaves qawma and jalsa, his prayer is invalid according to Abu Yusuf contrary to them.' Hence the problem remains. But some virtuous scholars said that the answer is possible: that bowing and prostration are mentioned in the noble verse absolutely, so they refer to the complete [act], which is that with the attribute of ta'dil. In that case, the objection of adding by a solitary report does not apply. In the glosses of al-Durar by 'Allamah Nuh Afandi after he established something similar to what is in al-Nahr: 'And indeed what is mentioned in most [works]...'
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the legal status of ta'dil al-arkan, i.e., the stillness and proper posture during the prayer's pillars (bowing and prostration). The author begins by defining ta'dil as the settling of the limbs until the joints are at rest, with a minimum of one tasbih. He then presents three views: (1) wajib according to al-Karkhi, which is the correct view; (2) sunnah according to al-Jirjani; (3) fard as transmitted by al-Hawi from the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). However, the majority hold that it is wajib for Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and fard for Abu Yusuf. The dispute is grounded in evidence: Abu Yusuf and those who agree with him use the hadith of the 'musi' salatahu' (the man who prayed badly) where the Prophet commanded repetition and tranquility, arguing that a command to repeat indicates invalidity, and an absolute command indicates obligation. They also cite the hadith 'No prayer is valid for a man who does not straighten his back in bowing and prostration.' The other side (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) rely on the Quranic verse 'Bow and prostrate' (al-Hajj:77), arguing that these are specific commands and cannot have additions imposed by a solitary report (khabar wahid). They interpret the command to repeat as indicating obligation (wujub) rather than fard, and the negation of prayer as negation of perfection. They support this with the end of the hadith where the Prophet calls it 'prayer' and says it is 'complete.' The commentator then discusses the resolution: Ibn al-Humam interprets Abu Yusuf's 'fard' as 'fard 'amali' (practical obligation), which is effectively wajib, thereby resolving the dispute. He notes that this disagreement is not found in the zahir al-riwayah. The text also distinguishes between ta'dil in the pillars (rukn) vs. in the standing and sitting (qawma and jalsa). According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, tranquility in qawma and jalsa is sunnah, while Abu Yusuf considers it fard. The practical consequence: leaving it forgetfully requires sajdat al-sahw; leaving it deliberately incurs karahah tahrirman and necessitates repetition. Some scholars argue that the Quranic verse refers to the complete act with ta'dil, so no addition is made. The passage ends with a citation from al-Nahr and glosses, indicating that the issue remains nuanced.

Key Terms
تعديل الأركان (ta'dil al-arkan): The stillness and proper posture of the limbs during bowing and prostration until the joints are at rest.
الطمأنينة (tuma'ninah): Tranquility and stillness; settling of the body in each posture.
الفرض العملي (fard 'amali): A 'practical fard' – a term used to reconcile Abu Yusuf's position; it is effectively the same as wajib, meaning it is not a pillar (rukn) but is obligatory to the extent that the prayer is valid only if performed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, what is the legal status of ta'dil al-arkan (proper stillness) in prayer?
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah mu'akkadah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon position is that ta'dil al-arkan is wajib, meaning deliberate omission invalidates the perfection but not the prayer itself, though repetition is required.

Salah — Prayer

The Status of Tuma'ninah in Prayer: Wajib or Fard?
Resolution of internal Hanafi dispute on tuma'ninah status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on tuma'ninah and state the mufta bihi position according to Ibn al-Humām.

Core Idea
Tuma'ninah in ruku' and sujud is wajib, not fard; Abu Yusuf's 'fard' is interpreted as fard 'amali.

This lesson explores a nuanced internal disagreement among the Hanafi imams regarding the legal status of tuma'ninah—tranquility—in prayer. While the Qur'an commands ruku' and sujud, the required level of stillness is debated. Understanding how later scholars reconciled the views of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf demonstrates the madhhab's method of harmonizing apparent contradictions within its own usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested acts
Determine which prayer postures are under discussion: ruku', sujud, qawmah (standing after ruku'), and jalsah (sitting between prostrations).
The dispute primarily focuses on whether tuma'ninah in these acts is a pillar (fard) or an obligatory element (wajib).
2
State the positions of the Hanafi imams
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, tuma'ninah in ruku' and sujud is wajib, while in qawmah and jalsah it is sunnah. Abu Yusuf considers it fard in all four.
Abu Yusuf's view appears to contradict the Hanafi principle that khabar wahid cannot add to a qat'i text.
3
Analyze the usul problem
Abu Yusuf's agreement with the other imams on the usul principle but differing on this branch requires reconciliation. The principle: a solitary hadith cannot add to the absolute Qur'anic command.
This tension led Ibn al-Humām to propose an interpretation.
4
Apply Ibn al-Humām's resolution
Ibn al-Humām interprets Abu Yusuf's 'fard' as fard 'amali, meaning practically obligatory (wajib), not a true pillar. This removes the contradiction.
Fard 'amali is a technical term used to denote that which is treated as fard in practice but is usulically wajib.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The later preferred position (Ibn al-Humām and Ibn Amir Hajj) is that tuma'ninah in all four postures is wajib, requiring sajdat al-sahw if omitted forgetfully and repetition if deliberate.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.

وللأمر في حديث المسيء صلاته وفي فتاوى قاضيخان في فصل ما يوجب السهو قال : المصلي إذا ركع ولم يرفع رأسه من الركوع حتى خرَّ ساجداً ساهياً تجوز صلاته في قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد وعليه السهو ا هـ . وفي المحيط : لو ترك تعديل الأركان أو القومة التي بين الركوع والسجود ساهياً لزمه سجود السهو ا هـ. فيكون حكم الجلسة بين السجدتين كذلك لأن الكلام فيهما واحد والقول بوجوب الكل هو مختار المحقق ابن الهمام وتلميذه ابن أمير حاج حتى قال : إنه الصواب والله الموفق للصواب.
Leaving i'tidal necessitates repetition (i'adah). Some mashayikh said: it necessitates (repetition) and the fard is the second, and there is no problem in the obligation of redoing because it is the ruling for every prayer performed with tahrimi karahah, and it becomes a compensator for the first because the fard does not repeat; making it the second implies that it did not fall with the first, and that is necessary for leaving a rukn, not a wajib, unless it is said: the meaning is that this is a grace from Allah, for He counts the complete one even if delayed from the fard because He the Exalted knows that he will perform it. So in Fath al-Qadir. And it may be said: The statement of Abu Yusuf that it is fard is problematic because he agreed with them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) in usul that adding to the specific via khabar wahid is not permissible, so how can he consistently allow it here? Hence, with knowledge from Allah, the muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam said: The statement of Abu Yusuf of being fard is interpreted as fard 'amali, which is wajib, so the difference is resolved. This is supported by the fact that this difference is not mentioned in the zahir al-riwayah according to what they said, as in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli. In Sharh al-Zahidi there is an indication of its obligation (wujub) with them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) like its obligation in the pillars, for he said: And Sadr al-Qudat mentioned that completing the ruku' and completing every pillar is wajib according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and according to Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i it is fard. Likewise raising the head from ruku', standing straight, and tuma'ninah in it; so he must complete the ruku' until every limb is at rest, and raise his head from ruku' standing and set every limb at rest, and likewise in sujud. If he leaves something of that forgetfully, two prostrations of forgetfulness are incumbent; if he leaves it deliberately, it is severely disliked and he must repeat the prayer. This indicates the obligation (wujub) of qawmah and jalsah, and explicit statements of their being sunnah will come later; and the evidence demands obligation (wujub) of tuma'ninah in the four (positions) and obligation of the very act of raising from ruku' and sitting between the two prostrations due to continuous practice (muwazabah). And he explicitly stated in the section on forgetfulness that: If he leaves the qawmah and jalsah, his prayer becomes invalid according to Abu Yusuf contrary to them. So the problem remains. But some virtuous scholars said: It is possible to answer that ruku' and sujud are mentioned in the noble verse as absolute, so they refer to the complete one, which is that which possesses the attribute of proper positioning (ta'dil); then the objection of adding via khabar wahid does not apply. In Hawashi al-Durar by 'Allamah Nuh Afandi, after establishing something similar to al-Nahr: And that which is mentioned in general all of that, and due to the command in the hadith of the one who prayed badly, and in Fatawa Qadikhan in the chapter on what necessitates forgetfulness he said: If one praying bows but does not raise his head from bowing until he falls prostrate forgetfully, his prayer is valid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and forgetfulness (sujud) is required. In al-Muhit: If he leaves the straightening of the limbs (ta'dil al-arkan) or the qawmah between ruku' and sujud forgetfully, sajdat al-sahw are required. So the ruling of the sitting (jalsah) between the two prostrations is similarly, because the discussion regarding both is the same; and the view of obligation of all is the choice of the muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam and his student Ibn Amir Hajj, until he said: It is correct, and Allah is the giver of success.
Source pages p. 523

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (intra_hanafi_dispute) concerning the status of tuma'ninah (tranquility/steadiness) in prayer, particularly in the positions of ruku' (bowing), sujud (prostration), qawmah (standing after ruku'), and jalsah (sitting between prostrations). The core issue is whether these elements are farḍ (obligatory in the strong sense, pillar) or wājib (obligatory but slightly weaker). The author first discusses leaving i'tidal (standing up from ruku') and notes that some mashāyikh hold the fard to be the second action (i.e., the corrected one), requiring i'adah (repetition) because the prayer was performed with makruh tahrimi. The author then raises a key problem: Abu Yusuf's view that tuma'ninah is fard seems inconsistent with the Ḥanafī principle that a khabar wāḥid (single-authenticated hadith) cannot add to the qat'i text of the Qur'an. The muḥaqqiq Ibn al-Humām resolves this by interpreting Abu Yusuf's 'fard' as fard 'amali, which is practically equivalent to wājib, thereby removing the inconsistency. The passage further notes that this khilāf is not mentioned in ẓāhir al-riwāyah (the core transmitted texts of Imam Muhammad), and that leading scholars like al-Ṭaḥāwī's view should also be interpreted as such. The commentary then elaborates on the positions: according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, tuma'ninah in ruku' and sujud is wājib, while in qawmah and jalsah it is sunnah (though some later texts indicate obligation). Abu Yusuf considers all four as farḍ. The passage concludes with a citation from al-Muḥīṭ and other sources that the muftā bihī position (the choice of Ibn al-Humām) is that all these elements are wājib, requiring sajdat al-sahw if omitted forgetfully and i'adah if deliberate.

Key Terms
طمأنينة (ṭuma'nīnah): Tranquility and steadiness in the prayer postures such that each limb settles.
فرض عملي (farḍ 'amalī): A term used by some Ḥanafī scholars to denote that which is practically obligatory though theoretically wājib; used to reconcile Abu Yūsuf's position with the madhhab's uṣūl.
مواظبة (muwāẓabah): The continuous and consistent practice of the Prophet upon a certain action, indicating wujūb.
تعديل الأركان (ta'dīl al-arkān): Straightening and completing the postures (rukū', sujūd, qawmah, jalsah) with proper pace and rest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn al-Humām's resolution, how is Abu Yūsuf's statement that tuma'ninah is farḍ to be understood?
A) It means it is a pillar (rukn) without which the prayer is invalid.
B) It means 'farḍ 'amalī' which is equivalent to wājib, not a true pillar.
C) It means it is sunnah mu'akkadah.
D) It means it is mustaḥabb.

Key Takeaway
The later Hanafi position (Ibn al-Humām) affirms that tuma'ninah in all four postures is wajib, resolving the internal dispute by interpreting Abu Yusuf's 'fard' as fard 'amali.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
