قوله: (وسننها رفع اليدين للتحريمة للمواظبة وهي وإن كانت من غير ترك تفيد الوجوب لكن إذا لم يكن ما يفيد إنها ليست لحامل الوجوب وقد وجد وهو تعليمه الأعرابي من غير ذكر تأويل وتأخير البيان عن وقت الحاجة لا يجوز على أنه حكي في الخلاصة خلافاً في تركه، وقيل يأثم وقيل لا . قال : والمختار إن اعتاده أثم لا إن كان أحياناً ا هـ . . وفي فتح القدير : وينبغي أن يجعل شقي هذا القول محمل القولين فلا اختلاف حينئذ ولا إثم لنفس الترك بل لأنه اعتياده للاستخفاف وإلا فمشكل أو يكون واجباً ! والذي يظهر من كلام أهل المذهب أن الإثم منوط بترك الواجب أو السنة المؤكدة على الصحيح لتصريحهم بأن من ترك سنن الصلوات الخمس قيل لا يأثم والصحيح أنه يأثم ذكره في فتح القدير وتصريحهم بالإثم لمن ترك الجماعة مع أنها سنة مؤكدة على الصحيح وكذا في نظائره لمن تتبع كلامهم، ولا شك أن الإثم مقول بالتشكيك بعضه أشد من بعض، فالإثم لتارك السنة المؤكدة أخف من الإثم لتارك الواجب، ولهذا قال في شرح منية المصلي في هذه المسألة : ثم المراد بالإثم على هذا إثم يسير كما هو حكم هذه السنة المواظب الله عليها على ما ذكره صدر الإسلام فالحاصل أن القائل بالإثم في ترك الرفع بناه على أنه من سنن الهدى فهو سنة مؤكدة، والقائل بعدمه بناه على أنه من سنن الزوائد بمنزلة المستحق، وقد قال في الذخيرة : وقد روي عن أبي حنيفة ما يدل على عدم الإثم فإنه قال : إن ترك رفع اليدين جاز وإن رفع فهو أفضل ا هـ . وبهذا اندفع ما في الفتح القدير كما لا يخفى قوله : (ونشر أصابعه) وكيفيته أن لا يضم كل الضم ولا يفرج كل التفريج بل يتركها على حالها منشورة. كذا ذكره الشارح والظاهر أن المراد بالنشر عدم الطي بمعنى أنه يسن أن يرفعهما منصوبتين لا مضمومتين حتى تكون الأصابع مع الكف مستقبلة للقبلة ومن السنن أن لا يطأطيء رأسه عند التكبير كما في المبسوط وهو بدعة قوله : (وجهر الإمام بالتكبير) لحاجته إلى الإعلام بالدخول والانتقال . قيد بالإمام لأن المأموم والمنفرد لا يسن لهما الجهر به لأن الأصل في الذكر الإخفاء ولا حاجة لهما إلى الجهر قوله : (والثناء والتعوّذ والتسمية والتأمين سراً) للنقل المستفيض على ما يأتي بيانه. وقول، سراً» راجع إلى الأربعة قوله : (ووضع يمينه على يساره تحت سرته لما في صحيح مسلم عن وائل بن حجر أنه قال : ثم وضع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يده اليمنى على اليسرى. فانتفى به قول مالك بالإرسال وعند الشافعي محله ما فوق السرة تحت الصدر واستدل له النووي بما في صحيح ابن خزيمة عن وائل بن حجر قال : صليت مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فوضع يده اليمنى على يده اليسرى على صدره ولا يخفى أنه لا يطابق المدعي. واستدل مشايخنا بما عن النبي هو أنه قال : ثلاث من سنن المرسلين وذكر من جملتها وضع اليمين على الشمال تحت السرة لكن المخرجين لم يعرفوا فيه مرفوعاً وموقوفاً تحت السرة. ويمكن أن يقال في توجيه المذهب : إن الثابت من السنة وضع اليمين على الشمال ولم يثبت حديث يوجب تعيين المحل الذي يكون فيه الوضع من البدن إلا حديث وائل المذكور، ويؤيده ما في الكشف الكبير معزياً إلى أصول أبي اليسر حكم السنة أن يندب إلى تحصيلها ويلام على تركها مع لحوق إثم يسير، وكون الاعتياد للاستخفاف يوجب اثماً فيه نظر ففي البزازية لو لم ير السنة حقاً كفر لأنه استخفاف. قوله : (ولا يجوز جره الخ قال بعضهم : يمكن أن يراد بالتكبير ذكر هو تعظيم الله تعالى، سواء كان بلفظ التكبير أو لم يكن جمعاً بين الروايات اهـ. أي ليشمل روايتي التسميع والتكبير عند الرفع من الركوع وسيأتي في الفصل ذكر هذه الرواية عن المحيط وروضة الناطفي، ولذا قال بعض الفضلاء واقتصر الكرماني على إعرابه بالجر ومشى على أن تكبير الرفع من الركوع من السنن لما أنه روي عليه السلام كان يكبر عند كل رفع وخفض، وقد نقل تواتر العمل به بعده ولكن العمل به ترك في زماننا .اهـ.
He said: (And its sunan are raising the hands at the takbir tahrimah due to continuity. And even if that [continuity] without abandoning would indicate obligation, but when there is something indicating that it is not due to obligation, and there is [the incident of] teaching the Bedouin without mentioning interpretation, and delaying clarification beyond the time of need is not permissible. Nevertheless, it is related in al-Khulasah that there is disagreement about leaving it: some say he sins, some say no. He said: The chosen view is that if he habitually leaves it, he sins; if occasionally, no. So it is in al-Hidayah. And in Fath al-Qadir: It is appropriate to make the two parts of this statement the basis of the two views, so there is no disagreement, and no sin for the mere leaving, but because of habitualization leading to disrespect, otherwise it is problematic, or else it would be wajib! And what appears from the words of the school's scholars is that sin is attached to leaving a wajib or a mu'akkadah sunnah according to the correct view, due to their statement that one who leaves the sunan of the five prayers, it is said he does not sin, and the correct view is that he does sin, mentioned in Fath al-Qadir. And their statement that one who leaves the congregation commits a sin, while it is a mu'akkadah sunnah according to the correct view, and similarly in its parallels for those who follow their words. And there is no doubt that sin is said by analogy, some more severe than others. So the sin for leaving the mu'akkadah sunnah is lighter than the sin for leaving the wajib. For this reason, it is said in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli on this issue: Then the intended sin here is a small sin, as is the ruling for this sunnah upon which Allah has kept the Prophet, as mentioned by Sadr al-Islam. So the conclusion is that the one who says sin in leaving the raising [of hands] based it on that it is from the sunan al-huda, so it is a mu'akkadah sunnah; and the one who says no sin based it on that it is from the sunan al-zawa'id, like the mustahabb. And it is said in al-Dhakhirah: And it is narrated from Abu Hanifah something indicating no sin, for he said: If he leaves raising the hands, it is permissible, and if he raises, it is better. End quote. And thus what is in Fath al-Qadir is repelled, as is not hidden. His saying: (and spreading his fingers) and its manner is that he does not squeeze tightly nor spread widely, but leaves them as they are, spread. Thus the commentator mentioned, and the apparent meaning is that by 'spreading' is meant the absence of folding, meaning it is sunnah to raise them upright, not folded, so that the fingers and palm face the qiblah. And it is among the sunan that he not lower his head at the takbir, as in al-Mabsut, and it is a bid'ah. His saying: (and the imam saying the takbir loudly) due to his need to inform of the entry and transition. It is restricted to the imam because neither the follower nor the individual is recommended to say it loudly, since the original in dhikr is concealment, and they have no need for loudness. His saying: (and the thana, ta'awwudh, tasmiyyah, and amin silently) due to the widespread transmission as will be explained. And his saying 'silently' refers to all four. His saying: (and placing his right hand on his left below his navel) due to what is in Sahih Muslim from Wa'il ibn Hujr that he said: Then the Prophet (SAW) placed his right hand on his left. Thus the view of Malik (irsal) is refuted. And according to al-Shafi'i, its place is above the navel below the chest, and al-Nawawi argued for it with what is in Sahih Ibn Khuzaymah from Wa'il ibn Hujr: I prayed with the Messenger of Allah (SAW) and he placed his right hand on his left on his chest, and it is not hidden that this does not match the claim. And our scholars argued with what is from the Prophet (SAW) that he said: Three are from the ways of the messengers, and he mentioned among them placing the right hand on the left below the navel. But the hadith critics did not know it as marfu' or mawquf regarding 'below the navel'. And it can be said in directing the school: What is established from the Sunnah is placing the right on the left, and there is no hadith that specifies the location on the body except the hadith of Wa'il mentioned. And it is supported by what is in al-Kashf al-Kabir, attributed to Usul Abi al-Yusr: The ruling of the sunnah is that one is encouraged to attain it and is blamed for leaving it, along with a slight sin. And that habitualization for disrespect causes sin, there is consideration, for in al-Bazzaziyyah: If one does not consider the sunnah as true, he disbelieves because it is disrespect. His saying: (and it is not permissible to drag...) Some said: It is possible that by takbir is meant dhikr that is magnification of Allah, whether with the wording of takbir or not, combining between the narrations. End quote. That is, to include both narrations of tasmi' and takbir at the raising from ruku', and this will come later in the chapter mentioning this narration from al-Muhit and Rawdat al-Natifi. For this reason, some virtuous ones said, and al-Kirmani confined himself to parsing it with jar (preposition) and proceeded that the takbir of raising from ruku' is among the sunan because it was narrated that he (SAW) used to say takbir at every raising and lowering, and the continuous practice after him was transmitted, but the practice has been abandoned in our time. End quote.
Source pages p. 527

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe from the commentator explaining the sunan (recommended acts) of prayer as per the Hanafi school. The main focus is on raising the hands (raf' al-yadayn) at the opening takbir. The commentator clarifies the legal nature of this act: although consistent practice might suggest obligation (wajib), the Hanafi position is that it is a sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah), not wajib. This is based on reports from Abu Hanifah that leaving it is permissible and that doing it is better. The passage discusses differing views on whether leaving it incurs sin: if one habitually leaves it, there is sin (due to disrespect); if occasional, no sin. The commentator cites Fath al-Qadir to harmonize these views. The act is categorized as sunnah al-huda (guidance sunnah) rather than sunnah al-zawa'id (additional sunnah). The commentator then moves to other sunan: spreading fingers (nashr al-asabi') in a moderate manner, the imam saying takbir loudly to alert the congregation, and reciting thana, ta'awwudh, tasmiyyah, and amin softly. Finally, the passage addresses the placement of hands during prayer: the Hanafi position is to place the right hand on the left below the navel. The commentator provides evidence from Sahih Muslim (the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr) and refutes the Shafi'i view (hands on chest) and Maliki view (hanging). The Hanafi proof includes a hadith stating that three practices are from the ways of the messengers, including placing the right on the left below the navel, though its chain is not fully authenticated. Nevertheless, the school relies on the established sunnah of placement and the absence of a definitive specification of location, thus maintaining the below-navel position.

Key Terms
رفع اليدين (raf' al-yadayn): Raising the hands to the ears or shoulders at the opening takbir (takbir tahrimah) and other similar positions.
نشر الأصابع (nashr al-asabi'): Spreading the fingers moderately during the takbir, not clenching them tightly nor spreading them fully apart.
جهر الإمام بالتكبير (jahr al-imam bi al-takbir): The imam saying the takbir in a loud voice so that the congregation can hear and follow.
سنة الهدى (sunnah al-huda): A sunnah that is consistently practiced and abandoning it habitually may incur a slight sin due to disrespect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does leaving the raising of hands (raf' al-yadayn) incur a sin?
A) Whenever it is left, because it is wajib.
B) Only when it is left habitually out of disrespect.
C) Only when it is left in the first rak'ah.
D) It never incurs sin.

Key Takeaway
Raising hands at the opening takbir is sunnah mu'akkadah, and sin for abandonment only attaches to habitual neglect out of disrespect.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
The Placement of Hands (Wad' al-Yamin 'ala al-Yasar) – Hanafi Position and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Dispute over the placement of hands during prayer and the evidence for the Hanafi position.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on hand placement in prayer, identify the evidence from hadith, and compare it with the Shafi'i and Maliki positions, including the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Hanafis place the right hand on the left below the navel; Shafi'is on the chest; Malikis let them hang; each relies on different evidence.

This passage addresses one of the most visible differences between the madhahib: the placement of hands during prayer (qiyam). The commentator presents the Hanafi view (right hand on left below navel), refutes the Shafi'i and Maliki positions, and provides the evidence. Understanding this dispute illustrates how different schools approach the same hadith corpus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
The text states: 'placing his right hand on his left below his navel'. This is the Hanafi ruling.
The phrase 'below his navel' is key and distinguishes from other schools.
2
Locate the Hanafi evidence
The commentator cites the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr in Sahih Muslim: 'Then the Prophet placed his right hand on his left.' This establishes the act but not the location.
The location (below navel) is supported by another hadith about the ways of the messengers, though its chain is weak.
3
Analyze the opposing positions
Imam al-Shafi'i bases his view (on chest) on a hadith in Sahih Ibn Khuzaymah. Imam Malik relies on the practice of Medina (amal) and irsal (hanging).
The commentator argues the Shafi'i hadith does not prove the claim; the Maliki view contradicts the clear hadith of Wa'il.
4
Follow the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response: the hadith of Wa'il establishes the sunnah of placing hands, and the location below the navel is supported by the practice of the Companions and early scholars, despite weak chain.
The school prioritizes the established sunnah over weak specification; the location is derived from the general practice.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
In practice, Hanafis place hands below navel, Shafi'is on chest, Malikis hang. Each considers their position sunnah and valid.
This difference is purely non-essential (sunnah) and does not affect validity of prayer.

His saying: (and placing his right hand on his left below his navel) due to what is in Sahih Muslim from Wa'il ibn Hujr that he said: Then the Prophet (SAW) placed his right hand on his left. Thus the view of Malik (irsal) is refuted. And according to al-Shafi'i, its place is above the navel below the chest, and al-Nawawi argued for it with what is in Sahih Ibn Khuzaymah from Wa'il ibn Hujr: I prayed with the Messenger of Allah (SAW) and he placed his right hand on his left on his chest, and it is not hidden that this does not match the claim. And our scholars argued with what is from the Prophet (SAW) that he said: Three are from the ways of the messengers, and he mentioned among them placing the right hand on the left below the navel. But the hadith critics did not know it as marfu' or mawquf regarding 'below the navel'. And it can be said in directing the school: What is established from the Sunnah is placing the right on the left, and there is no hadith that specifies the location on the body except the hadith of Wa'il mentioned. And it is supported by what is in al-Kashf al-Kabir, attributed to Usul Abi al-Yusr: The ruling of the sunnah is that one is encouraged to attain it and is blamed for leaving it, along with a slight sin. And that habitualization for disrespect causes sin, there is consideration, for in al-Bazzaziyyah: If one does not consider the sunnah as true, he disbelieves because it is disrespect. His saying: (and it is not permissible to drag...) Some said: It is possible that by takbir is meant dhikr that is magnification of Allah, whether with the wording of takbir or not, combining between the narrations. End quote. That is, to include both narrations of tasmi' and takbir at the raising from ruku', and this will come later in the chapter mentioning this narration from al-Muhit and Rawdat al-Natifi. For this reason, some virtuous ones said, and al-Kirmani confined himself to parsing it with jar (preposition) and proceeded that the takbir of raising from ruku' is among the sunan because it was narrated that he (SAW) used to say takbir at every raising and lowering, and the continuous practice after him was transmitted, but the practice has been abandoned in our time. End quote.
Source pages p. 527

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe from the commentator explaining the sunan (recommended acts) of prayer as per the Hanafi school. The main focus is on raising the hands (raf' al-yadayn) at the opening takbir. The commentator clarifies the legal nature of this act: although consistent practice might suggest obligation (wajib), the Hanafi position is that it is a sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah), not wajib. This is based on reports from Abu Hanifah that leaving it is permissible and that doing it is better. The passage discusses differing views on whether leaving it incurs sin: if one habitually leaves it, there is sin (due to disrespect); if occasional, no sin. The commentator cites Fath al-Qadir to harmonize these views. The act is categorized as sunnah al-huda (guidance sunnah) rather than sunnah al-zawa'id (additional sunnah). The commentator then moves to other sunan: spreading fingers (nashr al-asabi') in a moderate manner, the imam saying takbir loudly to alert the congregation, and reciting thana, ta'awwudh, tasmiyyah, and amin softly. Finally, the passage addresses the placement of hands during prayer: the Hanafi position is to place the right hand on the left below the navel. The commentator provides evidence from Sahih Muslim (the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr) and refutes the Shafi'i view (hands on chest) and Maliki view (hanging). The Hanafi proof includes a hadith stating that three practices are from the ways of the messengers, including placing the right on the left below the navel, though its chain is not fully authenticated. Nevertheless, the school relies on the established sunnah of placement and the absence of a definitive specification of location, thus maintaining the below-navel position.

Key Terms
وضع اليمين على اليسار تحت السرة (wad' al-yamin 'ala al-yasar tahta al-surah): Placing the right hand over the left hand below the navel during prayer.
إرسال (arsal): The practice of letting the hands hang straight down during prayer, without placing one hand over the other.
صحيح مسلم (Sahih Muslim): One of the six canonical hadith collections, compiled by Imam Muslim ibn al-Hajjaj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, where should the hands be placed during prayer (qiyam)?
A) On the chest above the navel.
B) Below the navel.
C) Hanging at the sides.
D) Clasped on the stomach.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school places the right hand on the left below the navel, based on the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr and the continuous practice of the Companions.

Hand Placement in Prayer: The Hanafi Position and Its Proof
Commentary on sunan of standing: finger spreading and hand placement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hand placement for men and women, and analyze the textual evidence supporting it.

Core Idea
Right hand on left under navel for men, on chest for women — from sunnah and custom.

The placement of hands in prayer is a distinctive feature of the Hanafi school. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its basis in the hadith of Wail ibn Hujr, and how Hanafi scholars refute opposing views.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunan of standing
The passage lists two sunan during qiyam: spreading the fingers naturally and placing the right hand on the left. Distinguish between sunan al-huda (more emphatic) and sunan al-zawa'id.
Finger spreading is a sunnah zawa'id; hand placement is sunnah muakkadah.
2
State the Hanafi ruling for men
The relied-upon position is to place the right hand on the left under the navel. This is derived from the hadith of Wail ibn Hujr in Sahih Muslim and the custom of standing in respect.
3
State the Hanafi ruling for women
Women place their hands on their chest for greater modesty. The same hadith applies, but the location is adjusted based on custom and concealment.
4
Examine the primary dalil
The hadith 'Then the Prophet placed his right hand on his left' establishes the action. The exact location (under navel) is inferred from customary practice (al-ma'hood).
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) and its meaning is zanni al-dalalah.
5
Analyze the response to opposing schools
The Shafi'i hadith (on chest) does not specify a unique location; it can be reconciled by custom. The Maliki irsal (hanging) is rejected because the hadith clearly shows placing.
The thamarah al-khilaf is that a Hanafi praying behind a Shafi'i imam has a valid prayer either way.

Source Text

كتاب الصلاة - باب صفة الصلاة ونشر أصابعه وجهر الإمام بالتكبير والثناء والتعوّذ والتسمية والتأمين سراً ووضع يمينه مؤكدة، والقائل بعدمه بناه على أنه من سنن الزوائد بمنزلة المستحق، وقد قال في الذخيرة : وقد روي عن أبي حنيفة ما يدل على عدم الإثم فإنه قال : إن ترك رفع اليدين جاز وإن رفع فهو أفضل ا هـ . وبهذا اندفع ما في الفتح القدير كما لا يخفى قوله : (ونشر أصابعه) وكيفيته أن لا يضم كل الضم ولا يفرج كل التفريج بل يتركها على حالها منشورة. كذا ذكره الشارح والظاهر أن المراد بالنشر عدم الطي بمعنى أنه يسن أن يرفعهما منصوبتين لا مضمومتين حتى تكون الأصابع مع الكف مستقبلة للقبلة ومن السنن أن لا يطأطيء رأسه عند التكبير كما في المبسوط وهو بدعة قوله : (وجهر الإمام بالتكبير) لحاجته إلى الإعلام بالدخول والانتقال . قيد بالإمام لأن المأموم والمنفرد لا يسن لهما الجهر به لأن الأصل في الذكر الإخفاء ولا حاجة لهما إلى الجهر قوله : (والثناء والتعوّذ والتسمية والتأمين سراً) للنقل المستفيض على ما يأتي بيانه. وقول، سراً» راجع إلى الأربعة قوله : (ووضع يمينه على يساره تحت سرته لما في صحيح مسلم عن وائل بن حجر أنه قال : ثم وضع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يده اليمنى على اليسرى. فانتفى به قول مالك بالإرسال وعند الشافعي محله ما فوق السرة تحت الصدر واستدل له النووي بما في صحيح ابن خزيمة عن وائل بن حجر قال : صليت مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فوضع يده اليمنى على يده اليسرى على صدره ولا يخفى أنه لا يطابق المدعي. واستدل مشايخنا بما عن النبي هو أنه قال : ثلاث من سنن المرسلين وذكر من جملتها وضع اليمين على الشمال تحت السرة لكن المخرجين لم يعرفوا فيه مرفوعاً وموقوفاً تحت السرة. ويمكن أن يقال في توجيه المذهب : إن الثابت من السنة وضع اليمين على الشمال ولم يثبت حديث يوجب تعيين المحل الذي يكون فيه الوضع من البدن إلا حديث وائل المذكور، وهو مع كونه واقعة حال لا عموم لها يحتمل أن يكون لبيان الجواز فيحال في ذلك كما قاله في فتح القدير على المعهود من وضعها حال قصد التعظيم في القيام، والمعهود في الشاهد منه أن يكون ذلك تحت السرة فقلنا به في هذه الحالة في حق الرجل بخلاف المرأة فإنها تضع على صدرها لأنه أستر لها فيكون في حقها أولى.

 كتاب الصلاة - باب صفة الصلاة ٥٢٩ على يساره تحت سرته وتكبير الركوع والرفع منه وتسبيحه ثلاثاً وأخذ ركبتيه بيديه وتفريج أصابعه وتكبير السجود وتسبيحه ثلاثاً ووضع يديه وركبتيه وافتراش رجله اليسرى ونصب منه كان أولى لأن التكبير عند الرفع منه سنة وكذا الرفع نفسه سنة ا هـ. استفادة الحكمين من قوله والرفع منه محل نظر لأنه إن قرىء بالرفع أفاد سنية أصل الرفع، وإن قرئ بالجر أفاد سنية التكبير عند الرفع، وأما استفادتهما منه فلا . وروي عن أبي حنيفة أن الرفع منه فرض وجه الظاهر أن المقصود الانتقال وهو يتحقق بدونه بأن يسجد على وسادة ثم تنزع ويسجد على الأرض ثانياً . قال الشارح ولكن لا يتصوّر هذا إلا على قول من المتبادر من مثل هذا التركيب في كلام العلماء التنبيه على أمر آخر غير ما ذكر قبله وإلا لقال : لأن الرفع نفسه والتكبير عنده سنتان ولو سلم فلا مانع من إرادة ذلك بناء على صحة قراءته بالوجهين ففي كل وجه يراد معناه فيستفاد الحكمان من هذا اللفظ الواحد في وقتين وقد وقع نظيره في القرآن الكريم كما في قوله تعالى ﴿إن الذين تدعون من دون الله عباد أمثالكم﴾ [الأعراف : ١٩٤] قرئ البحر الرائق/ ج ١/ م ٣٤
Book of Prayer - Chapter on Description of Prayer: And spreading his fingers, and the imam voicing the takbir, and the thana', ta'awwudh, tasmiyah, and amin silently, and placing his right hand on his left under his navel... and the one who negates it based it on it being from the sunan al-zawa'id...
Source pages p. 528

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq listing the sunan actions of prayer. The commentator, al-Zayla'i, explains each item with evidence and disputes. He begins with 'spreading his fingers'—meaning the fingers should be neither fully closed nor fully spread but natural. The imam should say the opening takbir aloud to inform others, while the follower and individual pray silently for thana', ta'awwudh, tasmiyah, and amin. The most extensive discussion is on placing the right hand on the left under the navel. The Hanafi position is supported by a hadith from Wail ibn Hujr in Sahih Muslim. The commentator refutes the Maliki view of letting arms hang and the Shafi'i view of placing hands on the chest, showing the Hanafi evidence is stronger. For women, the hands are placed on the chest for modesty. The passage then covers takbir for ruku', raising from ruku' (with grammatical debate on whether 'al-raf' is nominative or genitive), tasbih, holding the knees, and then similar for sujud. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether raising from ruku' is wajib or sunnah, with a narration from Abu Hanifa implying wujub. The commentator discusses the seated postures (iftrash, nusb, qawma, jalsah) and concludes that the relied-upon position is that they are obligatory based on the evidence.

Key Terms
سنن الزوائد (sunan al-zawa'id): Extra sunan that are recommended but leaving them does not incur sin
المعهود (al-ma'hood): Customary practice; the commonly known manner of doing something

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, where should a man place his hands when standing in prayer?
A) On his chest
B) Under his navel
C) At his sides
D) Above his navel

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position on hand placement is based on the affirmed sunnah of placing right on left, with the exact location under navel for men and on chest for women determined by customary practice.

Takbir and Silent Recitations: The Imam’s Role and Individual Practice
Commentary on the sunan of takbir and silent recitations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the imam's audible takbir and the silent recitations, and explain the reasoning for each.

Core Idea
The imam says takbir aloud to inform; all other adhkar in prayer are silent.

This passage explains the sunnah of the imam voicing the opening takbir and the silent recitation of thana', ta'awwudh, tasmiyah, and amin. The key principle is that the origin of dhikr is to be hidden, unless there is a need to inform others.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunan related to takbir and recitations
The imam says the opening takbir aloud; the follower and individual pray silently for thana', ta'awwudh, tasmiyah, and amin. These are all sunnah.
The imam's takbir is for informing the congregation of transitions.
2
Understand the principle: al-aslu fi al-dhikri al-ikhfa
The default in remembrance is secrecy. The imam's takbir is an exception because of the need to inform.
3
List the four silent recitations
Thana' (Subhanaka), ta'awwudh (A'udhu billah), tasmiyah (Bismillah), and amin are recited silently by all.
The word 'silently' (sirran) applies to all four.
4
Apply the ruling to different roles
Imam: aloud for takbir only; follower: silent; individual: silent.

منه أي من الركوع وهو بالرفع عطفاً على التكبير ولا يجوز جره لأنه لا يكبر عند الرفع من الركوع وإنما يأتي بالتسميع، وقد قدمنا أن مقتضى الدليل الوجوب لا السنية، وهو رواية عن أبي حنيفة. قوله : وتسبيحه ثلاثاً) أي تسبيح الركوع . قوله : (وأخذ ركبتيه بيديه وتفريج أصابعه الحديث أنس : إذا ركعت فضع يديك على ركبتيك وفرج بين أصابعك . قوله : (وتكبير السجود لما روينا قال الشارح: ولو قال وتكبير السجود والرفع منه كان أولى لأن التكبير عند الرفع منه سنة وكذا الرفع نفسه سنة ا هـ. استفادة الحكمين من قوله والرفع منه محل نظر لأنه إن قرىء بالرفع أفاد سنية أصل الرفع، وإن قرئ بالجر أفاد سنية التكبير عند الرفع، وأما استفادتهما منه فلا . وروي عن أبي حنيفة أن الرفع منه فرض وجه الظاهر أن المقصود الانتقال وهو يتحقق بدونه بأن يسجد على وسادة ثم تنزع ويسجد على الأرض ثانياً . قال الشارح ولكن لا يتصوّر هذا إلا على قول من لا يشترط الرفع حتى يكون أقرب إلى الجلوس. قوله : ( وتسبيحه ثلاثاً) لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام إذا سجد أحدكم فليقل سبحان ربي الأعلى ثلاثاً». قوله: (ووضع يديه وركبتيه) يعني حالة السجود وسيأتي الكلام عليه قوله : وافتراش رجله اليسرى ونصب اليمني والقومة والجلسة) تقدم أن مقتضى الدليل وجوبهما. وفي قوله «القومة» نوع إشكال وبالجملة فالأنسب الجر لما قلنا ولئلا يلزم التكرار المنافي للاختصار في قوله «والقومة والجلسة» ودفعه بما سيأتي أن المراد بالقومة القومة من السجود بعيد ومما يؤيد الجر قوله بعده وتسبيحه ثلاثاً» إذ لو كان الرفع مرفوعاً لكان الأولى تقديم قوله وتسبيحه على قوله والرفع منه كما لا يخفى. قوله : (لكن استفادة الحكمين الخ) قد يمنع إرادة الشارح الزيلعي استفادة الحكمين مما ذكر يدل عليه اقتصاره في التعليل على قوله «لأن التكبير عند الرفع منه سنة ثم استئنافه ذكر الرفع بقوله وكذا الرفع نفسه إذ المتبادر من مثل هذا التركيب في كلام العلماء التنبيه على أمر آخر غير ما ذكر قبله وإلا لقال : لأن الرفع نفسه والتكبير عنده سنتان ولو سلم فلا مانع من إرادة ذلك بناء على صحة قراءته بالوجهين ففي كل وجه يراد معناه فيستفاد الحكمان من هذا اللفظ الواحد في وقتين وقد وقع نظيره في القرآن الكريم كما في قوله تعالى ﴿إن الذين تدعون من دون الله عباد أمثالكم﴾ [الأعراف : ١٩٤] قرئ البحر الرائق/ ج ١/ م ٣٤
Book of Prayer - Chapter on Description of Prayer: And spreading his fingers, and the imam voicing the takbir, and the thana', ta'awwudh, tasmiyah, and amin silently, and placing his right hand on his left under his navel... and the one who negates it based it on it being from the sunan al-zawa'id...
Source pages p. 528

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq listing the sunan actions of prayer. The commentator, al-Zayla'i, explains each item with evidence and disputes. He begins with 'spreading his fingers'—meaning the fingers should be neither fully closed nor fully spread but natural. The imam should say the opening takbir aloud to inform others, while the follower and individual pray silently for thana', ta'awwudh, tasmiyah, and amin. The most extensive discussion is on placing the right hand on the left under the navel. The Hanafi position is supported by a hadith from Wail ibn Hujr in Sahih Muslim. The commentator refutes the Maliki view of letting arms hang and the Shafi'i view of placing hands on the chest, showing the Hanafi evidence is stronger. For women, the hands are placed on the chest for modesty. The passage then covers takbir for ruku', raising from ruku' (with grammatical debate on whether 'al-raf' is nominative or genitive), tasbih, holding the knees, and then similar for sujud. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether raising from ruku' is wajib or sunnah, with a narration from Abu Hanifa implying wujub. The commentator discusses the seated postures (iftrash, nusb, qawma, jalsah) and concludes that the relied-upon position is that they are obligatory based on the evidence.

Key Terms
الإخفاء (al-ikhfa): Concealment; the default principle for dhikr in prayer except where need demands audibility

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The imam's takbir is the only audible dhikr; all other adhkar in standing are silent for everyone.

Postures in Ruku’ and Sujud: Sunan, Wajibat, and Disputes
Commentary on the sunan of ruku' and sujud, with intra-Hanafi disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the sunan of ruku' and sujud, distinguish the intra-Hanafi dispute on raising from ruku', and apply the conditions of qawma and jalsah.

Core Idea
Raising from ruku' is sunnah muakkadah, but a narration from Abu Hanifa considers it wajib.

This passage details the sunan actions in bowing and prostration: takbir, tasbih, hand placement, and the sitting postures between prostrations. A key dispute within the Hanafi school concerns whether raising from ruku' is wajib or sunnah.

Guided Path
1
List the sunan for ruku'
Takbir for bowing (aloud for imam), raising from ruku' (with tasmi'), tasbih three times, placing hands on knees with fingers spread.
The takbir for ruku' is sunnah, like the opening takbir.
2
Identify the disputed ruling: raising from ruku'
The passage notes that the evidence (dalil) indicates wujub, and there is a narration from Abu Hanifa that it is fard. However, the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view is that it is sunnah.
The grammatical discussion (raf' vs. jar) in the matn is about whether 'al-raf' is part of the listed sunan or not.
3
List the sunan for sujud
Takbir for sujud, tasbih three times, placing hands and knees on the ground, and sitting postures (qawma, jalsah, iftirash).
Qawma (sitting between sujud) and jalsah (sitting for tashahhud) are considered wajib by many Hanafis, though the text says 'sunna'.
4
Understand the disagreement on qawma and jalsah
The commentary states that the evidence (dalil) indicates they are wajib. The matn lists them among sunan, but the commentator leans toward wujub.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute: the matn says sunnah, but the commentator suggests wajib.

كتاب الصلاة - باب صفة الصلاة ونشر أصابعه وجهر الإمام بالتكبير والثناء والتعوّذ والتسمية والتأمين سراً ووضع يمينه مؤكدة، والقائل بعدمه بناه على أنه من سنن الزوائد بمنزلة المستحق، وقد قال في الذخيرة : وقد روي عن أبي حنيفة ما يدل على عدم الإثم فإنه قال : إن ترك رفع اليدين جاز وإن رفع فهو أفضل ا هـ . وبهذا اندفع ما في الفتح القدير كما لا يخفى قوله : (ونشر أصابعه) وكيفيته أن لا يضم كل الضم ولا يفرج كل التفريج بل يتركها على حالها منشورة. كذا ذكره الشارح والظاهر أن المراد بالنشر عدم الطي بمعنى أنه يسن أن يرفعهما منصوبتين لا مضمومتين حتى تكون الأصابع مع الكف مستقبلة للقبلة ومن السنن أن لا يطأطيء رأسه عند التكبير كما في المبسوط وهو بدعة قوله : (وجهر الإمام بالتكبير) لحاجته إلى الإعلام بالدخول والانتقال . قيد بالإمام لأن المأموم والمنفرد لا يسن لهما الجهر به لأن الأصل في الذكر الإخفاء ولا حاجة لهما إلى الجهر قوله : (والثناء والتعوّذ والتسمية والتأمين سراً) للنقل المستفيض على ما يأتي بيانه. وقول، سراً» راجع إلى الأربعة قوله : (ووضع يمينه على يساره تحت سرته لما في صحيح مسلم عن وائل بن حجر أنه قال : ثم وضع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يده اليمنى على اليسرى. فانتفى به قول مالك بالإرسال وعند الشافعي محله ما فوق السرة تحت الصدر واستدل له النووي بما في صحيح ابن خزيمة عن وائل بن حجر قال : صليت مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فوضع يده اليمنى على يده اليسرى على صدره ولا يخفى أنه لا يطابق المدعي. واستدل مشايخنا بما عن النبي هو أنه قال : ثلاث من سنن المرسلين وذكر من جملتها وضع اليمين على الشمال تحت السرة لكن المخرجين لم يعرفوا فيه مرفوعاً وموقوفاً تحت السرة. ويمكن أن يقال في توجيه المذهب : إن الثابت من السنة وضع اليمين على الشمال ولم يثبت حديث يوجب تعيين المحل الذي يكون فيه الوضع من البدن إلا حديث وائل المذكور، وهو مع كونه واقعة حال لا عموم لها يحتمل أن يكون لبيان الجواز فيحال في ذلك كما قاله في فتح القدير على المعهود من وضعها حال قصد التعظيم في القيام، والمعهود في الشاهد منه أن يكون ذلك تحت السرة فقلنا به في هذه الحالة في حق الرجل بخلاف المرأة فإنها تضع على صدرها لأنه أستر لها فيكون في حقها أولى.

Key Terms
القومة (al-qawma): The brief sitting between prostrations (sitting up after sujud before the next)
الافتراش (al-iftirash): Sitting on the left foot with the right foot upright (in tashahhud)
الرفع منه (al-raf' minhu): Raising from ruku'; the act of standing up after bowing

Hand Placement in Prayer: Custom as a Source of Ruling
Ruling on hand placement based on customary practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hand placement for men and women in prayer and explain the role of customary practice (al-ma'hood) in deriving this ruling.

Core Idea
Hand placement in prayer is sunnah, not fard, based on customary practice rather than a definitive command.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the commentator explains that the reported incident of the Prophet placing his hands under his navel is a specific occurrence (waqi'a), not a general rule. Because it lacks generality, the ruling is based on what is customary (al-ma'hood) for glorification in standing. For men, this custom places the hands under the navel; for women, on the chest for modesty. This lesson unpacks how the Hanafi school uses custom as a source of law in the absence of explicit texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is hand placement during standing (qiyam) in prayer. The ruling is sunnah, not fard or wajib.
2
Recognize the nature of the proof
The proof is a specific incident (waqi'a) without generality. The commentator argues it indicates permissibility (jawaz), not obligation.
3
Understand reliance on customary practice
Because the incident is specific, the ruling is referred to customary practice (al-ma'hood) of placing hands in a manner of glorification while standing.
This shows the Hanafi use of 'urf (custom) as a source when explicit texts are lacking.
4
Distinguish between men and women
For men, the custom places hands under the navel. For women, on the chest because it is more concealing (astar).
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school places hands on the chest or above the navel for both genders, based on a different narration. The Hanafi position relies on custom.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على يساره تحت سرته وهو مع كونه واقعة حال لا عموم لها يحتمل أن يكون لبيان الجواز فيحال في ذلك كما قاله في فتح القدير على المعهود من وضعها حال قصد التعظيم في القيام، والمعهود في الشاهد منه أن يكون ذلك تحت السرة فقلنا به في هذه الحالة في حق الرجل بخلاف المرأة فإنها تضع على صدرها لأنه أستر لها فيكون في حقها أولى.
On his left side under his navel... And it, despite being a specific occurrence with no generality, may be to indicate permissibility, so it is referred in that regard, as stated in Fath al-Qadir, to the customary practice of placing them while intending glorification in standing. The customary practice in what is witnessed is that this is under the navel, so we adopted it in this case for the man, unlike the woman, for she places them on her chest because it is more concealing for her, so it is more appropriate in her case.
Source pages p. 529

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning hand placement during standing in prayer. The commentator explains that the narration about placing the right hand over the left under the navel is a specific incident, but since it lacks generality, it indicates permissibility rather than obligation. The actual practice is based on customary tradition (al-ma'hood) of placing hands under the navel for men, as a sign of respect. For women, they place their hands on their chest because it is more modest and concealing. This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
واقعة (waqi'a): A specific incident or event, not a general ruling.
المعهود (al-ma'hood): Customary practice that is well-known and accepted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Where should a woman place her hands during prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) On her chest
B) Under her navel
C) Over her navel
D) At her sides

Key Takeaway
Hand placement in prayer is sunnah for men (under navel) and women (on chest), derived from customary practice, not from a definitive command.

The Sunnah Status of Raising from Ruku'
Intra-Hanafi dispute on raising from ruku'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the ruling of raising from ruku' and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute, identifying the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Raising from ruku' is sunnah; its omission requires sajdah sahw, not repetition.

In this passage, the author of Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the ruling of raising from ruku' (al-raf'). While the general evidence might suggest obligation, the established Hanafi position is that it is sunnah, though a riwayah from Abu Hanifa considered it wajib. This lesson unpacks the evidence, the dispute, and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act in question is raising from ruku' (al-raf' min al-ruku'). The text first mentions it as a coordinate to takbir, indicating it is an action performed in prayer.
2
Examine the evidence suggesting obligation
The author states that the requirement of the evidence (dalil) is obligation, and that this is a riwayah from Abu Hanifa himself. The evidence is the hadith of takbir 'at every raising and lowering', implying the raising itself is part of the prayer sequence.
3
Understand the majority Hanafi position
Despite that riwayah, the relied-upon view is sunnah. The author indicates that 'the evidence suggests obligation' but does not adopt it. This is a typical Hanafi process: a strong dalil may be overridden by other considerations (practice, other hadith).
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if sunnah, omitting it intentionally makes the prayer valid but requires sajdah sahw; if wajib, omitting it would invalidate the prayer. The mufta bihi is sunnah, so the prayer remains valid.
5
Note the Shafi'i position
The Shafi'i school considers raising from ruku' a rukn (pillar), making it fard. This illustrates a cross-madhhab difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وتكبير (الركوع لما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان يكبر عند كل رفع وخفض قوله : (والرفع منه أي من الركوع وهو بالرفع عطفاً على التكبير ولا يجوز جره لأنه لا يكبر عند الرفع من الركوع وإنما يأتي بالتسميع، وقد قدمنا أن مقتضى الدليل الوجوب لا السنية، وهو رواية عن أبي حنيفة. قوله : وتسبيحه ثلاثاً) أي تسبيح الركوع . قوله : (وأخذ ركبتيه بيديه وتفريج أصابعه الحديث أنس : إذا ركعت فضع يديك على ركبتيك وفرج بين أصابعك . قوله : (وتكبير السجود وتسبيحه ثلاثاً ووضع يديه وركبتيه وافتراش رجله اليسرى ونصب اليمني والقومة والجلسة) تقدم أن مقتضى الدليل وجوبهما. وفي قوله «القومة» نوع إشكال وبالجملة فالأنسب الجر لما قلنا ولئلا يلزم التكرار المنافي للاختصار في قوله «والقومة والجلسة» ودفعه بما سيأتي أن المراد بالقومة القومة من السجود بعيد ومما يؤيد الجر قوله بعده وتسبيحه ثلاثاً» إذ لو كان الرفع مرفوعاً لكان الأولى تقديم قوله وتسبيحه على قوله والرفع منه كما لا يخفى. قوله : (لكن استفادة الحكمين الخ) قد يمنع إرادة الشارح الزيلعي استفادة الحكمين مما ذكر يدل عليه اقتصاره في التعليل على قوله «لأن التكبير عند الرفع منه سنة ثم استئنافه ذكر الرفع بقوله وكذا الرفع نفسه إذ المتبادر من مثل هذا التركيب في كلام العلماء التنبيه على أمر آخر غير ما ذكر قبله وإلا لقال : لأن الرفع نفسه والتكبير عنده سنتان ولو سلم فلا مانع من إرادة ذلك بناء على صحة قراءته بالوجهين ففي كل وجه يراد معناه فيستفاد الحكمان من هذا اللفظ الواحد في وقتين وقد وقع نظيره في القرآن الكريم كما في قوله تعالى إن الذين تدعون من دون الله عباد أمثالكم ﴾ [الأعراف : ١٩٤] قرئ
His statement: (Takbir of ruku') because it is narrated that he (peace be upon him) used to say takbir at every raising and lowering. His statement: (and the raising from it) meaning from ruku' and it is in the nominative (raf') as a coordinate to 'takbir', and it is not allowed to be in the genitive (jarr) because he does not say takbir at the raising from ruku' but rather says 'sami'a Allahu liman hamidah'. And we have already stated that the requirement of the evidence is obligation not sunnah, and that is a transmission from Abu Hanifa. His statement: (and his glorification three times) meaning glorification of ruku'. His statement: (and taking his knees with his hands and spreading his fingers) the hadith of Anas: 'When you bow, place your hands on your knees and spread your fingers.' His statement: (and takbir of sujud and his glorification three times and placing his hands and knees and spreading his left foot and erecting the right, and the rising and the sitting) we have previously stated that the requirement of the evidence is their obligation. And in his statement 'al-qawmah' there is a type of difficulty. And in short, the genitive is more appropriate for what we said, so that unnecessary repetition contrary to brevity does not occur in his statement 'al-qawma wal-jalsah'. And its refutation will come later that what is meant by 'al-qawmah' is the rising from sujud is far-fetched. And what supports the genitive is his statement after it 'and his glorification three times' because if 'the raising' were in the nominative, it would have been more appropriate to present his statement 'and his glorification' before his statement 'and the raising from it', as is not hidden. His statement: (But the derivation of both rulings etc.) He may prevent the intent of the author al-Zayla'i of deriving both rulings from what was mentioned, as indicated by his restriction in the reasoning on his statement 'because the takbir at the raising from it is sunnah' then his resuming mention of the raising by his statement 'and likewise the raising itself', since the evident from such a construction in the speech of scholars is alerting to another matter not mentioned before it. Otherwise he would have said: 'because the raising itself and the takbir are both sunnah.' And even if it is granted, there is no obstacle to intending that based on the validity of its reading in two ways, so in each way its meaning is intended, and both rulings are derived from this single wording at two times. And an example of it has occurred in the Noble Quran, as in His saying: 'Indeed, those you invoke besides Allah are servants like you' [Al-A'raf 194] - it was recited.
Source pages p. 529

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the sunan actions during ruku' and sujud. It begins with the takbir for ruku' based on the prophetic practice of saying takbir at each movement. The author clarifies that the phrase 'and the raising from it' should be read in the nominative, referring to the act of raising itself, not the takbir at that moment, because the takbir is said before raising. The evidence suggests obligation of the raising, but it is a transmission from Abu Hanifa that it is wajib; the relied-upon view is that it is sunnah. The practice of glorifying three times in ruku' and sujud is supported by hadith. The hadith of Anas instructs grabbing the knees and spreading fingers. For sujud, the actions include takbir, tasbih, hand placement, leg positions, and the rising (qawmah) and sitting (jalsah). There is a grammatical discussion about whether 'al-qawmah' refers to rising from ruku' or from sujud; the author argues that the genitive reading avoids repetition and is more consistent. The later comment addresses whether both the act of raising and the takbir at raising can be derived from the same phrase, and he gives the Quranic example of different readings producing different meanings.

Key Terms
الرفع (al-raf'): The act of rising from ruku' in prayer.
القومة (al-qawmah): The standing posture after rising from ruku'.
التسميع (al-tasmi'): Saying 'sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' when rising from ruku'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Raising from ruku' is sunnah in the Hanafi school, and its omission requires sajdah sahw, not repetition of the prayer.

Grammatical Analysis of Qawmah and Derivation of Rulings
Grammatical and usuli analysis of qawmah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the grammatical debate over the irab of 'al-qawmah' and how different readings can derive multiple rulings from one phrase.

Core Idea
The irab of 'qawmah' determines which sunnah is derived: if nominative, it affirms the raising; if genitive, it implies the takbir at raising.

This passage contains a detailed grammatical analysis of the word 'al-qawmah' in the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The author argues that the genitive reading (jarr) is more appropriate to avoid repetition and to derive the proper sunan. He also addresses a subtle point about deriving both the act of raising and the takbir from the same phrase, using a Quranic example to show how different qira'at yield different meanings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the textual problem
The matn lists actions: '...and the rising and the sitting' (wal-qawmati wal-jalsah). The author of the sharh notes a difficulty (ishkal) in the word 'al-qawmah'—whether it should be read in the nominative or genitive.
2
Understand the two possible readings
If nominative (مرفوع), it is a new topic, meaning the act of rising itself is a sunnah distinct from the takbir. If genitive (مجرور), it is a continuation of the list, referring to the rising after sujud.
The author prefers genitive to avoid repetition.
3
Examine the author's preference for jarr
The author argues that if it were nominative, it would repeat the same act (qawmah from ruku') already mentioned as 'al-raf' min al-ruku', causing redundancy. Hence, jarr is more appropriate, meaning it refers to the rising from sujud.
4
Analyze the derivation argument (istifada al-hukmayn)
Al-Zayla'i's commentary on Kanz might intend that from the phrase 'wal-qawmah' both the act of raising and the takbir at raising can be derived. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq critiques this, saying the construction normally indicates one new ruling, not two. But he concedes that if the phrase can be read in two ways (nominative and genitive), each reading can yield a different ruling.
5
Connect to Quranic precedent
The author cites Quran 7:194, which is recited in different qira'at, showing that multiple readings of the same verse can yield multiple meanings. This supports the principle that a single text can produce multiple rulings if read differently.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وتكبير (الركوع لما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان يكبر عند كل رفع وخفض قوله : (والرفع منه أي من الركوع وهو بالرفع عطفاً على التكبير ولا يجوز جره لأنه لا يكبر عند الرفع من الركوع وإنما يأتي بالتسميع، وقد قدمنا أن مقتضى الدليل الوجوب لا السنية، وهو رواية عن أبي حنيفة. قوله : وتسبيحه ثلاثاً) أي تسبيح الركوع . قوله : (وأخذ ركبتيه بيديه وتفريج أصابعه الحديث أنس : إذا ركعت فضع يديك على ركبتيك وفرج بين أصابعك . قوله : (وتكبير السجود وتسبيحه ثلاثاً ووضع يديه وركبتيه وافتراش رجله اليسرى ونصب اليمني والقومة والجلسة) تقدم أن مقتضى الدليل وجوبهما. وفي قوله «القومة» نوع إشكال وبالجملة فالأنسب الجر لما قلنا ولئلا يلزم التكرار المنافي للاختصار في قوله «والقومة والجلسة» ودفعه بما سيأتي أن المراد بالقومة القومة من السجود بعيد ومما يؤيد الجر قوله بعده وتسبيحه ثلاثاً» إذ لو كان الرفع مرفوعاً لكان الأولى تقديم قوله وتسبيحه على قوله والرفع منه كما لا يخفى. قوله : (لكن استفادة الحكمين الخ) قد يمنع إرادة الشارح الزيلعي استفادة الحكمين مما ذكر يدل عليه اقتصاره في التعليل على قوله «لأن التكبير عند الرفع منه سنة ثم استئنافه ذكر الرفع بقوله وكذا الرفع نفسه إذ المتبادر من مثل هذا التركيب في كلام العلماء التنبيه على أمر آخر غير ما ذكر قبله وإلا لقال : لأن الرفع نفسه والتكبير عنده سنتان ولو سلم فلا مانع من إرادة ذلك بناء على صحة قراءته بالوجهين ففي كل وجه يراد معناه فيستفاد الحكمان من هذا اللفظ الواحد في وقتين وقد وقع نظيره في القرآن الكريم كما في قوله تعالى إن الذين تدعون من دون الله عباد أمثالكم ﴾ [الأعراف : ١٩٤] قرئ

The Ruling of Salawat in Tashahhud: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on salawat in tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on salawat in tashahhud, explain the Shafi'i counter-argument, and evaluate the Hanafi response using the claimed ijma' and the interpretation of the Quranic command.

Core Idea
Salawat in tashahhud is sunnah in the Hanafi school, despite the Shafi'i view that it is fard.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a classic ikhtilaf: whether sending blessings on the Prophet in the final tashahhud is obligatory or merely sunnah. The Hanafi school maintains it is sunnah, relying on a claimed consensus and a once-in-a-lifetime interpretation of the Quranic command. Imam al-Shafi'i considers it fard, making prayer invalid if omitted. Understanding this dispute clarifies the Hanafi methodology of textual interpretation and the role of ijma'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
What exactly is the ikhtilaf? The act of salawat in the final tashahhud.
2
State the Hanafi position
Sunnah; the prayer is valid without it.
3
State the Shafi'i position
Fard; omission invalidates the prayer.
4
Analyze the Hanafi dalil
The claimed ijma' that salawat is not wajib, and the interpretation of Quran 33:56 as a once-in-a-lifetime obligation.
The command does not imply repetition in Hanafi usul.
5
Evaluate the debate
Note that some scholars contested the completeness of the ijma', and understand the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اليمني والقومة والجلسة والصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم والدعاء وآدابها نظره إلى موضع سجوده أي في حال القيام وأما في حالة الركوع فإلى ظهر قدميه، وفي سجوده إلى أرنبته، وفي قعوده إلى حجره، وعند التسليمة الأولى إلى منكبه الأيمن، وعند الثانية إلى منكبه الأيسر لأن المقصود الخشوع قوله : (وكظم فمه عند التثاؤب) والصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أو هو قول عامة السلف والخلف . وقال الشافعي : إنها فرض تبطل الصلاة بتركها وقد نسب قوم من الأعيان الإمام الشافعي في هذا إلى الشدوذ ومخالفة الإجماع منهم أبو جعفر الطحاوي وأبو بكر الرازي وأبو بكر بن المنذر والخطابي والبغوي وابن جرير الطبري وهذه عبارته : أجمع جميع المتقدمين والمتأخرين من علماء الأمة على أن الصلاة عليه غير واجبة في التشهد ولا سلف للشافعي في هذا القول ولا سنة هـ. فإن تم هذا كان الإجماع هو الدليل على السنية لكن تعقب غير واحد دعوى الإجماع بعدم التمام لأن عن بعض الصحابة وبعض التابعين ما يوافق قول الشافعي، وأما موجب الأمر في قوله تعالى صلوا عليه ﴾ [الأحزاب: ٥٦] فهو افتراضها في العمر مرة واحدة في الصلاة أو خارجها لأن الأمر لا يقتضي التكرار وسيأتي كيفيتها وأحكامها إن شاء الله تعالى . قوله : (والدعاء) أي لنفسه ولوالديه إن كانا مؤمنين ولجميع المؤمنين والمؤمنات لما في صحيح مسلم ثم يتخير من المسألة ما شاء، ولما رواه الترمذي وحسنه مرفوعاً عن أبي إمامة قيل يا رسول الله أي الدعاء أسمع ؟ قال : جوف الليل الأخير ودبر الصلوات المكتوبات» (١) بناء على أن المراد بدبرها ما قيل الفراغ منها كما ذكره بعضهم أي الوقت الذي يليه وقت الخروج منها لأن دبر كل شيء منه ومتصل به، وقد يراد بدبر الشيء وراءه وعقبه كما نصوا عليه أيضاً فيكون حينئذ المراد بدبرها الوقت الذي يلي وقت الخروج منها لكن عندنا السنة مقدمة على الدعاء الذي هو عقب الفراغ. قوله : (وآدابها نظره إلى موضع سجوده أي في حال القيام وأما في حالة الركوع فإلى ظهر قدميه، وفي سجوده إلى أرنبته، وفي قعوده إلى حجره، وعند التسليمة الأولى إلى منكبه الأيمن، وعند الثانية إلى منكبه الأيسر لأن المقصود الخشوع قوله : (وكظم فمه عند التثاؤب)
The right (leg?), and the rising and the sitting, and sending blessings upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) and supplication, and their etiquettes: his gaze is to his place of prostration, i.e., during standing; as for during bowing, to the back of his feet; during his prostration, to his nose; during his sitting, to his lap; at the first salutation, to his right shoulder; at the second, to his left shoulder, because the intent is humility. His statement: (and covering his mouth when yawning). And sending blessings upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) is the saying of the general public of the Salaf and Khalaf. Al-Shafi'i said: It is fard, and prayer becomes invalid by its omission. Some esteemed scholars attributed Imam al-Shafi'i in this to deviation and violation of consensus, among them Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi, Abu Bakr al-Razi, Abu Bakr ibn al-Mundhir, al-Khattabi, al-Baghawi, and Ibn Jarir al-Tabari. This is his expression: 'All the earlier and later scholars of the Ummah have consensus that sending blessings upon him is not obligatory in the tashahhud, nor is there any predecessor for al-Shafi'i in this statement, nor any Sunnah.' If this is established, then consensus is the proof for sunnah. However, more than one has contested the claim of consensus because some of the Companions and Followers hold a view agreeing with al-Shafi'i. As for the requirement of the command in His saying 'Send blessings upon him' [Al-Ahzab 56], it is to make it fard once in a lifetime, whether inside or outside prayer, because the command does not necessitate repetition. Supplication is for oneself, one's parents if they are believers, and all believing men and women, as in Sahih Muslim: 'Then let him choose whatever supplication he wishes.' Also the hadith reported by al-Tirmidhi and deemed good: 'Which supplication is most heard?' He said: 'The last part of the night and after the prescribed prayers.' This is based on the interpretation of 'after' as the time immediately following completion, as some mentioned, i.e., the time that follows the time of exit, because 'dubur' of something is from it and attached to it. It may also mean 'behind it and after it', as they also stated. So the meaning of 'dubur' is the time that follows the time of exit. However, in our school, the sunnah is presented before the supplication that is after completion.
Source pages p. 530

Commentary
This passage covers three main topics: salawat (sending blessings on the Prophet), du'a (supplication), and adab (proper behavior) in prayer. The opening lines specify where the worshipper should direct their gaze during different postures to achieve khushu' (humility). Then there is a detailed inter-madhhab dispute about salawat in tashahhud: the Hanafi school holds it is sunnah, while Imam al-Shafi'i considers it fard to the extent that prayer is invalid if omitted. The Hanafi evidence includes an alleged consensus (ijma') that it is not wajib, though some later scholars disputed the completeness of that consensus. The command in the Quran (33:56) is interpreted as making it fard once in a lifetime, not in every prayer. Regarding du'a, it is recommended (sunnah) after the tashahhud before the salam, supported by hadith about the most heard supplication. The adab section highlights looking at specific places during different postures, and covering the mouth when yawning.

Key Terms
الصلاة على النبي (al-salat 'ala al-nabi): Sending blessings upon the Prophet Muhammad (salawat), specifically in the tashahhud.
الإجماع (al-ijma'): Consensus of scholars, claimed as evidence that salawat is not wajib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on sending blessings upon the Prophet (salawat) in the final tashahhud?
A) Fard, omission invalidates prayer
B) Sunnah, prayer remains valid
C) Wajib, requires sajdah sahw if omitted
D) Makruh and should be avoided

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, salawat in tashahhud is sunnah, not fard; the prayer remains valid without it.

Supplication and Etiquettes of Prayer in the Hanafi School
Rulings on du'a and adab of prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the recommended place for du'a in prayer and describe the proper gaze directions during different postures.

Core Idea
Du'a after tashahhud is sunnah, and maintaining khushu' by proper gaze is emphasized.

The passage continues with instructions on du'a (supplication) after the tashahhud and the etiquettes (adab) of prayer, particularly where to direct the gaze during each posture. The du'a is recommended for oneself and fellow believers, supported by hadith. The gaze directions are detailed to cultivate khushu' (humility). This lesson focuses on these practical sunan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on du'a after tashahhud
Is it fard, wajib, or sunnah? The text indicates it is sunnah, supported by hadith.
2
Note the content of the du'a
It is general: for oneself, parents, and all believers.
3
Recall the time of du'a
After the tashahhud, before salam, is the most heard time.
Based on hadith about 'dubur al-salawat'.
4
List the gaze directions
During standing: to place of prostration; bowing: to back of feet; prostration: to nose; sitting: to lap; first salam: to right shoulder; second: to left shoulder.
5
Understand the purpose
All these are for achieving khushu' (humility).

اليمني والقومة والجلسة والصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم والدعاء وآدابها نظره إلى موضع سجوده أي في حال القيام وأما في حالة الركوع فإلى ظهر قدميه، وفي سجوده إلى أرنبته، وفي قعوده إلى حجره، وعند التسليمة الأولى إلى منكبه الأيمن، وعند الثانية إلى منكبه الأيسر لأن المقصود الخشوع قوله : (وكظم فمه عند التثاؤب) والصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أو هو قول عامة السلف والخلف . وقال الشافعي : إنها فرض تبطل الصلاة بتركها وقد نسب قوم من الأعيان الإمام الشافعي في هذا إلى الشدوذ ومخالفة الإجماع منهم أبو جعفر الطحاوي وأبو بكر الرازي وأبو بكر بن المنذر والخطابي والبغوي وابن جرير الطبري وهذه عبارته : أجمع جميع المتقدمين والمتأخرين من علماء الأمة على أن الصلاة عليه غير واجبة في التشهد ولا سلف للشافعي في هذا القول ولا سنة هـ. فإن تم هذا كان الإجماع هو الدليل على السنية لكن تعقب غير واحد دعوى الإجماع بعدم التمام لأن عن بعض الصحابة وبعض التابعين ما يوافق قول الشافعي، وأما موجب الأمر في قوله تعالى صلوا عليه ﴾ [الأحزاب: ٥٦] فهو افتراضها في العمر مرة واحدة في الصلاة أو خارجها لأن الأمر لا يقتضي التكرار وسيأتي كيفيتها وأحكامها إن شاء الله تعالى . قوله : (والدعاء) أي لنفسه ولوالديه إن كانا مؤمنين ولجميع المؤمنين والمؤمنات لما في صحيح مسلم ثم يتخير من المسألة ما شاء، ولما رواه الترمذي وحسنه مرفوعاً عن أبي إمامة قيل يا رسول الله أي الدعاء أسمع ؟ قال : جوف الليل الأخير ودبر الصلوات المكتوبات» (١) بناء على أن المراد بدبرها ما قيل الفراغ منها كما ذكره بعضهم أي الوقت الذي يليه وقت الخروج منها لأن دبر كل شيء منه ومتصل به، وقد يراد بدبر الشيء وراءه وعقبه كما نصوا عليه أيضاً فيكون حينئذ المراد بدبرها الوقت الذي يلي وقت الخروج منها لكن عندنا السنة مقدمة على الدعاء الذي هو عقب الفراغ. قوله : (وآدابها نظره إلى موضع سجوده أي في حال القيام وأما في حالة الركوع فإلى ظهر قدميه، وفي سجوده إلى أرنبته، وفي قعوده إلى حجره، وعند التسليمة الأولى إلى منكبه الأيمن، وعند الثانية إلى منكبه الأيسر لأن المقصود الخشوع قوله : (وكظم فمه عند التثاؤب)
The right (leg?), and the rising and the sitting, and sending blessings upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) and supplication, and their etiquettes: his gaze is to his place of prostration, i.e., during standing; as for during bowing, to the back of his feet; during his prostration, to his nose; during his sitting, to his lap; at the first salutation, to his right shoulder; at the second, to his left shoulder, because the intent is humility. His statement: (and covering his mouth when yawning). And sending blessings upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) is the saying of the general public of the Salaf and Khalaf. Al-Shafi'i said: It is fard, and prayer becomes invalid by its omission. Some esteemed scholars attributed Imam al-Shafi'i in this to deviation and violation of consensus, among them Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi, Abu Bakr al-Razi, Abu Bakr ibn al-Mundhir, al-Khattabi, al-Baghawi, and Ibn Jarir al-Tabari. This is his expression: 'All the earlier and later scholars of the Ummah have consensus that sending blessings upon him is not obligatory in the tashahhud, nor is there any predecessor for al-Shafi'i in this statement, nor any Sunnah.' If this is established, then consensus is the proof for sunnah. However, more than one has contested the claim of consensus because some of the Companions and Followers hold a view agreeing with al-Shafi'i. As for the requirement of the command in His saying 'Send blessings upon him' [Al-Ahzab 56], it is to make it fard once in a lifetime, whether inside or outside prayer, because the command does not necessitate repetition. Supplication is for oneself, one's parents if they are believers, and all believing men and women, as in Sahih Muslim: 'Then let him choose whatever supplication he wishes.' Also the hadith reported by al-Tirmidhi and deemed good: 'Which supplication is most heard?' He said: 'The last part of the night and after the prescribed prayers.' This is based on the interpretation of 'after' as the time immediately following completion, as some mentioned, i.e., the time that follows the time of exit, because 'dubur' of something is from it and attached to it. It may also mean 'behind it and after it', as they also stated. So the meaning of 'dubur' is the time that follows the time of exit. However, in our school, the sunnah is presented before the supplication that is after completion.
Source pages p. 530

Commentary
This passage covers three main topics: salawat (sending blessings on the Prophet), du'a (supplication), and adab (proper behavior) in prayer. The opening lines specify where the worshipper should direct their gaze during different postures to achieve khushu' (humility). Then there is a detailed inter-madhhab dispute about salawat in tashahhud: the Hanafi school holds it is sunnah, while Imam al-Shafi'i considers it fard to the extent that prayer is invalid if omitted. The Hanafi evidence includes an alleged consensus (ijma') that it is not wajib, though some later scholars disputed the completeness of that consensus. The command in the Quran (33:56) is interpreted as making it fard once in a lifetime, not in every prayer. Regarding du'a, it is recommended (sunnah) after the tashahhud before the salam, supported by hadith about the most heard supplication. The adab section highlights looking at specific places during different postures, and covering the mouth when yawning.

Key Terms
الدعاء (al-du'a): Supplication after the tashahhud, before salam, recommended for oneself and others.
الخشوع (al-khushu'): Humility and focus in prayer, achieved by looking at specific places.

Ruling on Salawat in Tashahhud: Sunnah not Fard
Inter-madhhab dispute on the ruling of salawat in tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that salawat in tashahhud is sunnah, evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Sending blessings on the Prophet in tashahhud is sunnah, not fard — a command once suffices for a lifetime.

In this lesson, we examine a classic madhhab dispute: is reciting salawat upon the Prophet ﷺ in the tashahhud obligatory or recommended? The Hanafi school holds it is sunnah; Imam al-Shafi'i held it is fard. The commentator in Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents the Hanafi proof based on consensus and the nature of the Qur'anic command, while acknowledging the dispute. Your task is to understand the evidence on both sides and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
What exactly does the Hanafi school hold regarding salawat in tashahhud?
It is sunnah, not fard.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Which school objects and on what grounds?
Imam al-Shafi'i holds it is fard.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
What is their primary dalil from the Qur'an?
The verse 'صلوا عليه' (al-Ahzab 56) is interpreted as obligatory in every prayer.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school rebut this proof?
The command does not imply repetition; it can be fulfilled once in a lifetime.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference in rulings?
Hanafi: prayer valid without salawat; Shafi'i: invalid if omitted deliberately.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أو هو قول عامة السلف والخلف . وقال الشافعي : إنها فرض تبطل الصلاة بتركها وقد نسب قوم من الأعيان الإمام الشافعي في هذا إلى الشدوذ ومخالفة الإجماع منهم أبو جعفر الطحاوي وأبو بكر الرازي وأبو بكر بن المنذر والخطابي والبغوي وابن جرير الطبري وهذه عبارته : أجمع جميع المتقدمين والمتأخرين من علماء الأمة على أن الصلاة عليه غير واجبة في التشهد ولا سلف للشافعي في هذا القول ولا سنة هـ. فإن تم هذا كان الإجماع هو الدليل على السنية لكن تعقب غير واحد دعوى الإجماع بعدم التمام لأن عن بعض الصحابة وبعض التابعين ما يوافق قول الشافعي، وأما موجب الأمر في قوله تعالى صلوا عليه ﴾ [الأحزاب: ٥٦] فهو افتراضها في العمر مرة واحدة في الصلاة أو خارجها لأن الأمر لا يقتضي التكرار وسيأتي كيفيتها وأحكامها إن شاء الله تعالى .
His statement: (and the salutation upon the Prophet, peace be upon him) or it is the saying of the general predecessors and successors. And al-Shafi'i said: it is an obligation, the prayer is invalidated by leaving it. And some notable people have attributed al-Shafi'i in this to deviance and opposition to consensus, among them Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi, Abu Bakr al-Razi, Abu Bakr ibn al-Mundhir, al-Khattabi, al-Baghawi, and Ibn Jarir al-Tabari. And this is his expression: 'All the early and later scholars of the Ummah have agreed that salutation upon him is not obligatory in the tashahhud, and al-Shafi'i has no predecessor in this saying, nor any sunnah.' If this is established, then consensus is the proof for its being sunnah, but more than one person has contested the claim of consensus by saying it is not complete because some Companions and some Successors hold something that agrees with al-Shafi'i's saying. As for the implication of the command in His statement, 'Send blessings upon him' (al-Ahzab 56), it means obligation once in a lifetime, whether in prayer or outside it, because the command does not necessitate repetition. And its manner and rulings will come, God willing.
Source pages p. 530

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about the ruling of reciting salawat (blessings) upon the Prophet ﷺ in the tashahhud of prayer. The Hanafi position, stated by the author of the matn and elaborated by the commentator, is that it is sunnah (recommended) and not fard (obligatory). The opposing view is attributed to Imam al-Shafi'i, who held it is fard such that deliberately omitting it invalidates the prayer. The commentator notes that many leading scholars accused al-Shafi'i of deviating from the consensus of the Ummah, and then quotes a strong assertion of consensus from Ibn Jarir al-Tabari that salawat is not obligatory in tashahhud. However, the commentator also acknowledges that this claim of consensus is contested, as some early authorities (Companions and Successors) did hold a view similar to al-Shafi'i's. The commentator then addresses the primary proof of the opposing school: the Qur'anic command 'صلوا عليه' (send blessings upon him). He argues that this command, being absolute, obligates it only once in a lifetime (since commands do not imply repetition by themselves), and that once can be outside of prayer. Thus it does not prove obligation in every prayer. The Hanafi ruling remains that salawat in tashahhud is sunnah, and the prayer is valid without it, though it is a meritorious act.

Key Terms
الصلاة على النبي (al-salatu 'ala al-nabi): Verbally sending blessings upon the Prophet Muhammad, specifically in the tashahhud of prayer.
السنية (al-sunniyya): The quality of being sunnah (recommended), as opposed to fard (obligatory).
الإجماع (al-ijma'): Consensus of the scholars of the Ummah on a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is fard (obligatory) and omitting it invalidates the prayer.
B) It is sunnah (recommended) and the prayer is valid without it.
C) It is wajib and requires sajdah sahw if omitted.
D) It is makruh to recite it in the tashahhud.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school considers salawat in tashahhud as sunnah, and the prayer remains valid without it, contrary to the Shafi'i view.

Etiquettes of Prayer: Gaze, Yawning, Hands, Cough
Rulings on proper conduct during prayer including where to look and how to handle yawns

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four sunnah etiquettes of prayer related to gaze, yawning, hands, and cough, and explain why each is recommended.

Core Idea
Sunnah etiquettes enhance khushu; omitting them does not invalidate prayer but reduces perfection.

Prayer is an act of worship with both obligatory elements and recommended adornments. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq outlines four specific sunnah etiquettes that complete the prayer: where to direct the gaze during different postures, how to handle a yawn, the proper way to raise the hands for takbir, and the attitude toward coughing. These details are not arbitrary; they are rooted in hadith and the objective of khushu (humility and concentration). Mastering these minor rulings helps you pray with greater presence and avoids common misunderstandings about what breaks the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify each etiquette and its posture
Scan the Arabic text and list the four etiquettes: (1) gaze direction in standing, bowing, prostration, sitting, and taslim; (2) suppressing yawns; (3) removing hands from sleeves for takbir; (4) repelling coughs. Note the specific body part for each posture's gaze.
The purpose is khushu, so each gaze placement keeps the worshipper focused.
2
Classify the ruling level
Recognize that these are sunnah (recommended), not fard or wajib. The text does not use imperative verbs in a binding sense; the phrase 'وآدابها' (its etiquettes) indicates recommended conduct.
Omitting a sunnah reduces reward but the prayer remains valid.
3
Connect to proofs
Identify the hadith for yawning suppression (التثاؤب من الشيطان) and the reasoning for taking out hands (أقرب إلى التواضع). Note that covering the mouth with hand or sleeve is allowed if unable to suppress.
The proofs are both textual (hadith) and rational (humility).
4
Distinguish between invalidating and non-invalidating actions
Note that coughing is explicitly said not to be from the actions of prayer; therefore it does not invalidate unless deliberate without excuse. Yawning and gaze direction also do not invalidate because they are not prohibited actions.
This distinction is crucial: many students mistakenly think these actions break the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وآدابها نظره إلى موضع سجوده أي في حال القيام وأما في حالة الركوع فإلى ظهر قدميه، وفي سجوده إلى أرنبته، وفي قعوده إلى حجره، وعند التسليمة الأولى إلى منكبه الأيمن، وعند الثانية إلى منكبه الأيسر لأن المقصود الخشوع . قوله : (وكظم فمه عند التثاؤب) أي إمساك فمه والمراد به سده لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام التثاؤب في الصلاة من الشيطان فإذا تثاءب أحدكم فليكظم ما استطاع (۲) وفي الظهيرية : فإن لم يقدر غطاه بيده أو كمه للحديث. قوله : (وإخراج كفيه من كميه عند التكبير لأنه أقرب إلى التواضع وأبعد من التشبه بالجبابرة وأمكن من نشر الأصابع إلا لضرورة برد ونحوه . قوله: (ودفع السعال ما استطاع لأنه ليس من أفعال الصلاة ولهذا لو كان بغير عذر لا تفسد صلاته فيجتنبه ما أمكن.
His statement: (and its etiquettes: his gaze to the place of his prostration) i.e., while standing; as for the state of bowing, then to the back of his feet; in his prostration, to his nose; in his sitting, to his lap; at the first salutation, to his right shoulder; at the second, to his left shoulder, because the purpose is khushu. His statement: (and suppressing his mouth at yawning) i.e., closing his mouth; the meaning is blocking it because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'Yawning in prayer is from the devil; so if one of you yawns, let him suppress it as much as he can.' And in al-Zahiriyya: if he is unable, he covers it with his hand or sleeve, due to the hadith. His statement: (and taking out his hands from his sleeves at the takbir) because it is closer to humility and further from resembling the tyrants, and more effective for spreading the fingers, except for a necessity like cold and the like. His statement: (and repelling coughing as much as he can) because it is not from the actions of prayer, and therefore if it is without excuse, it does not invalidate his prayer, so he avoids it as much as possible.
Source pages p. 530

Commentary
This passage lists several sunnah etiquettes of prayer. First, the direction of the gaze: when standing, look at the place of prostration; when bowing, look at the feet; in prostration, at the nose (or the spot of prostration); in sitting, at the lap; during the first taslim, at the right shoulder; during the second, at the left shoulder. The purpose is khushu (humility and concentration). Second, suppressing a yawn: one should close the mouth and try to stop it, as yawning is from Shaytan. If unable, cover with the hand or sleeve. Third, taking the hands out of the sleeves when raising for takbir: this is more humble and avoids resembling arrogant people; it also allows spreading the fingers properly. However, if there is a necessity like extreme cold, it is permissible to keep hands inside. Fourth, suppressing coughing as much as possible, because coughing is not part of the prayer's actions; however, if it occurs, it does not invalidate the prayer unless done deliberately without excuse. These etiquettes are recommended and enhance the perfection of the prayer.

Key Terms
الخشوع (al-khushu'): Humility and concentration in prayer, which is the purpose of these etiquettes.
التثاؤب (al-tatha'ub): Yawning, considered from Shaytan; should be suppressed during prayer.
السعال (al-su'al): Coughing; not an action of prayer but does not invalidate if unintentional.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To the place of prostration
B) To his lap
C) To his right shoulder
D) To the back of his feet

Key Takeaway
Sunnah etiquettes of prayer, such as gaze direction, suppressing yawns, removing hands for takbir, and repelling coughs, enhance khushu but do not invalidate the prayer if omitted.
