Standing for Iqamah and Imam's Start: Hanafi Rulings and Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Rulings on when to stand for prayer and when the imam begins

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended time to stand for prayer and explain the Hanafi dispute on when the imam should begin.

Core Idea
Stand at 'hayya ala al-falah' is sunnah; imam starts at 'qad qamat' according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but Abu Yusuf prefers after iqamah.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses two practical aspects of congregational prayer: when the congregation should rise and when the imam should commence. Understanding these rulings helps avoid confusion in the mosque and recognizes a legitimate difference within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage covers two separate issues: (1) the recommended time to stand for prayer, and (2) the imam's starting time. Note the conditions attached to each.
The standing ruling applies generally, but has exceptions when the imam is also the mu'adhdhin.
2
State the recommended standing time
The text says standing at 'hayya ala al-falah' is commanded, so it is mustahab. Apply this to imam and followers, with the nuances about the imam's location.
The source uses 'أمر به' to indicate recommendation (sunnah), not obligation.
3
Map the intra-Hanafi dispute on imam's start
Identify the two positions: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say start at 'qad qamat'; Abu Yusuf says start after full iqamah.
Both are valid views within the school.
4
Analyze the reasoning behind each view
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad argue to avoid falsehood of the mu'adhdhin's report and that following most of the iqamah suffices. Abu Yusuf emphasizes the virtue of following the entire iqamah and assisting the mu'adhdhin.
The commentator notes that responding to iqamah is actually recommended, complicating the argument.
5
Determine the practical outcome and mufta bihi
The Zahiriyya states that delaying is not objectionable in all views. Thus both timings are permissible, but the primary position is to start at 'qad qamat'.
The mufta bihi likely follows Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but the flexibility is important for practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( والقيام حين قيل حي على الفلاح لأنه أمر به فيستحب المسارعة إليه. أطلقه فشمل الإمام والمأموم إن كان الإمام بقرب المحراب وإلا فيقوم كل صف ينتهي إليه الإمام الأظهر، وإن دخل من قدام وقفوا حين يقع بصرهم عليه. وهذا كله إذا كان المؤذن غير الإمام، فإن كان واحداً وأقام في المسجد فالقوم لا يقومون حتى يفرغ من إقامته. كذا في الظهيرية. قوله : (وشروع الإمام مذ قيل قد قامت الصلاة عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد وقال أبو يوسف : يشرع إذا فرغ من الإقامة محافظة على فضيلة متابعة المؤذن وإعانة للمؤذن على الشروع معه. ولهما أن المؤذن أمين وقد أخبر بقيام الصلاة فيشرع عنده صوناً لكلامه عن الكذب، وفيه مسارعة إلى المناجاة وقد تابع المؤذن في الأكثر فيقوم مقام الكل على أنهم قالوا المتابعة في الأذان دون الإقامة. كذا ذكره الشارح وفيه نظر لما نقلناه في باب الأذان أن إجابة الإقامة مستحبة . وفي الظهيرية : ولو أخر حتى يفرغ المؤذن من الإقامة لا بأس به في قولهم جميعاً والله أعلم .
His statement: (and standing when 'hayya 'alā al-falāḥ' is said) because it is commanded, so it is recommended to hasten to it. He made it general, including the imam and the follower if the imam is near the mihrab; otherwise, each row stands when the imam reaches it, apparently. And if he enters from the front, they stop when their sight falls upon him. All this is when the mu'adhdhin is other than the imam. If he is one and he makes the iqamah in the mosque, the people do not stand until he finishes his iqamah. Thus in al-Zahiriyya. His statement: (and the imam's commencement from when 'qad qāmat al-ṣalāh' is said, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: he commences when he finishes the iqamah, to preserve the virtue of following the mu'adhdhin and to assist the mu'adhdhin in starting with him. Their (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's) argument is that the mu'adhdhin is trustworthy and has informed of the prayer's establishment, so he commences at that time to save his words from falsehood, and there is haste to the private conversation, and he has followed the mu'adhdhin in most [of the iqamah], so it stands in place of the whole, given that they said following is in the adhan, not the iqamah. Thus the commentator mentioned, but there is consideration because we have transmitted in the chapter of adhan that responding to the iqamah is recommended. And in al-Zahiriyya: if he delays until the mu'adhdhin finishes the iqamah, it is not objectionable in all their statements. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 531

Commentary
This passage contains two rulings: (1) When to stand for prayer: It is sunnah to stand when the mu'adhdhin says 'hayya 'alā al-falāḥ' (come to success). This applies to both imam and followers. However, if the imam is not near the mihrab, the rows stand when the imam reaches their row. If the imam enters from the front, they stand when they see him. If the same person is both mu'adhdhin and imam, the congregation does not stand until he finishes the iqamah. (2) A dispute between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad on one side and Abu Yusuf on the other: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say the imam should begin the prayer (i.e., say the takbir) when the mu'adhdhin says 'qad qāmat al-ṣalāh' (the prayer has been established). Abu Yusuf says the imam should wait until the mu'adhdhin completes the entire iqamah. The reasoning: Abu Hanifa/Muhammad argue that the mu'adhdhin is a trustworthy reporter; if the imam delays, the mu'adhdhin's report would be false. Also, the imam has followed most of the iqamah, so it suffices. Moreover, following (ijabah) is for adhan, not iqamah (according to one view). Abu Yusuf's reasoning is to preserve the virtue of following the mu'adhdhin entirely and to assist him. The commentator notes that this is debatable because responding to iqamah is recommended. However, the Zahiriyya states that delaying until the end is permissible according to all. The relied-upon position seems to be the permissibility of both, with a preference for starting at 'qad qamat'.

Key Terms
القيام (al-qiyam): Standing for prayer, specifically at the call 'hayya 'ala al-falah'.
الآذان (al-adhan): The call to prayer; 'ijabah' (responding) is recommended. Here, the imam's starting time is discussed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, when should the imam begin the prayer?
A) After the entire iqamah is finished
B) When the mu'adhdhin says 'qad qamat al-salah'
C) When the mu'adhdhin says 'Allahu Akbar' the first time
D) When the worshippers are all ready

Key Takeaway
The recommended time to stand for prayer is when 'hayya ala al-falah' is called, and the imam may start at 'qad qamat' or after iqamah; both are permissible.

Sunnah of Raising Hands in Takbir: Timing and Gender Differences
Explains the sunnah of takbir, hand raising, and presents three opinions on timing, plus the ruling for women.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on raising hands at the opening takbir, explain the three opinions on its timing, and identify the preferred view for women.

Core Idea
Raising hands at takbir is sunnah muakkadah; the timing (before, during, or after) is debated among Hanafi imams.

The opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram) is the first step into prayer. Among its sunan, raising the hands is a well-known practice. But when exactly should one raise – before saying 'Allahu Akbar', simultaneously, or after? And where should a woman raise – to her ears like a man or to her shoulders for modesty? These questions are not trivial; they reflect the richness of Hanafi fiqh and the school's method of reconciling different hadiths. In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author presents the evidence and the ikhtilaf within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being discussed? It is the raising of hands at the opening takbir. State the hukm level: it is sunnah muakkadah, not wajib.
The text mentions 'min sunan al-takbir' (from the sunnahs of takbir) indicating sunnah.
2
Locate the primary evidence
The author cites the hadith of Anas where the Prophet aligned his thumbs with his ears. Also references the hadith of Ibn 'Umar about raising to shoulders, which is reconciled by interpreting different circumstances or different parts of the hand.
The reconciliation shows the Hanafi method of jam' (harmonisation) between contradictory proofs.
3
Analyze the three opinions on timing
Three views: (1) simultaneous with takbir (Abu Yusuf, Qadi Khan, many later scholars), (2) before takbir (Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, authenticated in al-Hidayah), (3) after takbir. Each is supported by a hadith. Note who supports which view.
The first view is supported by many; the second is also strong.
4
Determine the ruling for women
The apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) says women raise like men to the ears. But Ibn Muqatil narrates raising to shoulders for modesty, which is preferred in al-Hidayah.
Both narrations are from within the Hanafi school; the mufta bihi often follows al-Hidayah's choice.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Understand that the practical difference (thamarah) is in how one prays: if following the first opinion, raise simultaneously; if the second, raise first then say takbir. For women, the difference is raising to ears vs. shoulders. Both are valid within the school.
One should not criticise those following another valid opinion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإذا أراد الدخول في الصلاة (كبر أي تكبيرة الافتتاح قائماً كما قدمناه، وتقدم أنه يكون شارعاً بالنية عند التكبير لا ،به وأن العاجز عن النطق لا يلزمه تحريك اللسان على الصحيح، ومن سنن التكبير حذفه كما في البدائع والمحيط . قوله : ( ورفع يديه حذاء أذنيه) لما رويناه ولما رواه الحاكم وصححه عن أنس قال : رأيت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كبر فحاذي بإبهاميه أذنيه . وما ورد في حديث ابن عمر أنه صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يرفع يديه إلى منكبيه فمحمول على حالة العذر حين كانت عليهم الأكسية والبرانس في زمن الشتاء كما أخبر به وائل بن حجر رضي الله عنه على ما رواه الطحاوي عنه، أو المراد بما رويناه رؤوس الأصابع وبالثاني الأكف والأرساغ عملاً بالدلائل بالقدر الممكن كما في البدائع واعتمده في فتح القدير. أطلقه فشمل الرجل والمرأة قالوا يذكر حكم رفعها في ظاهر الرواية، وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أنها كالرجل فيه لأن كفيها ليستا بعورة، وروى ابن مقاتل أنها ترفع حذاء منكبيها لأنه أستر لها وصححه في الهداية ولا فرق بين الحرة والأمة على الروايتين. والمراد بالمحاذاة أن بإبهاميه شحمتي أذنيه ليتيقن بمحاذاة يديه بأذنيه كما ذكره في النقاية. ولم يبين المصنف وقت الرفع لأنه عبر بالواو وهي . المطلق الجميع وفيه ثلاثة أقوال : القول الأول أنه يرفع مقارناً للتكبير وهو المروي عن أبي يوسف قولاً والمحكي عن الطحاوي فعلاً واختاره شيخ الإسلام وقاضيخان وصاحب الخلاصة والتحفة والبدائع والمحيط حتى قال البقالي : هذا قول أصحابنا جميعاً. ويشهد له المروي عنه عليه الصلاة والسلام أنه كان يكبر عند كل خفض ورفع، وما رواه أبو داود أنه لو كان يرفع يديه مع التكبير وفسر قاضيخان المقارنة بأن تكون بداءته عند بداءته وختمه عند ختمه . القول الثاني وقته قبل التكبير ونسبه في المجمع إلى أبي حنيفة ومحمد، وفي غاية البيان إلى عامة علمائنا، وفي المبسوط إلى أكثر مشايخنا، وصححه في الهداية، ويشهد له ما في الصحيحين عن ابن عمر قال : كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا افتتح الصلاة رفع يديه حتى يكونا حذو منكبيه ثم كبر. القول الثالث وقته بعد التكبير فيكبر أولاً ثم يرفع
His statement: 'When he intends to enter the prayer, he says takbir' i.e., the takbirat al-ihram while standing as we have presented. It has preceded that he becomes a starter by intention at the takbir, not before, and that one unable to speak is not obliged to move his tongue according to the correct view. Among the sunnahs of takbir is its conciseness (hazf) as in al-Bada'i' and al-Muhit. His statement: 'And he raises his hands to the level of his ears' due to what we have narrated and due to what al-Hakim narrated and authenticated from Anas who said: I saw the Prophet, peace be upon him, say takbir and bring his thumbs near his ears. And what is reported in the hadith of Ibn 'Umar that he used to raise his hands to his shoulders is interpreted as a case of excuse when they were wearing cloaks and hoods in winter, as reported by Wa'il ibn Hujr, may Allah be pleased with him, according to what al-Tahawi narrated from him. Or the meaning of what we narrated is the tips of the fingers, and the second is the palms and wrists, acting upon the evidences as much as possible, as in al-Bada'i' and adopted in Fath al-Qadir. He made it general, including men and women. They said: The ruling of her raising is mentioned in the apparent narration. Al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that she is like the man in this because her palms are not 'awrah. Ibn Muqatil narrated that she raises to the level of her shoulders because it is more concealing for her, and this was authenticated in al-Hidayah. There is no difference between a free woman and a slave-girl according to the two narrations. The meaning of 'alignment' is that with his thumbs he aligns with the lobes of his ears to be certain of alignment of his hands with his ears, as mentioned in al-Niqayah. The author did not specify the time of raising because he expressed it with the waw which is absolute. There are three opinions: The first: that he raises simultaneously with the takbir, which is narrated from Abu Yusuf as a statement and reported from al-Tahawi as an action, and chosen by Shaykh al-Islam, Qadi Khan, author of al-Khulasah, al-Tuhfah, al-Bada'i', and al-Muhit, so much so that al-Baqqali said: This is the saying of all our companions. It is supported by what is narrated from him, peace be upon him, that he used to say takbir at every lowering and raising, and what Abu Dawud narrated that he used to raise his hands with the takbir. Qadi Khan interpreted simultaneity as his beginning at his beginning and his ending at his ending. The second opinion: its time is before the takbir, attributed in al-Majma' to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, in Ghayat al-Bayan to the generality of our scholars, and in al-Mabsut to most of our mashayikh, and authenticated in al-Hidayah. It is supported by what is in the two Sahihs from Ibn 'Umar: The Prophet, peace be upon him, when he opened the prayer, raised his hands until they were level with his shoulders, then said takbir. The third opinion: its time is after the takbir: he says takbir first, then raises.
Source pages p. 532

Commentary
This passage is a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute on the sunnah of raising hands during the opening takbir. The text begins by clarifying that the takbir is the takbirat al-ihram performed while standing, and that one becomes a musharr' (initiator) by intention at the moment of takbir. Among the sunan of takbir is hazf (conciseness) — not prolonging the pronunciation. Then the main topic: raising hands to the ears. The proof is from the hadith of Anas where the Prophet aligned his thumbs with his ears. The hadith of Ibn 'Umar (raising to shoulders) is interpreted as either a case of excuse (wearing thick clothes) or indicating different parts of the hand (fingertips vs. palms). The ruling includes women: according to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya), women raise like men. But a narration from Ibn Muqatil says women raise to the shoulders for modesty, which is preferred in al-Hidayah. There is no difference between free and slave women. The text then presents three opinions on the timing of raising hands relative to the takbir: (1) simultaneous with takbir (preferred by Abu Yusuf, Qadi Khan, and many later scholars), (2) before takbir (attributed to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, authenticated in al-Hidayah), (3) after takbir. Each opinion is supported by a hadith. The text does not explicitly choose a mufta bihi, but by presenting the first view in detail with many supporters, it may indicate its strength; however, the second view is also strong. The student should note the ikhtilaf and the practical implications.

Key Terms
حذف (hazf): Conciseness in pronouncing takbir, not prolonging the vowels or exaggerating
محاذاة (muhadhat): Alignment: the thumbs aligning with the earlobes or hands with shoulders
مقارنة (muqaranah): Simultaneity: beginning and ending the raising with the takbir

Key Takeaway
Raising hands at the opening takbir is a confirmed sunnah with multiple valid timings and a preferred practice for women, reflecting the Hanafi school's flexibility.

Raising Hands in Prayer: Description and Women's Ruling
Describes the sunnah for raising hands and intra-Hanafi dispute on women's ruling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi sunnah of raising hands in the opening takbir and identify the preferred position for women.

Core Idea
Raising hands to the ears is sunnah; for women, raising to shoulders is more modest and preferred.

In this passage, we explore the sunnah of raising hands at the opening takbir of prayer. The author presents the prophetic evidence and then addresses a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute regarding women. Understanding both the general ruling and the preferred position for women ensures your practice aligns with the relied-upon view of the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is raising the hands during the opening takbir. Determine its hukm level: fard, wajib, or sunnah. The text indicates it is sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah).
Confirmed sunnah means the Prophet consistently performed it, but omitting it does not invalidate the prayer.
2
Analyze the proof from hadith
The author cites the hadith of Anas (verified by al-Hakim) describing the Prophet aligning his thumbs with his earlobes. Also references the hadith of Ibn 'Umar (raising to shoulders) which is reconciled as due to winter garments or as a different hand position.
The reconciliation shows how Hanafi scholars harmonize apparent contradictions in the sunnah.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute for women
Two narrations exist: one from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa (women raise like men) and another from Ibn Muqatil (women raise to shoulders). The first argues palms are not 'awrah; the second emphasizes greater concealment.
The text notes there is no distinction between free and slave women in either narration.
4
Apply the tarjih and state the mufta bihi
The author declares the position of Ibn Muqatil (women raise to shoulders) as correct (sahhaha) in al-Hidayah. This becomes the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position for fatwa.
Tarjih is based on the principle of modesty (sitr) and the authority of al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإذا أراد الدخول في الصلاة (كبر أي تكبيرة الافتتاح قائماً كما قدمناه، وتقدم أنه يكون شارعاً بالنية عند التكبير لا به وأن العاجز عن النطق لا يلزمه تحريك اللسان على الصحيح، ومن سنن التكبير حذفه كما في البدائع والمحيط . قوله : ( ورفع يديه حذاء أذنيه) لما رويناه ولما رواه الحاكم وصححه عن أنس قال : رأيت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كبر فحاذي بإبهاميه أذنيه . وما ورد في حديث ابن عمر أنه صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يرفع يديه إلى منكبيه فمحمول على حالة العذر حين كانت عليهم الأكسية والبرانس في زمن الشتاء كما أخبر به وائل بن حجر رضي الله عنه على ما رواه الطحاوي عنه، أو المراد بما رويناه رؤوس الأصابع وبالثاني الأكف والأرساغ عملاً بالدلائل بالقدر الممكن كما في البدائع واعتمده في فتح القدير. أطلقه فشمل الرجل والمرأة قالوا يذكر حكم رفعها في ظاهر الرواية، وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أنها كالرجل فيه لأن كفيها ليستا بعورة، وروى ابن مقاتل أنها ترفع حذاء منكبيها لأنه أستر لها وصححه في الهداية ولا فرق بين الحرة والأمة على الروايتين. والمراد بالمحاذاة أن بإبهاميه شحمتي أذنيه ليتيقن بمحاذاة يديه بأذنيه كما ذكره في النقاية.
His statement: 'And when he intends to enter the prayer, he says the takbir (i.e., the opening takbir) standing, as we have mentioned. And it has been stated that he becomes a prayer-starter with the intention at the time of takbir, not by it, and that one unable to speak is not required to move his tongue according to the correct view. Among the sunnahs of the takbir is its conciseness (without prolongation), as in al-Bada'i' and al-Muhit. His statement: 'and he raises his hands opposite his ears' based on what we have narrated and what al-Hakim narrated and authenticated from Anas who said: 'I saw the Prophet (peace be upon him) say the takbir and he aligned his thumbs with his earlobes.' What is reported in the hadith of Ibn 'Umar that he (peace be upon him) used to raise his hands to his shoulders is interpreted as a case of excuse when they wore cloaks and hoods in winter as informed by Wa'il ibn Hujr (may Allah be pleased with him) according to what al-Tahawi narrated from him, or it means by 'what we narrated' the fingertips and by the second the palms and wrists, acting upon the evidences as much as possible as in al-Bada'i' and relied upon in Fath al-Qadir. He made it general, thus including men and women. They mentioned the ruling of her raising in the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah). al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that she is like a man because her palms are not 'awrah. Ibn Muqatil narrated that she raises to her shoulders because it is more concealing for her, and this was declared correct in al-Hidayah, and there is no difference between a free woman and a slave woman according to the two narrations. The meaning of 'alignment' is that he aligns his thumbs with his earlobes to be certain of the alignment of his hands with his ears as mentioned in al-Niqayah.
Source pages p. 532

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof explaining the sunnah of raising hands during the opening takbir. The author begins by noting that the opening takbir is said standing, and that one becomes a prayer-starter with the intention at the time of takbir, not by the takbir itself. One who cannot speak is not required to move his tongue. Conciseness (hazf) in the takbir is sunnah. The passage then addresses the raising of hands: the sunnah is to raise them so that the thumbs align with the earlobes, as reported by Anas. The hadith of Ibn 'Umar about raising to the shoulders is explained as due to winter garments. There is a dispute among Hanafi authorities: in Zahir al-Riwayah, women raise like men; al-Hasan narrates from Abu Hanifa that women raise like men because their palms are not 'awrah; Ibn Muqatil narrates that women raise to their shoulders for modesty, and this is declared correct in al-Hidayah. There is no difference between free and slave women in either narration. The alignment is clarified as placing thumbs at earlobes to ensure the hands are opposite the ears.

Key Terms
رفع اليدين (raf' al-yadayn): Raising the hands during the opening takbir of prayer, a confirmed sunnah.
محاذاة (muhādā): Alignment; here meaning thumbs opposite earlobes to confirm hands are opposite ears.
حذف (hazf): Conciseness in pronouncing the takbir without prolongation or excessive elongation.

D) She should not raise her hands at all.

Key Takeaway
Raising hands is sunnah muakkadah; for women, the preferred position is to the shoulders for modesty.

Timing of Raising Hands in Salah: Three Intra-Hanafi Opinions
Discusses the three opinions on when hands are raised: before, with, or after the opening takbir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three Hanafi opinions on the timing of raising hands before the opening takbir, state the dalil for each, and explain which view is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Three Hanafi views on when to raise hands: before, with, or after the takbir; the preponderant view is before.

The timing of raising hands at the start of salah is a sunnah act with varying interpretations within the Hanafi school. The author of al-Kanz used the conjunction 'wa' (and), leaving the timing ambiguous. This lesson examines the three opinions—simultaneous, before, and after—and their supporting evidence, culminating in the relied-upon position according to al-Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Determine the precise fiqh question: what is the recommended (sunnah) timing for raising hands relative to the opening takbir?
The ruling is sunnah, not wajib.
2
List the three opinions
Enumerate the three positions within the Hanafi school: (1) raising simultaneously with the takbir, (2) raising before the takbir, (3) raising after the takbir.
Attribution: opinion 1 to Abu Yusuf and later scholars; opinion 2 to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad; opinion 3 to some later authorities.
3
Examine the dalil for each opinion
For opinion 1: hadith that the Prophet raised hands 'with' the takbir (narrated by Abu Dawud). For opinion 2: hadith of Ibn 'Umar in Sahihayn that he raised hands 'then' said the takbir. For opinion 3: limited evidence, often considered weak.
The word 'thumma' (then) in the Ibn 'Umar hadith is explicit for sequence.
4
Understand the tarjih
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah declared the second opinion (raising before takbir) as correct, based on the strength of the Ibn 'Umar hadith and its explicit sequence.
This is the mufta bihi position.
5
Recognize the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if one raises after the takbir, the sunnah time is lost (but salah is still valid). The optimal practice is to raise before or simultaneously, with before being preferred.
This affects the form of the prayer, not its validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يبين المصنف وقت الرفع لأنه عبر بالواو وهي . المطلق الجميع وفيه ثلاثة أقوال : القول الأول أنه يرفع مقارناً للتكبير وهو المروي عن أبي يوسف قولاً والمحكي عن الطحاوي فعلاً واختاره شيخ الإسلام وقاضيخان وصاحب الخلاصة والتحفة والبدائع والمحيط حتى قال البقالي : هذا قول أصحابنا جميعاً. ويشهد له المروي عنه عليه الصلاة والسلام أنه كان يكبر عند كل خفض ورفع، وما رواه أبو داود أنه لو كان يرفع يديه مع التكبير وفسر قاضيخان المقارنة بأن تكون بداءته عند بداءته وختمه عند ختمه . القول الثاني وقته قبل التكبير ونسبه في المجمع إلى أبي حنيفة ومحمد، وفي غاية البيان إلى عامة علمائنا، وفي المبسوط إلى أكثر مشايخنا، وصححه في الهداية، ويشهد له ما في الصحيحين عن ابن عمر قال : كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا افتتح الصلاة رفع يديه حتى يكونا حذو منكبيه ثم كبر. القول الثالث وقته بعد التكبير فيكبر أولاً ثم يرفع
The author did not specify the time of raising because he expressed it with 'wa' which is absolute for all. There are three opinions: The first opinion is that he raises simultaneously with the takbir, which is narrated from Abu Yusuf as a statement and reported from al-Tahawi as an action, and it was chosen by Shaykh al-Islam, Qadi Khan, the author of al-Khulasa, al-Tuhfa, al-Bada'i', and al-Muhit, such that al-Baqqali said: 'This is the statement of all our companions.' It is supported by what is narrated from him (peace be upon him) that he used to say the takbir at every lowering and raising, and what Abu Dawud narrated that he would raise his hands with the takbir. Qadi Khan interpreted simultaneity as beginning with the beginning and ending with the end. The second opinion: its time is before the takbir, attributed in al-Majma' to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, in Ghayat al-Bayan to most of our scholars, and in al-Mabsut to most of our shaykhs, and it was declared correct in al-Hidayah. It is supported by what is in the Two Sahihs from Ibn 'Umar who said: 'When the Prophet (peace be upon him) began prayer, he raised his hands until they were level with his shoulders, then he said the takbir.' The third opinion: its time is after the takbir, so he says the takbir first then raises.
Source pages p. 532

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the timing of raising hands at the start of prayer. The author (al-Kanz) did not specify a time, using the conjunction 'wa' which allows simultaneity. Three positions are recorded: (1) Raising simultaneously with the takbir, attributed to Abu Yusuf and preferred by many later Hanafi scholars. (2) Raising before the takbir, attributed to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, and declared correct in al-Hidayah. (3) Raising after the takbir. The text here lists only the first two opinions fully; the third is mentioned but cut off. The preferred view according to al-Hidayah is the second (raising before takbir), supported by the hadith of Ibn 'Umar. The simultaneity view relies on hadiths about the Prophet raising with the takbir. The third view (after takbir) has limited evidence. The passage sets the stage for a tarjih that follows on the next page.

Key Terms
مقارنة (muqārana): Simultaneity; raising hands at the same time as the takbir, beginning and ending together.
الواو (al-wāw): The conjunction 'and' (wa) used in the matn; it is ambiguous as to sequence, allowing multiple interpretations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which view on the timing of raising hands is declared correct (mufta bihi) in al-Hidayah?
A) Raising simultaneously with the takbir.
B) Raising before the takbir.
C) Raising after the takbir.
D) It is makruh to raise hands.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has three valid positions on when to raise hands; the mufta bihi is raising before the takbir.

Starting Prayer with Words Other Than 'Allahu Akbar'
Ruling on alternative opening phrases for prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the majority Hanafi position on valid opening phrases for prayer and explain Abu Yusuf's dissenting view, including why the majority view is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Any pure praise of Allah can serve as the opening takbir, according to the majority of Hanafi imams.

You probably know that prayer begins with takbir. But what if someone says 'Subhan Allah' instead? Is the prayer still valid? This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute over the required wording of takbirat al-iftitah, clarifying the majority position and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is starting prayer (takbirat al-iftitah). The matn rules it valid (sahih) if done with tasbih, tahlil, or Persian phrases.
The matn uses 'shara'a' (to start) and 'sahha' (is valid).
2
Extract the majority definition
The commentator explains that 'takbir' means every word that is pure praise (thana' khalis) indicating glorification of Allah.
This definition is broad, covering all praise phrases.
3
Note Abu Yusuf's dissenting view
Abu Yusuf restricts the valid phrases to those derived from the root k-b-r: five specific forms like 'Allahu Akbar' and 'Allah al-Akbar'.
The passage is cut off; the full list is not preserved here.
4
Understand the evidence
The majority relies on the linguistic meaning of takbir (to magnify), so any wording that conveys magnification is acceptable. Abu Yusuf emphasizes the specific usage in the Quran and Sunnah.
The dalil is linguistic and textual.
5
Apply the mufta bihi
In practice, the majority view is relied upon because it is more accommodating and consistent with the purpose of the takbir.
The mufta bihi is the majority view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ( ولو شرع بالتسبيح أو بالتهليل أو بالفارسية صح) شروع في المراد بتكبيرة الافتتاح فأفاد أن المراد بها كل لفظ هو ثناء خالص دال على التعظيم وقال أبو يوسف : لا شارعاً إلا بألفاظ مشتقة من التكبير وهي خمسة ألفاظ : الله أكبر، الله الأكبر، الله
His statement: 'And if he starts with tasbih or tahlil or Persian, it is valid.' This is a start regarding the meaning of the opening takbir, so it indicates that its meaning is every word that is pure praise indicating glorification. Abu Yusuf said: 'He is not a starter except with words derived from takbir, which are five words: Allahu Akbar, Allah al-Akbar, Allah...'
Source pages p. 533

Commentary
This passage discusses the validity of starting prayer with phrases other than 'Allahu Akbar'. The matn of al-Kanz states that if someone begins with tasbih (e.g., 'Subhan Allah'), tahlil ('La ilaha illa Allah'), or in Persian (e.g., 'Khuda-yi buzurg'), the prayer is valid. The commentator explains that the key is that the phrase must be pure praise (thana') indicating glorification of Allah. However, Abu Yusuf disagrees, restricting the opening phrase to words derived from the root of takbir ('k-b-r'), namely five specific forms: 'Allahu Akbar', 'Allah al-Akbar', 'Allah' (presumably with 'Akbar' implied), and two others. The passage is incomplete due to a page break, but the dispute is clear: the majority of Hanafi scholars (including Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) accept any praise phrase, while Abu Yusuf requires a takbir derivative. The mufta bihi is the more expansive view from the majority, as it is consistent with the principle that the opening takbir is a declaration of Allah's greatness in any wording.

Key Terms
تكبيرة الافتتاح (takbīrat al-iftitāḥ): The opening takbir that begins prayer; its wording is generally 'Allahu Akbar' but other praise phrases may suffice.
ثناء خالص (thanā' khāliṣ): Pure praise or glorification of Allah, devoid of any other meaning.
تكبير (takbīr): Saying 'Allahu Akbar' or any phrase that magnifies Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view, which of the following phrases can be used for the opening takbir?
A) Only 'Allahu Akbar'.
B) Only 'Allahu Akbar' and 'Allah al-Akbar'.
C) Any words of pure praise like 'Subhan Allah' or 'La ilaha illa Allah'.
D) Only Arabic phrases.

Key Takeaway
The opening takbir in Hanafi prayer can be any phrase of pure praise, not just 'Allahu Akbar', according to the majority of the school's founders.

Hand Raising During the Opening Takbir: Timing and Protocol
Ruling on timing and manner of hand raising with proof and reconciliation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the timing of hand raising during the opening takbir and apply the rule for those with physical limitations.

Core Idea
Hands should be raised simultaneously with the opening takbir; delay misses the sunnah but does not invalidate.

The proper timing of raising the hands (raf' al-yadayn) during the opening takbir is a matter of sunnah in the Hanafi school. This lesson examines the preferred timing based on the Prophet's practice, the reconciliation of conflicting narrations, and the rulings for those who cannot fully raise their hands.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act of raising hands during the opening takbir is a sunnah, not a pillar (rukn) of prayer. Its omission does not invalidate the prayer but means the sunnah is missed.
This is a sunnah muakkadah according to the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage cites the hadith in Sahih Muslim that the Prophet used to say the takbir and then raise his hands. This is the primary textual evidence.
The hadith is a proof for the timing of hand raising.
3
Understand the reconciliation of narrations
The word 'thumma' (then) in the hadith is interpreted as simultaneous (meaning 'waw') because other narrations show the Prophet raising with the takbir. The commentator explains that definitive texts take precedence over probabilistic ones.
This reconciliation supports the preferred view of simultaneity.
4
Apply the rule for delays
If one finishes the takbir before raising the hands, the opportunity for the sunnah has passed. Raising after the takbir does not count. However, if one raises during the takbir, the sunnah is still achieved.
The sunnah is tied to the time of the takbir.
5
Note the concession for inability
If one cannot raise to the sunnah position (ears or shoulders), they raise as much as possible. If only one hand can be raised, that is sufficient. If raising normally requires an exaggerated motion, they still raise.
The principle of ease (yusr) applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

١١٠] ولهذا يجوز الذبح باسم الرحمن أو باسم ، فكذا هذا. ثم غاية ما هنا أن الثابت بالنص ذكر الله تعالى على سبيل التعظيم ولفظ التكبير ثبت بالخبر فيجب العمل به حتى يكره افتتاح الصلاة بغيره لمن يحسنه كما الافتتاح بغير الله أكبر) عند أبي حنيفة، فالمراد كراهة التحريم لأنها في رتبة الواجب من جهة الترك، فعلى هذا يضعف ما صححه السرخسي من أن الأصح أنه لا يكره مستدلاً بما روي عن مجاهد قال : كان الأنبياء يفتتحون الصلاة بلا إله إلا الله ونبينا من جملتهم. وهذا على تقدير صحته فالمراد غير نبينا بدلیل نقل المواظبة عنه على لفظ التكبير . ويضعف أيضاً ما ذكره المصنف في المستصفى من أن مراعاة لفظ التكبير في الافتتاح واجبة في صلاة العيد بخلاف سائر الصلوات لما علمت أنها واجبة في الكل. والظاهر أنه مبني على تصحيح السرخسي بدليل ما ذكره في الكافي. وأراد المصنف بالتسبيح والتهليل ما ذكرنا من اللفظ الدال على التعظيم لا خصوص سبحان الله والحمد لله فأفاد بإطلاقه أنه لا فرق بين الأسماء الخاصة أو المشتركة حتى يصير شارعاً بالرحيم أكبر أو أجل كما نص عليه في المحيط والبدائع والخلاصة، وصرح في المجتبى بأنه الأصح، وأفتى به المرغيناني. فما في الذخيرة عن فتاوى الفضلي أنه لا يصير شارعاً بالرحيم ضعيف. وقيده في شرح المنية بأن لا يقترن به ما يفسد الصلاة أما إذا قرن به ما كان كذلك فلا شارعاً يصير اتفاقاً كقوله العالم بالمعدوم والموجود أو بأحوال الخلق كما أن القول بأنه لا يجوز بكل اسم مشترك مقيد بما إذا لم يقترن بما يزيل اشتراكه أما إذا قرن بما يزيله لا يفسد الصلاة كقوله معنی المراد لذلك الحمل كما لا يخفى قوله : (شروع) في المراد بتكبيرة الافتتاح) ظاهره أن ذلك هو من قول المصنف كبر» والظاهر خلافه وإلا لأتى بالفاء وقال فلو شرع بل مراده بالتكبير ظاهره لأنه الواجب على من أراد الشروع وقوله ولو شرع» بيان لصحة الشروع بغيره فيحمل كلامه على أن المراد ذلك من الحديث لا من كلام المصنف. قوله : ( ثم غاية ما هنا الخ) النص هو قوله (وذكر اسم ربه فصلى [الأعلى: ١٥] والذكر يشمل التكبير وغيره ولفظ التكبير ثبت بالحديث المار وهو مع
Book of Prayer - Chapter on Description of Prayer. With tahlil or in Persian it is valid, just as if one recites while incapable or slaughters and names with it, not with 'O Allah forgive me.' And it is preferred [to raise hands] in front of him, and testimony to that is in Sahih Muslim that he, when he prayed, said the takbir and then raised his hands. And in al-Hidayah, he preferred what was authenticated, that his action negates pride from other than Allah, and negation is given precedence over affirmation like the word of shahada. It was objected that this is in wording, so it does not necessarily apply elsewhere, and the response is that he did not claim its necessity elsewhere, rather the discussion is about priority. So among the three sayings, there is a narration from him, peace be upon him, indicating that he performed all his actions giving precedence to raising in the mentioned sense, and the word 'thumma' in his saying 'then he raised' is interpreted as 'waw' and 'ma'a' in the sense of 'before' because adverbs substitute for each other. And it could be said: the precedence of negation in the word of shahada is a necessity because it is impossible to speak negation and affirmation together, unlike here. And the narration that he used to raise with the takbir is a definitive text on simultaneity, and the narration that he used to raise and then say takbir, and vice versa, could have 'thumma' meaning 'waw', and it applies to simultaneity like order, so it is interpreted as simultaneity to reconcile the narrations. And it was not reversed because the definitive is preferable to the probabilistic. Thus in Sharh al-Muniyah, and there is a discussion about it, because the word 'thumma' is established for order with delay, and its use to mean 'waw' is metaphorical, so it is apparent in its meaning just as 'ma'a' is apparent in simultaneity and its use to mean 'after' is metaphorical as in His saying 'Indeed, with hardship comes ease' and as in his saying 'You are divorced twice along with the freeing of your master' as they mentioned in the chapter on divorce, so it is not definitive. So the contradiction between the narrations is established, so the preferred view is based on the mentioned meaning, not on what he mentioned. As for the comparison to the word of shahada, it is in the realm of representation, not the technical qiyas. And if he says takbir and does not raise his hands until he finishes the takbir, he does not bring it because its place has passed, and he should bring it according to the third opinion, as is not hidden. And if he mentions it during the takbir, he raises because its place has not passed. And if he cannot [raise] to the sunnah position, he raises as much as he can, and if he can raise one hand without the other, he raises that one. And if he cannot raise except by excess over the sunnah, he raises both. Thus mentioned the Sharh, may Allah have mercy on him. His saying: (And if he starts with tasbih or tahlil or in Persian, it is valid) is a commencement regarding the intended meaning of the opening takbir, so it indicates that what is meant is every word that is pure praise indicating glorification. And Abu Yusuf said: He does not commence except with words derived from takbir, which are five words: Allahu Akbar, Allah al-Akbar, Allah al-Kabir, Allah Kabir, Allah al-Kubbar - as in al-Khulasa - except if he does not know the takbir or does not know that the commencement of prayer is with it, because of the hadith 'and its opening is the takbir', and it is achieved with these words because af'al and fa'il are equal in His attributes. And they have that takbir linguistically means glorification, and these words are established for it, especially Allah A'zam, so it is takbir even if not with the well-known wording of takbir. And in al-Bada'i: The evidence that the saying 'Allahu Akbar' and 'al-Rahman Akbar' are equal is His saying 'Say, call upon Allah or call upon al-Rahman, whichever you call, to Him belong the most beautiful names' [17:110], and for this reason slaughtering is permissible with the name al-Rahman or with, so likewise this. Then the utmost here is that what is established by text is the mention of Allah in the way of glorification, and the wording of takbir is established by hadith, so it is obligatory to act upon it, so it is disliked to open prayer with other than it for one who can say it well, as we said regarding reciting the Qur'an along with al-Fatiha and in bowing and prostration along with the tasmi' mentioned in al-Kafi. This indicates obligation, and it is more similar to continuous practice not accompanied by actual leaving. This is what is mentioned in al-Tuhfa, al-Dhakhira, and al-Nihaya that the correct view is that it is disliked to open with other than 'Allahu Akbar' according to Abu Hanifa, so what is meant is prohibition-level dislike (karahah tahrimeyah) because it is in the rank of wajib from the aspect of leaving. On this basis, what al-Sarkhasi authenticated that it is not disliked is weakened, using as evidence what was narrated from Mujahid that he said: The prophets used to open prayer with 'La ilaha illa Allah' and our prophet is among them. Even if this is authentic, the intended meaning is other than our prophet, due to the transmission of his continuous practice of the wording of takbir. And it also weakens what the author mentioned in al-Mustasfa that observing the wording of takbir in the opening is obligatory in the prayer of Eid but not in other prayers, because we know it is obligatory in all. And it appears that it is based on al-Sarkhasi's authentication as indicated by what is in al-Kafi. And the author intended by tasbih and tahlil the word we mentioned indicating glorification, not specifically Subhanallah and Alhamdulillah. So his absolute expression indicates that there is no difference between specific or shared names, so he becomes a commencer with 'al-Rahim Akbar' or 'Ajal' as stated in al-Muhit, al-Bada'i, and al-Khulasa, and in al-Mujtaba it is declared that this is the correct view, and al-Marghinani gave fatwa accordingly. So what is in al-Dhakhira from the fatwas of al-Fadli that he does not become a commencer with 'al-Rahim' is weak. And it is restricted in Sharh al-Muniyah by that it should not be accompanied by what would invalidate the prayer; if it is accompanied by something that does that, then he does not become a commencer by agreement, like his saying 'the Knower of the non-existent and the existent' or with the conditions of creatures, just as the statement that it is not permissible with every shared name is restricted to when the removal of its ambiguity is not accompanied; if it is accompanied by what removes it, it does not invalidate the prayer, like his saying… the intended meaning of that interpretation, as is not hidden. His saying: (commencement) regarding the intended meaning of the opening takbir, outwardly that is from the author's saying 'he says takbir' but the opposite is apparent, otherwise he would have used 'fa' and said 'if he starts', but his meaning with takbir is its outward meaning because it is obligatory on whoever wants to start, and his saying 'and if he starts' is an explanation of the validity of starting with other than it, so his words are interpreted as that the intended meaning is from the hadith, not from the author's words. His saying: (then the utmost here) the text is his saying 'and mention the name of his Lord and pray' [87:15], and mention includes takbir and other, and the wording of takbir is established by the hadith mentioned.
Source pages p. 533

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq in the chapter on the description of prayer. The author addresses two interrelated issues regarding the opening of prayer: the validity of alternative formulae for the opening takbir, and the proper timing and manner of raising the hands (raf' al-yadayn). The passage first discusses the hand raising: the preferred view is that the hands should be raised at the beginning of the takbir, based on a hadith in Sahih Muslim and supported by rational argument (negation of greatness from others precedes affirmation). The author resolves conflicting narrations by interpreting 'thumma' as 'waw' (simultaneity) to reconcile reports. If one delays raising until after the takbir, the sunnah is missed; if during the takbir, it is still valid. For those unable to raise to the sunnah position, they raise as much as possible. The second issue is the opening formula: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, any word of pure praise indicating glorification (like tasbih, tahlil, or Persian translation) is valid for the opening takbir if one does not know Arabic or is unable to say 'Allahu Akbar'. Imam Abu Yusuf restricts it to five specific Arabic words derived from 'k-b-r'. The majority of Hanafi scholars hold that it is makruh tahrimeen (prohibitively disliked) to open with other than 'Allahu Akbar' when one can say it, due to the Prophet's continuous practice. The passage also discusses that using names like 'al-Rahim Akbar' is valid if not accompanied by something invalidating the prayer. The commentary emphasizes that the relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and the later scholars, rejecting the view that it is permissible without dislike.

Key Terms
رَفْعُ الْيَدَيْن (rafʿ al-yadayn): Raising the hands during the opening takbir. The text discusses the preferred timing (with the takbir) and the ruling for those unable to do so fully.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi position, when should the hands be raised during the opening takbir?
A) Before saying 'Allahu Akbar'
B) Simultaneously with saying 'Allahu Akbar'
C) After completing 'Allahu Akbar'
D) It does not matter

Key Takeaway
The sunnah is to raise hands simultaneously with the opening takbir; if one cannot raise fully, they raise as much as possible.

Salah — Prayer

Valid Opening Formulae: Is Any Praise Sufficient?
Ruling on alternative opening formulae with intra-madhhab and inter-madhhab disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on the validity of opening prayer with words other than 'Allahu Akbar' and identify the prohibition-level dislike for the capable.

Core Idea
Any word of pure praise indicating glorification is valid for the opening takbir, but using other than 'Allahu Akbar' when able is prohibitively disliked.

The Hanafi school holds that the opening takbir (takbirat al-iftitah) does not require the exact phrase 'Allahu Akbar'; any wording that expresses glorification suffices. However, due to the Prophet's continuous practice, it is makruh tahrimeen to use alternatives when one can say the standard phrase. This lesson examines the evidence and the dispute within the school.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, the opening of prayer is valid with any word of pure praise (tasbih, tahlil, etc.) that indicates glorification of Allah.
This includes Persian translation or names like 'al-Rahim Akbar'.
2
Identify the intra-madhhab dispute
Imam Abu Yusuf restricts valid opening words to five specific Arabic phrases derived from the root k-b-r: Allahu Akbar, Allah al-Akbar, Allah al-Kabir, Allah Kabir, Allah al-Kubbar.
The disagreement is over the linguistic scope of 'takbir'.
3
Analyze the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafi proof includes the Quranic verse 'Say, call upon Allah or call upon al-Rahman…' (17:110) which equates different names of Allah in glorification. Also, the term 'takbir' linguistically means 'glorification' in Arabic.
The hadith 'the opening of prayer is the takbir' is interpreted broadly.
4
Note the ruling for the capable
For those who can correctly say 'Allahu Akbar', it is makruh tahrimeen (prohibitively disliked) to open with any other word due to the Prophet's continuous practice (muwazabah).
This is based on the principle that abandoning the sunnah without excuse is sinful.
5
Apply the exception for the incapable
For those unable to say 'Allahu Akbar' (e.g., due to language barrier or inability), it is valid and not disliked to use other glorifying words.
The same applies if one does not know that the opening must be with takbir.

Book of Prayer - Chapter on Description of Prayer. With tahlil or in Persian it is valid, just as if one recites while incapable or slaughters and names with it, not with 'O Allah forgive me.' And it is preferred [to raise hands] in front of him, and testimony to that is in Sahih Muslim that he, when he prayed, said the takbir and then raised his hands. And in al-Hidayah, he preferred what was authenticated, that his action negates pride from other than Allah, and negation is given precedence over affirmation like the word of shahada. It was objected that this is in wording, so it does not necessarily apply elsewhere, and the response is that he did not claim its necessity elsewhere, rather the discussion is about priority. So among the three sayings, there is a narration from him, peace be upon him, indicating that he performed all his actions giving precedence to raising in the mentioned sense, and the word 'thumma' in his saying 'then he raised' is interpreted as 'waw' and 'ma'a' in the sense of 'before' because adverbs substitute for each other. And it could be said: the precedence of negation in the word of shahada is a necessity because it is impossible to speak negation and affirmation together, unlike here. And the narration that he used to raise with the takbir is a definitive text on simultaneity, and the narration that he used to raise and then say takbir, and vice versa, could have 'thumma' meaning 'waw', and it applies to simultaneity like order, so it is interpreted as simultaneity to reconcile the narrations. And it was not reversed because the definitive is preferable to the probabilistic. Thus in Sharh al-Muniyah, and there is a discussion about it, because the word 'thumma' is established for order with delay, and its use to mean 'waw' is metaphorical, so it is apparent in its meaning just as 'ma'a' is apparent in simultaneity and its use to mean 'after' is metaphorical as in His saying 'Indeed, with hardship comes ease' and as in his saying 'You are divorced twice along with the freeing of your master' as they mentioned in the chapter on divorce, so it is not definitive. So the contradiction between the narrations is established, so the preferred view is based on the mentioned meaning, not on what he mentioned. As for the comparison to the word of shahada, it is in the realm of representation, not the technical qiyas. And if he says takbir and does not raise his hands until he finishes the takbir, he does not bring it because its place has passed, and he should bring it according to the third opinion, as is not hidden. And if he mentions it during the takbir, he raises because its place has not passed. And if he cannot [raise] to the sunnah position, he raises as much as he can, and if he can raise one hand without the other, he raises that one. And if he cannot raise except by excess over the sunnah, he raises both. Thus mentioned the Sharh, may Allah have mercy on him. His saying: (And if he starts with tasbih or tahlil or in Persian, it is valid) is a commencement regarding the intended meaning of the opening takbir, so it indicates that what is meant is every word that is pure praise indicating glorification. And Abu Yusuf said: He does not commence except with words derived from takbir, which are five words: Allahu Akbar, Allah al-Akbar, Allah al-Kabir, Allah Kabir, Allah al-Kubbar - as in al-Khulasa - except if he does not know the takbir or does not know that the commencement of prayer is with it, because of the hadith 'and its opening is the takbir', and it is achieved with these words because af'al and fa'il are equal in His attributes. And they have that takbir linguistically means glorification, and these words are established for it, especially Allah A'zam, so it is takbir even if not with the well-known wording of takbir. And in al-Bada'i: The evidence that the saying 'Allahu Akbar' and 'al-Rahman Akbar' are equal is His saying 'Say, call upon Allah or call upon al-Rahman, whichever you call, to Him belong the most beautiful names' [17:110], and for this reason slaughtering is permissible with the name al-Rahman or with, so likewise this. Then the utmost here is that what is established by text is the mention of Allah in the way of glorification, and the wording of takbir is established by hadith, so it is obligatory to act upon it, so it is disliked to open prayer with other than it for one who can say it well, as we said regarding reciting the Qur'an along with al-Fatiha and in bowing and prostration along with the tasmi' mentioned in al-Kafi. This indicates obligation, and it is more similar to continuous practice not accompanied by actual leaving. This is what is mentioned in al-Tuhfa, al-Dhakhira, and al-Nihaya that the correct view is that it is disliked to open with other than 'Allahu Akbar' according to Abu Hanifa, so what is meant is prohibition-level dislike (karahah tahrimeyah) because it is in the rank of wajib from the aspect of leaving. On this basis, what al-Sarkhasi authenticated that it is not disliked is weakened, using as evidence what was narrated from Mujahid that he said: The prophets used to open prayer with 'La ilaha illa Allah' and our prophet is among them. Even if this is authentic, the intended meaning is other than our prophet, due to the transmission of his continuous practice of the wording of takbir. And it also weakens what the author mentioned in al-Mustasfa that observing the wording of takbir in the opening is obligatory in the prayer of Eid but not in other prayers, because we know it is obligatory in all. And it appears that it is based on al-Sarkhasi's authentication as indicated by what is in al-Kafi. And the author intended by tasbih and tahlil the word we mentioned indicating glorification, not specifically Subhanallah and Alhamdulillah. So his absolute expression indicates that there is no difference between specific or shared names, so he becomes a commencer with 'al-Rahim Akbar' or 'Ajal' as stated in al-Muhit, al-Bada'i, and al-Khulasa, and in al-Mujtaba it is declared that this is the correct view, and al-Marghinani gave fatwa accordingly. So what is in al-Dhakhira from the fatwas of al-Fadli that he does not become a commencer with 'al-Rahim' is weak. And it is restricted in Sharh al-Muniyah by that it should not be accompanied by what would invalidate the prayer; if it is accompanied by something that does that, then he does not become a commencer by agreement, like his saying 'the Knower of the non-existent and the existent' or with the conditions of creatures, just as the statement that it is not permissible with every shared name is restricted to when the removal of its ambiguity is not accompanied; if it is accompanied by what removes it, it does not invalidate the prayer, like his saying… the intended meaning of that interpretation, as is not hidden. His saying: (commencement) regarding the intended meaning of the opening takbir, outwardly that is from the author's saying 'he says takbir' but the opposite is apparent, otherwise he would have used 'fa' and said 'if he starts', but his meaning with takbir is its outward meaning because it is obligatory on whoever wants to start, and his saying 'and if he starts' is an explanation of the validity of starting with other than it, so his words are interpreted as that the intended meaning is from the hadith, not from the author's words. His saying: (then the utmost here) the text is his saying 'and mention the name of his Lord and pray' [87:15], and mention includes takbir and other, and the wording of takbir is established by the hadith mentioned.

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq in the chapter on the description of prayer. The author addresses two interrelated issues regarding the opening of prayer: the validity of alternative formulae for the opening takbir, and the proper timing and manner of raising the hands (raf' al-yadayn). The passage first discusses the hand raising: the preferred view is that the hands should be raised at the beginning of the takbir, based on a hadith in Sahih Muslim and supported by rational argument (negation of greatness from others precedes affirmation). The author resolves conflicting narrations by interpreting 'thumma' as 'waw' (simultaneity) to reconcile reports. If one delays raising until after the takbir, the sunnah is missed; if during the takbir, it is still valid. For those unable to raise to the sunnah position, they raise as much as possible. The second issue is the opening formula: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, any word of pure praise indicating glorification (like tasbih, tahlil, or Persian translation) is valid for the opening takbir if one does not know Arabic or is unable to say 'Allahu Akbar'. Imam Abu Yusuf restricts it to five specific Arabic words derived from 'k-b-r'. The majority of Hanafi scholars hold that it is makruh tahrimeen (prohibitively disliked) to open with other than 'Allahu Akbar' when one can say it, due to the Prophet's continuous practice. The passage also discusses that using names like 'al-Rahim Akbar' is valid if not accompanied by something invalidating the prayer. The commentary emphasizes that the relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and the later scholars, rejecting the view that it is permissible without dislike.

Key Terms
تَكْبِيرَةُ الِافْتِتَاح (takbīrat al-iftitāḥ): The opening formula of prayer, which is a statement of glorification to begin the prayer. The text discusses what qualifies as this formula.
كَرَاهَةُ التَّحْرِيم (karāhat al-taḥrīm): Prohibition-level dislike, close to haram. Used to describe the ruling of using other than 'Allahu Akbar' for the opening when able to say it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling if a person who knows Arabic opens the prayer by saying 'Subhanallah' instead of 'Allahu Akbar'?
A) The prayer is invalid because the opening must be with 'Allahu Akbar'.
B) The prayer is valid and there is no dislike because it is praise.
C) The prayer is valid but it is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimeen).
D) The prayer is valid but must be repeated without dislike.

Key Takeaway
The opening takbir is valid with any glorification, but it is prohibitively disliked to abandon the Prophet's practice without excuse.

Takbirat al-Ihram: Specific Wording, Alternatives, and Conditions
Commentary on the ruling, validity of alternatives, and conditions for takbirat al-ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the specific wording of takbirat al-ihram, distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the two disciples, and apply the conditions for validity of alternative phrases.

Core Idea
Only 'Allahu Akbar' is the prescribed takbir; alternatives are makruh tahrimi.

The takbirat al-ihram is the pillar that commences prayer. While the specific phrase 'Allahu Akbar' is universally known, the Hanafi school discusses whether other words of exaltation can serve the same function. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, the evidence used, and the conditions for valid alternatives.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Takbirat al-ihram. What is the hukm level? Wajib based on constant practice (muwazabah).
The text states that opening with other than the specific wording is makruh tahrimi.
2
State the dispute
Abu Hanifa holds that only 'Allahu Akbar' is valid. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that any word conveying ta'zim suffices.
The dispute is intra-Hanafi; the two disciples are called al-Sahibayn.
3
Examine the proofs
The disciples cite Quran 17:110 and linguistic meaning. Abu Hanifa relies on the hadith 'tahrimuha al-takbir' and the Prophet's constant practice of the specific wording.
The commentary refutes the disciples' view by emphasizing muwazabah.
4
Apply the conditions for alternatives
Even according to the disciples, alternative phrases must be a complete sentence (subject + predicate). Single words like 'Allah' or 'Akbar' are insufficient in the apparent riwayah.
Hasan ibn Ziyad's riwayah allows single words, but the fatwa is on the apparent riwayah.
5
Determine the ruling on Persian takbir
Abu Hanifa allows takbir in any language even for those who know Arabic. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad restrict it to those unable to speak Arabic.
The fatwa is on Abu Hanifa's view, making Persian takbir valid absolutely.

The Compassionate, the Merciful, the Great, Allah the Great, Allah the Most Great - as in al-Khulasa - except for one who does not know the takbir or does not know that entering prayer is done with it due to the hadith and that its prohibition is takbir, and it is attained by these words because af'al and fa'il in His attributes are the same. And for them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) that takbir linguistically is exaltation and these words are specifically placed for it, especially Allahu A'zam, so it is takbir even if not in the known wording of takbir. And in al-Bada'i: The proof that the saying Allahu Akbar and Ar-Rahmanu Akbar are equal is the verse 'Say: call upon Allah or call upon Ar-Rahman; whichever you call, to Him belong the most beautiful names' [17:110], and for this it is permissible to slaughter in the name of Ar-Rahman, so likewise this. Then the sum is that what is established by revelation is the remembrance of Allah Ta'ala in the manner of exaltation, and the wording of takbir is established by report (khabar), so one must act upon it such that it is disliked (makruh) to open prayer with other than it for one who can do it well, as we said regarding reciting the Quran with al-Fatiha and in bowing and prostrating with the prescribed glorifications, as mentioned in al-Kafi. This indicates obligation (wujub) and it is more fitting due to constancy (muwazabah) not accompanied by actual abandonment. This is what is mentioned in al-Tuhfah, al-Dhakhirah, and al-Nihayah that the correct view is that it is makruh to open with other than Allahu Akbar according to Abu Hanifa, so the intended meaning is karahah tahrimiyyah because it is in the rank of wajib in terms of omission. Based on this, what al-Sarakhsi corrected (that it is not makruh) is weak, using the report from Mujahid who said: The prophets used to open prayer with La ilaha illa Allah, and our Prophet is among them. Even if this is authentic, the intended meaning is other than our Prophet due to the transmitted constancy of his wording of takbir. And also weak is what the author said in al-Mustasfa that observing the wording of takbir in opening is wajib in Eid prayer unlike other prayers, since we know it is wajib in all. And it appears that this is based on al-Sarakhsi's correction, as indicated by what is in al-Kafi. And the author meant by tasbih and tahlil the word indicating exaltation as we mentioned, not specifically Subhan Allah and Alhamdulillah, so his absolute expression indicates that there is no difference between specific or common names, so that one becomes a shar'i by saying ar-Rahimu Akbar or Ajall, as stated in al-Muhit, al-Bada'i, and al-Khulasa, and it is stated in al-Mujtaba that this is the correct view, and al-Marghinani gave fatwa accordingly. So what is in al-Dhakhirah from the Fatawa of al-Fadli that one does not become a shar'i by ar-Rahim is weak. And it is restricted in Sharh al-Munyah by that it is not accompanied by something that invalidates the prayer; but if accompanied by such, then unanimously one does not become a shar'i, like saying 'the Knower of the non-existent and existent' or 'the states of creation', just as the saying that it is not permissible with every common noun is restricted to when it is not accompanied by what removes its commonality; if accompanied by what removes it, it does not invalidate the prayer, like saying meaning the intended, so that this is clear. His statement: (shuru') regarding the intended meaning of takbirat al-iftitah) apparently that this is from the author's statement 'kabbara', and the apparent is contrary, otherwise he would have said 'fa' and said 'law shar'a', but his intended meaning is the apparent wording of takbir because it is wajib for one who intends to begin, and his statement 'law shar'a' is an explanation of the validity of beginning with other than it, so his words are to be interpreted as that the intended meaning is from the hadith, not from the author's words. His statement: (thumma ghayat ma huna) the text is His statement 'and mention the name of his Lord and pray' [87:15], and dhikr includes takbir and other, and the wording of takbir is established by the hadith mentioned, and it is with the Powerful over everything, the Merciful to His servants, the Knower of the unseen and the witnessed, so one should become a shar'i by their agreement. End. And he indicated by mentioning tasbih and tahlil that one does not become a shar'i except with a complete sentence, so one does not become a shar'i by the subject alone like 'Allah' or 'Akbar', and this is the apparent riwayah as transmitted in al-Tajrid. And it is reasoned that exaltation, which is the meaning of takbir, is a predicate (hukm) on the exalted one, so there must be a predicate. And some said: one becomes a shar'i by every single name, subject and predicate, no difference between the word of majesty and others, and this is the riwayah of Hasan. And Qadikhan differentiated in his Fatawa regarding words: if one says 'Allah' or 'al-Rabb' and does not add, he becomes a shar'i; if he says 'al-Kabir' or 'al-Akbar' clearly or says 'Akbar', he does not become a shar'i. It is said in Fath al-Qadir: the difference is specificity in absolute usage or its absence. And the benefit of the difference appears in issues: one, that a menstruating woman if she becomes pure at the end of ten days and in the time there is room only for the noble name, that prayer is not obligatory on her according to the apparent riwayah, but is obligatory according to that riwayah. Another: when one catches the imam in bowing and says 'Allahu Akbar' such that his saying 'Allah' was while standing and his saying 'Akbar' was while bowing, he becomes a shar'i according to Hasan's riwayah, not according to the apparent, but what is in al-Khaniyah and al-Khulasa is that he does not become a shar'i and they did not mention other, so it seems they built it on the chosen opinion. Another: if his saying 'Allah' coincides with the imam and 'Akbar' comes before, he does not become a shar'i according to the apparent. And if he explains in Persian, then it is valid because we explained that takbir is exaltation and it is attained in any language, because the principle in texts is rationale ('illah) so one does not deviate from it except with proof, so it is like faith: if one believed in non-Arabic it is valid by consensus because the purpose is achieved, and similarly talbiyah in hajj, the greeting (salam), and saying the name at slaughter are permissible as will come. Abu Hanifa regarding Arabic so that one becomes a shar'i by other than the wording of takbir from Arabic when it indicates exaltation, and with Abu Yusuf regarding Persian such that one does not become a shar'i in prayer with it when one knows Arabic well, and on this difference are the khutbah, qunut, and tashahhud, and in adhan custom (ta'aruf) is considered. And Muhammad (related to) Arabic, built on meaning, constancy on it indicates obligation not obligation (fard) to avoid adding to the text. If you say: It previously passed that they (the two) interpreted takbir as exaltation, so how can it be said that the wording of takbir is established by report? I say: The apparent is that it is terminological or that it is determined by constancy. His statement: (that prayer is not obligatory on her) said in al-Nahr: but in 'Uqad al-Fara'id the fatwa is on obligation. His statement: (before it) i.e. before his completion by the imam prolonging the takbir. His statement: (and in adhan custom is considered) said in al-Nahr: except that in Adhan al-Siraj it is said: the correct view is that it is not valid even if it is known that it is an adhan. The author's statement: as if he recited it while unable, in al-Nahr he said: the condition of inability indicates that with ability it is not permissible, and this is what the Imam returned to as narrated by Nuh ibn Abi Maryam and al-Razi, and it is the correct view, and this is more appropriate than the commentator's saying 'it is valid by consensus'. I say: his restriction by inability here without the beginning indicates that the chosen view regarding beginning is the madhhab of the Imam that it is valid in Persian without inability; rather, Shaykh Ala al-Din al-Haskafi transmitted from al-Tatarkhaniyyah that he made it like talbiyah, permissible by agreement. Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary (sharh) on Kanz al-Daqa'iq addressing the takbirat al-ihram (opening takbir) of prayer. The author first discusses the ruling that the specific phrase 'Allahu Akbar' is the prescribed wording, but also addresses a dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that only 'Allahu Akbar' is valid, while his two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that any word conveying the meaning of ta'zim (exaltation) suffices, such as 'Allahu A'zam' or 'Ar-Rahmanu Akbar'. The proof cited is the Quranic verse (17:110) that allows calling on Allah or Ar-Rahman, and the hadith that 'the key to prayer is purification and its prohibition is takbir'. The commentary then explains that the obligation (wujub) of using this specific wording is derived from the Prophet's constant practice (muwazabah). Opening prayer with other than 'Allahu Akbar' is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) for one who knows it. The author then refutes al-Sarakhsi's view that it is not makruh and the author of al-Mustasfa's view that it is only wajib in Eid prayer. Next, the passage discusses conditions for alternative phrases to be valid: they must be a complete sentence (subject and predicate), not just a single word like 'Allah' or 'Akbar'. There are different opinions: the Zahir al-Riwayah requires a full sentence, while Hasan ibn Ziyad's riwayah allows any single word. Qadikhan differentiates between specific names (like 'Allah') and descriptive attributes (like 'al-Kabir'). The practical consequences of this difference are illustrated with examples: a menstruating woman who becomes pure at the end of the time for prayer, a person catching the imam in ruku', and the timing of parts of the takbir. Finally, the passage examines the validity of takbir in Persian. Abu Hanifa holds that takbir in any language is valid, even for one who knows Arabic, because the meaning is exaltation. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad restrict this to those unable to speak Arabic, and the same dispute applies to khutbah, qunut, tashahhud, and adhan (where custom is considered). The commentary concludes by noting the difference between obligation (wajib) and fard, emphasizing that the constant practice indicates wujub not fard to avoid adding to the text.

Key Terms
تكبير (takbir): The act of saying 'Allahu Akbar' or any phrase conveying exaltation of Allah, specifically for entering prayer (takbirat al-ihram).
شروع (shuru'): The act of beginning prayer, which is accomplished by the takbirat al-ihram.
شارع (shari'): One who has entered prayer by uttering the takbir; the predicate 'shari'an' means someone who has initiated the prayer.
كراهة تحريم (karahah tahrimiyyah): A prohibition that is close to haram, making the act sinful but not invalidating the prayer without compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what is the ruling for someone who knows Arabic but opens prayer by saying 'Allahu Kabir' instead of 'Allahu Akbar'?
A) The prayer is valid and there is no dislike.
B) The prayer is valid but it is makruh tahrimi.
C) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
D) The prayer is valid only if he is unable to say 'Allahu Akbar'.

Key Takeaway
The specific wording 'Allahu Akbar' for takbirat al-ihram is wajib; using other words of exaltation is makruh tahrimi for one who knows Arabic, but the prayer remains valid.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Conditions for Valid Takbir al-Tahrimah: Complete Sentence Required
Expansion of takbir wording requirements with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the zahir al-riwaya requirement for the wording of takbir al-tahrimah, identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on sufficient wording, and apply the rule to practical scenarios.

Core Idea
A valid takbir requires a complete sentence—subject and predicate—to enter prayer; isolated words do not suffice.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq expands on the requirement for the wording of the opening takbir. While it is settled that takbir is wajib, a dispute arises within the Hanafi school about the exact minimum wording. The commentator clarifies that according to the authoritative zahir al-riwaya, only a complete sentence like 'Allahu Akbar' qualifies, because the very meaning of takbir is magnification (ta'zim), which is a predicate requiring a subject. However, alternative riwayas exist, leading to practical differences in certain cases such as the menstruating woman with limited time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the opening takbir (takbir al-tahrimah). Its hukm is wajib, as it is the condition for entering prayer.
2
State the zahir al-riwaya requirement
According to the transmitted core books, one becomes a shar'i only with a complete sentence (jumla tamma), e.g., 'Allahu Akbar'. Isolated words like 'Allah' or 'Akbar' are insufficient.
3
Understand the rationale (ta'lil)
The meaning of takbir is ta'zim (magnification), which is a predicate (khabar). A predicate requires a subject, so the complete sentence is necessary.
This is the core legal reasoning.
4
Explore the intra-Hanafi dispute
There are two other views: (a) Hasan ibn Ziyad's riwaya: any single noun or predicate suffices; (b) Qadikhan's distinction: certain names like 'Allah' or 'al-Rabb' suffice, but descriptive words like 'al-Kabir' or 'Akbar' do not.
These are minority views; the mufta bihi is the zahir al-riwaya.
5
Apply to practical cases (thamarah)
Two examples: (1) Menstruating woman with only time for 'Allah': according to zahir al-riwaya, prayer not obligatory; according to Hasan's riwaya, obligatory. (2) Takbir split between standing and bowing: according to zahir al-riwaya, not valid; according to Hasan's riwaya, valid. The relied-upon view is the zahir al-riwaya.
The thamarah shows the real-world impact of the dispute.
