القادر على كل شيء، والرحيم بعباده وعالم الغيب والشهادة، فينبغي أن يصير شارعاً باتفاقهم على قولهما .اهـ. وأشار بذكر التسبيح والتهليل إلى أنه لا يصير شارعاً إلا بجملة تامة فلا يصير شارعاً بالمبتدأ وحده كـ «الله» أو «أكبر) وهو ظاهر الرواية كما نقله في التجريد. وعلل له بأن التعظيم الذي هو معنى التكبير حكم على المعظم فلا بد من الخبر، ومنهم من قال : شارعاً يصير بكل اسم مفرداً وخبر لا فرق بين الجلالة وغيرها وهو رواية الحسن وفرق قاضيخان في فتاواه الألفاظ فقال : لو قال «الله» أو «الرب» ولم يزد يصير شارعاً، ولو قال «الكبير» أو «الأكبر» بين أو قال «أكبر» لا . يصير شارعاً. قال في فتح القدير : كان الفرق الاختصاص في الإطلاق وعدمه. وفائدة الاختلاف تظهر في مسائل منها : أن الحائض إذا طهرت على عشر وفي الوقت ما يسع الاسم الشريف فقط لا تجب تلك الصلاة عليها على ظاهر الرواية، وتجب على تلك الرواية. ومنها أنه ينبغي فيما إذا أدرك الإمام في الركوع فقال (الله أكبر» إلا أن قوله «الله». كان في قيامه وقوله «أكبر) كان في ركوعه أنه يكون شارعاً على رواية الحسن لا على الظاهر، لكن الذي في الخانية والخلاصة أنه لا يكون شارعاً ولم يحكيا غيره فكأنهما بنياه على القول المختار .
The One capable of everything, the Merciful to His servants, the Knower of the unseen and the witnessed. So it befits that one becomes a shar'i (entering prayer) by their agreement on his statement. End. And he indicated by mentioning tasbih and tahlil that one does not become a shar'i except with a complete sentence; so one does not become a shar'i with just a subject alone like 'Allah' or 'Akbar'. This is the zahir al-riwaya as transmitted in al-Tajrid. And he gave the reason that ta'zim (magnification) which is the meaning of takbir is a predicate upon the magnified, so a predicate is necessary. Among them is one who said: one becomes a shar'i with every single noun or predicate, no difference between the name of majesty and other names – this is the riwaya of al-Hasan. Qadikhan made a distinction in his Fatawa about the words; he said: if he says 'Allah' or 'al-Rabb' and did not add, he becomes a shar'i; if he says 'al-Kabir' or 'al-Akbar' clearly, or says 'Akbar', he does not become a shar'i. In Fath al-Qadir it is said: the difference is specificity in absolute use and lack thereof. The benefit of the difference appears in issues including: the menstruating woman when she becomes pure on the tenth day and there is only time for the noble name alone, that prayer is not obligatory on her according to the zahir al-riwaya, and is obligatory according to that other riwaya. And among them is: if he catches the imam in bowing and says 'Allah Akbar' except that his saying 'Allah' occurred while standing and his saying 'Akbar' occurred while bowing, then he becomes a shar'i according to the riwaya of al-Hasan, not according to the zahir. But what is in al-Khaniyya and al-Khulasa is that he does not become a shar'i, and they did not relate other than that, so it is as if they built it on the chosen view.
Source pages p. 535

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the ruling on the takbir al-tahrimah necessary to enter prayer. The base text states that one becomes a shar'i (i.e., enters the state of prayer) by the wording of takbir, but the commentator clarifies that this requires a complete sentence expressing magnification. According to the zahir al-riwaya, simply saying 'Allah' or 'Akbar' as an isolated word does not suffice, because the meaning of takbir is ta'zim (magnification), which is a predicate that must be attributed to a subject. Thus the complete phrase 'Allahu Akbar' is needed. However, there is a transmission from Imam al-Hasan ibn Ziyad that even a single word suffices, and Qadikhan distinguishes between specific names like 'Allah' and descriptive words like 'al-Akbar'. The practical consequence (thamarah) appears in two cases: a woman who becomes pure after hayd with time only for saying 'Allah' – according to the zahir al-riwaya she does not owe that prayer, but according to al-Hasan's riwaya she does. Similarly, if one's takbir is split between standing and bowing while catching the imam, some riwayas consider him a shar'i, but the relied-upon view (al-mukhtar) is that he is not.

Key Terms
صار شارعا (sara shar'i'an): Entered the state of prayer (ihram) by uttering the takbir al-tahrimah.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The transmitted ruling from Imam Muhammad's six core books, considered authoritative.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the zahir al-riwaya, does a woman who becomes pure from hayd with only enough time to say 'Allah' (without 'Akbar') owe that prayer?
A) Yes, because she became pure in time.
B) No, because she cannot complete the takbir with a full sentence.
C) Yes, according to all views.
D) No, because she is not obligated regardless.

Key Takeaway
The opening takbir must be a complete sentence of magnification ('Allahu Akbar'); isolated words do not suffice for entering prayer according to the authoritative Hanafi view.

Ruling on Takbir in Persian: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on permissible language for takbir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on takbir in Persian and identify the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
Takbir is ta'zim, but the Sahibayn restrict the language to Arabic if one is able.

This lesson examines the permissibility of saying the takbir and other formulas in Persian. Abu Hanifa held that meaning suffices, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad required Arabic when one is capable. We will explore the proofs, the practical consequence, and how this applies to other acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central act and its ruling
The act is takbir (saying 'Allahu Akbar'). Its ruling is wajib for entering prayer. The question is about the language used, which affects validity.
Takbir al-tahrimah is a rukn of prayer; the language condition is what is disputed.
2
Understand Abu Hanifa's reasoning
Abu Hanifa relies on the principle that texts are based on meaning (ta'lil). Takbir is ta'zim, achievable in any language. Analogy with iman, talbiyya, tasmiyya supports permissibility.
He argues that the essence is the magnification, not the specific Arabic wording.
3
Understand the Sahibayn's reasoning
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad emphasize the prophetic practice (tawqif) and the specific verbal form as part of the ritual. They restrict to Arabic if one is able.
They consider the wording a condition for validity, like the recitation of Fatiha.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if one prays with Persian takbir while able, prayer is invalid according to mufta bihi (Sahibayn), but valid per Abu Hanifa.
The mufta bihi follows the Sahibayn for caution in worship.
5
Apply to other formulas
The same difference applies to khutba, qunut, and tashahhud. For adhan, custom is considered, not language per se.
This consistency shows the principle extends beyond takbir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما إذا شرح بالفارسية فإنما يصح لما بيناه من أن التكبير هو التعظيم وهو حاصل بأي لسان كان، ولأن الأصل في النصوص التعليل فلا يعدل عنه إلا بدليل فهو كالإيمان فإنه لو آمن بغير العربية جاز إجماعاً لحصول المقصود وكذا التلبيه في الحج والسلام والتسمية عند الذبح بها يجوز كما سيأتي . أبي حنيفة في العربية حتى يصير شارعا بغير لفظ التكبير من العربية حيث دل على مع التعظيم، ومع أبي يوسف في الفارسية حتى لا يكون شارعا في الصلاة بها حيث كان يحسن ، وعلى هذا الخلاف الخطبة والقنوت والتشهد، وفي الأذان يعتبر التعارف .
And as for explaining (the takbir) in Persian, it is valid because of what we have explained: that takbir is ta'zim (magnification), and that is achieved in any language. And because the principle in texts is rationale, so one does not deviate from it except with proof. It is like iman (faith): if one affirms faith in other than Arabic, it is valid by consensus because the purpose is achieved. Similarly, talbiyya in Hajj, salam (greeting), and tasmiyya at slaughter are permissible as will come. Abu Hanifa: (requires) Arabic so that one becomes a shar'i with other than the verbal form of takbir from Arabic where it indicates ta'zim. And with Abu Yusuf: (requires) Persian so that one does not become a shar'i in prayer with it when he is competent (in Arabic). And on this difference are khutba, qunut, and tashahhud. Regarding adhan, customary familiarity is considered.
Source pages p. 535

Commentary
This ruling discusses whether the takbir al-tahrimah or other formulas like khutba, qunut, tashahhud can be said in Persian. The commentator argues that the essential meaning of takbir is ta'zim (magnification), and that is achieved in any language. Therefore, translating it into Persian is valid. This is analogous to the shahada (iman) which is valid in any language by consensus, and to talbiyya, salam, and tasmiyya. However, within the Hanafi school, there is a dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that one must use Arabic to become a shar'i; if one uses Persian but intends ta'zim, it is sufficient? The text says 'Abu Hanifa: in Arabic' meaning he requires Arabic wording for the takbir to be valid. Abu Yusuf requires Persian? Actually the text is unclear: 'مع أبي يوسف في الفارسية' – apparently Abu Yusuf requires Persian? That seems unlikely; the text might be corrupt. The standard position is that Abu Hanifa permits takbir in Persian even if one is able to speak Arabic, while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) do not permit it if one can speak Arabic. The text says: 'مع أبي يوسف في الفارسية حتى لا يكون شارعا في الصلاة بها حيث كان يحسن' meaning that according to Abu Yusuf, one does not become a shar'i with Persian if he is competent in Arabic. This is a known intra-madhhab khtilaf. The same difference applies to khutba, qunut, and tashahhud. For adhan, the criterion is what is customarily recognized as adhan, not language.

Key Terms
تكبير (takbir): Utterance of 'Allahu Akbar' or its equivalent in any language to express magnification of Allah.
الأصل في النصوص التعليل (al-aslu fi al-nususi al-ta'lil): The principle that legal texts are based on rational meaning (illa), not merely on literal wording.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, if a person who knows Arabic says the takbir in Persian to enter prayer, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is valid.
B) The prayer is invalid.
C) The prayer is makruh tanzihi.
D) The person becomes a shar'i and must repeat the takbir.

Key Takeaway
While Abu Hanifa permitted takbir in any language based on meaning, the mufta bihi restricts to Arabic when one is able, making prayer invalid if Persian is used.

Reciting Quran Translation in Prayer: The Hanafi Retraction
Examining permissibility of reciting Quran translation in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting Quran translation in prayer, explain the proof from the Quran, and distinguish between the initial and retracted positions of Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
Reciting a Quran translation in prayer invalidates it for one able to read Arabic; Abu Hanifa retracted and agreed with the Sahibayn.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq delves into a critical issue in Hanafi fiqh: the permissibility of reciting the Quran in Persian during salah. It traces the evolution of the school's position, from Abu Hanifa's initial allowance based on the linguistic meaning of 'Quran' to his retraction and adoption of the Sahibayn's stricter view. Understanding this retraction (ruju') is essential because it shows how the school's authoritative ruling (mufta bihi) can change when the evidence is re-evaluated.

Guided Path
1
Identify Abu Hanifa's initial position
Abu Hanifa initially allowed reciting Quran in Persian even if one knows Arabic, arguing that the essence of Quran is meaning, and 'Quran' linguistically includes any recited text.
He cited Q 41:44 'If We had made it a non-Arabic Quran' to argue that it would still be called Quran.
2
Trace the retraction
Abu Hanifa later retracted and agreed with Abu Yusuf and Muhammad that Persian recitation is not valid for the able. The new proof is Q 73:20 'so recite what is easy of the Quran' where the definite article indicates the specific Arabic revelation.
The retraction is based on legal custom and the specific usage of 'al-Quran' in the Shariah.
3
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that reciting a translation invalidates the prayer if the person is able to read Arabic. For the unable, it is valid by consensus.
This is the view of the Sahibayn, which Abu Hanifa adopted.
4
Distinguish between qira'ah and shuru'
The retraction only applies to recitation (qira'ah) of Quran, not to takbir (shuru'). For takbir, Abu Hanifa's view that Persian is valid remains the school's position.
Some later scholars confused the two issues; the text warns that al-Shurunbulali made this error.
5
Apply the ruling
Consider a person who knows Arabic but recites the translation of Surah al-Fatiha in Persian during prayer. According to the mufta bihi, the prayer is invalid. If the person is unable to read Arabic, the prayer is valid.
The ruling also distinguishes between verses of stories/commands (invalidates) and dhikr (does not invalidate), but the base rule for the able is invalidity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

His statement: 'as if he recited it (Quran) while unable' – al-Nahr said: the condition of inability indicates that it is not permissible when able, and that is what the Imam (Abu Hanifa) retracted to, as narrated by Nuh ibn Abi Maryam and al-Razi, and it is the soundest. This is better than the statement of the commentator 'it is valid by consensus'. End. I said: Its restriction to inability here as opposed to the start (takbir) indicates that the chosen view for the start is the Imam's view that it is valid in Persian without inability. Rather, Sheikh Ala al-Din al-Haskafi transmitted from al-Tatarkhaniyya that he made it like talbiyya: permissible by agreement. As for the statement of al-`Ayni in his commentary: 'They said it is not permissible except' – from his statement: 'as if he recited it while unable', meaning if he recited in Persian while unable to do Arabic, it is valid by consensus. He restricted it to inability because if he were able, it is not valid unanimously according to the correct view. Abu Hanifa initially would say validity, considering that Arabic is not taken as a condition for the meaning of Quran; hence His saying 'And if We had made it a non-Arabic Quran' (Fussilat 44) implies it would still be called Quran if non-Arabic. Then he retracted and agreed with the two companions on non-permissibility, which is the truth, because the meaning of Quran with the definite article is the Arabic one in the legal custom, which is what is required from His saying 'so recite what is easy of the Quran' (Muzammil 20). As for the Quran of the indefinite (Qur'anan), no transmission is known transferring it from the linguistic meaning, so it encompasses every recited thing. And what was said that the composition is for i'jaz, and in prayer the purpose of Quran is munajat (intimate conversation) not i'jaz, so composition is not necessary in it – this is rejected, because it is opposing the text with meaning, for the text demands Arabic, and this reasoning permits other than it. The discussion on this issue is extensive in principles and branches. The restriction to Persian is not to exclude other languages, for the correct view is that Persian and others are the same; so his intention by Persian is non-Arabic. And translation is not permissible by consensus because it is the speech of people. In al-Hidaya: the disagreement is about permissibility when one is content with it (i.e., only translation), but there is no disagreement about invalidity (fasad) if he also recites in Arabic the amount that makes the prayer valid; then his prayer is valid. In Fatawa Qadikhan: it invalidates according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The reconciliation between them is by carrying what is in al-Hidaya to the case where it is dhikr or glorification, and carrying what is in the Fatawa to the case where the recited content is stories, commands, and prohibitions, like shadhdh qira'ah. For they explicitly said in the branches that one is not content with it and it does not invalidate. In Fath: 'when unable, and the three (i.e., Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) said this, and the fatwa is upon it, and the unretraction of Abu Hanifa to the view of the two is correct' – that is confusing the issue of recitation with the issue of start. Sheikh Ala al-Din objected saying: he has no predecessor nor support for it, rather the apparent of al-Tatarkhaniyya is that the two retracted to him, not he to them. So preserve this, for it has confused many deficient ones even al-Shurunbulali in all his books, so be careful. In summary, it is confirmed that the Imam retracted to the view of the two companions in the issue of recitation; as for the issue of start (takbir), the correct is the Imam's view, rather the implication of the Tatarkhaniyya is that it is agreed upon. So the retraction is from them to him, not from him to them. His statement: 'The reconciliation between them' – al-Nahr said: In al-Qadir he chose that if the recited is stories or commands or prohibitions, the prayer is invalid; if it is dhikr or glorification, it is not. I (the commentator) say: It should be that the two parts of this statement are carried on the two views. And what supports this choice is what is in al-Khulasa about a slip of the reciter: if he substitutes a Quranic word with another similar in meaning, if it is from stories and the like, the prayer is invalid; if it is praise, glorification, or dhikr, it is not. End of al-Nahr's speech. I say: It has just passed that the one unable in Arabic, his recitation in Persian is valid by consensus. So if stories invalidate by consensus because he becomes a speaker thereby as said in Fath, then the unable would be forced to remain silent if he knows only stories, unless one claims that the consensus is specific to other than stories. His statement: 'like shadhdh qira'ah' – al-Nahr said: In my view there is a difference between them: because Persian while able to read Arabic is not Quran at all due to it being diverted from
Source pages p. 535

Commentary
This passage discusses the crucial issue: can one recite the Quran in Persian translation during prayer? The initial view of Abu Hanifa allowed it even if one knows Arabic, based on the idea that the essence of Quran is the meaning, and the word 'Quran' linguistically includes any recited text. He cited the verse 'If We had made it a non-Arabic Quran' (41:44) implying it would still be called Quran. However, he later retracted and agreed with Abu Yusuf and Muhammad that it is not permissible when able, due to the legal convention that 'al-Quran' refers specifically to the Arabic revelation. The proof is the command 'faqra'u ma tayassara min al-Quran' (73:20) where the definite article indicates the known Arabic Quran. Thus, reciting a translation is like reciting human speech, which invalidates prayer if it replaces the required recitation. There is no dispute that if one is unable to read Arabic, reciting the translation is valid by consensus. For the able, the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that it is invalid. Further, there is a distinction: if one recites the translation of verses containing stories, commands, or prohibitions, it invalidates the prayer absolutely; if it is dhikr (remembrance) or glorification, it may not invalidate. This is analogous to shadhdh qira'ah (non-mutawatir recitations). However, if one recites both the Arabic original and the translation, the prayer is valid. The commentator also clarifies that the retraction of Abu Hanifa is only in the issue of reading Quran, not in the issue of takbir (shuru'), where his view remains that Persian is valid. There is confusion among later scholars, but the correct position is that Abu Hanifa retracted to the Sahibayn in qira'ah, while in shuru' the Sahibayn retracted to him.

Key Terms
قراءة بالفارسية (qira'ah bi al-farisiyyah): Reciting a Persian translation of Quranic verses in prayer, intending it as Quran recitation.
رجوع (ruju'): Retraction of an earlier opinion; here Abu Hanifa retracted his view allowing Persian Quran recitation for the able.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person who knows Arabic recites the translation of Surah al-Fatiha in Persian during prayer, what is the ruling according to the mufta bihi?
A) The prayer is valid because the meaning is conveyed.
B) The prayer is invalid because Arabic is required.
C) The prayer is valid but makruh.
D) The prayer requires sajdah al-sahw.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that reciting a Quran translation in prayer invalidates it if the person is able to read Arabic; for the unable, it is valid by consensus.

Reciting Persian in Prayer: Dispute and Ruling
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Persian recitation in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on reciting Persian in prayer for the capable and incapable, and explain the evidence and retraction of Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
Reciting Persian in prayer is valid only for those incapable of Arabic; the capable invalidate their prayer.

Can a person recite the Quran in their own language during prayer? The Hanafi school addresses this with a nuanced position, distinguishing between those who can read Arabic and those who cannot. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the intra-Hanafi dispute, Abu Hanifa's initial view and retraction, and the final mufta bihi ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage distinguishes between a person capable of Arabic and one incapable. Note that the ruling differs for each.
2
Trace the dispute
Abu Hanifa initially held Persian recitation valid even for the capable; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) held it invalid. Abu Hanifa later retracted.
Find the evidence each side used: the linguistic vs. Shariah custom of 'Quran'.
3
Analyze the evidence
The key verse is 'فاقرءوا ما تيسر من القرآن' (Muzzammil:20) — the definite article 'al' in 'al-Quran' refers to Arabic by Shariah custom. The verse 'ولو جعلناه قرآناً أعجمياً' (Fussilat:44) was used by Abu Hanifa initially.
Understand the qiyas khafi based on urf.
4
Apply the final ruling
The mufta bihi: For the capable, Persian recitation invalidates the prayer; for the incapable, it is valid. Also, if the Persian recitation consists of dhikr/tasbih versus stories/commands, it may affect validity.
Check the reconciliation between al-Hidayah and Fatawa Qadikhan.
5
Distinguish from commencement issue
The passage warns confusion with another issue: starting prayer with Persian phrases. Abu Hanifa's retraction is specifically about recitation, not commencement.
Memorize this distinction to avoid error.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رجع عن قوله : (كما لو قرأ بها عاجزاً) أي لو قرأ بالفارسية حالة العجز عن العربية فإنه يصح، وهذا بالاتفاق. قيد بالعجز لأنه لو كان قادراً فإنه لا يصح اتفاقاً على الصحيح وكان أبو حنيفة أولا يقول بالصحة نظراً إلى عدم أخذ العربية في مفهوم القرآن ولذا قال تعالى {ولو جعلناه قرآناً أعجمياً} [فصلت: ٤٤] فإنه يستلزم تسميته قرآناً أيضاً لو كان أعجمياً، ثم هذا القول ووافقهما في عدم الجواز وهو الحق لأن المفهوم من القرآن باللام إنما هم العربي في عرف الشرع وهو المطلوب من قوله تعالى {فاقرءوا ما تيسر من القرآن} [المزمل: ٢٠] وأما قرآن المنكر فلم يعهد فيه نقل عن المفهوم اللغوي فيتناول كل مقروء. وما قيل النظم مقصود للإعجاز وحالة الصلاة المقصود من القرآن فيها المناجاة لا الإعجاز فلا يكون النظم لازماً فيها فمردود، لأنه معارضة للنص بالمعنى فإن النص طلب بالعربي وهذا التعليل يجيزه بغيرها، والكلام في هذه المسألة كثير أصولاً وفروعاً. والتقييد بالفارسية ليس للاحتراز عن غيرها فإن الصحيح أن الفارسية وغيرها سواء فحينئذ كان مراده من الفارسية غير العربية. ولا يجوز بالتفسير إجماعاً لأنه كلام الناس وفي الهداية: والخلاف في الجواز إذا اكتفي به، ولا خلاف في عدم الفساد حتى إذا قرأ معه بالعربية قدر ما تجوز به الصلاة جازت صلاته. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان : إنها تفسد عندهما والتوفيق بينهما بحمل ما في الهداية على ما إذا كان ذكراً أو تنزيهاً. ويحمل ما في الفتاوى على ما إذا كان المقروء من مكان القصص والأمر والنهي كالقراءة الشاذة فإنهم صرحوا في الفروع أنه لا يكتفي بها ولا تفسد. وفي فتح عند العجز وبه قالت الثلاثة وعليه الفتوى وصح رجوع أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى إلى قولهما» اهـ. فهو اشتباه مسألة القراءة بمسألة الشروع، وقد اعترضه الشيخ علاء الدين رحمه الله فقال : لا سلف له فيه ولا سند يقويه بل ظاهر التتارخانية رجوعهما إليه لا هو إليهما فاحفظه فقد اشتبه على كثير من القاصرين حتى الشرنبلالي في كل كتبه فتنبه .اهـ. والحاصل أنه قد ثبت رجوع الإمام إلى قولهما في مسألة القراءة، وأما مسألة الشروع فالصحيح قول الإمام فيها بل مقتضى كلام التتارخانية أنها اتفاقية وعليه فيكون الرجوع منهما إليه لا منه إليهما قوله : (والتوفيق بينهما (الخ) قال في النهر : اختار في القدير أن المقروء إن كان قصصاً أو أمراً أو نهياً فسدت وإن ذكراً أو تنزيهاً. لا أقول: وينبغي يكون شقي هذا القول محمولاً على القولين ويشهد لهذا الاختيار ما في الخلاصة من زلة القارىء لو أبدل كلمة من القرآن بأخرى تقاربها في المعنى أن من القصص ونحوها فسدت وإن حمداً أو تنزيهاً أو ذكراً لا . اهـ . كلام النهر أقول: قد مر آنفاً أن العاجز عن العربية تصح قراءته بالفارسية اتفاقاً، فلو كان القصص مفسداً اتفاقاً لكونه يصير به متكلماً كما قاله في الفتح للزم العاجز السكوت إن لم يعرف غير القصص إلا أن يدعي تخصيص الاتفاق بغير القصص. قوله : (كالقراءة الشاذة الخ) قال في النهر : عندي بينهما فرق وذلك أن الفارسي مع القدرة على العربي ليس قرآناً أصلاً لانصرافه في عرف الشرع إلى العربي، فإذا قرأ قصة صار متكلماً بكلام الناس بخلاف الشاذ فإنه قرآن إلا أن في قرآنيته شكاً فلا تفسد به ولو قصة وحكوا الاتفاق فيه على عدمه فالأوجه ما في المحيط من : تأويله كلام شمس الأئمة بما إذا اقتصر عليه .اهـ. أي أنه إذا اقتصر على الشاذ تفسد لتركه فرض القراءة لا أن الفاسد به.
He retracted from his statement: (as if he recited it while incapable) meaning if he recited in Persian while incapable of Arabic, it is valid, and this is by agreement. He restricted it to incapacity because if he were capable, it is not valid by agreement according to the correct view. Abu Hanifa initially held validity based on the fact that Arabic is not a condition for the concept of Quran, and Allah said {And if We had made it a non-Arabic Quran} [Fussilat:44], which implies it would still be called Quran if non-Arabic. Then he retracted and agreed with the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) on impermissibility, which is the truth, because the understood meaning of 'al-Quran' by the definite article is only Arabic in the custom of the Law, and that is required by His statement {So recite whatever is easy of the Quran} [Muzzammil:20]. As for a Quran rejected, no transfer from the linguistic concept is known, so it includes every recited thing. And what is said that the composition is intended for inimitability, while in prayer the purpose of the Quran is supplication not inimitability, so composition is not necessary in it, is rejected because it opposes the text with meaning; the text requires Arabic, and this reasoning permits other than it. The discussion on this issue is extensive in usul and furu'. The restriction to Persian is not to exclude other languages, for the correct view is that Persian and others are the same; so by 'Persian' he meant non-Arabic. Translation is not permissible by consensus because it is speech of people. In al-Hidayah: The disagreement is about permissibility when he suffices with it; there is no disagreement about invalidity not occurring, such that if he recites with it in Arabic to the extent that the prayer is valid, his prayer is valid. In Fatawa Qadikhan: It invalidates according to the two (Sahibayn). The reconciliation between them is by interpreting what is in al-Hidayah as when it is dhikr or tasbih, and what is in the Fatawa as when the recited part is from stories, commands, and prohibitions, like irregular recitations (shadhdh), for they stated in the branches that it is not sufficient and does not invalidate. In Fath: 'when incapable, and the three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) said so, and the fatwa is upon it, and the retraction of Abu Hanifa to their view is confirmed.' So there is confusion between the issue of recitation and the issue of commencement. Shaykh Ala al-Din objected saying: 'he has no predecessor in this nor any support; rather the apparent meaning of al-Tatarakhaniyya is their retraction to him, not he to them. Memorize this, for it has confused many deficient ones, even al-Shurunbulali in all his books, so beware.' The conclusion: The Imam's retraction to their view in the issue of recitation is confirmed. As for the issue of commencement, the correct view is the Imam's statement therein; rather, the implication of al-Tatarakhaniyya is that it is agreed upon, so the retraction would be from them to him, not from him to them. His statement: (and the reconciliation between them etc.) Al-Nahr said: He chose in al-Qadir that if what is recited is stories, commands, or prohibitions, it invalidates; but if it is dhikr or tasbih, no. I say: It should be that the two parts of this statement are carried on the two views. This choice is supported by what is in al-Khulasa regarding a reciter's slip: if he substitutes a word of the Quran with another similar in meaning, if it is stories and the like, it invalidates; but if it is praise, tasbih, or dhikr, no. End of al-Nahr's words. I say: It has just been mentioned that the one incapable of Arabic having his Persian recitation valid is agreed upon. So if stories were invalidating by agreement because he becomes a speaker as stated in al-Fath, the incapable person would have to remain silent if he knows only stories, unless the agreement is specified to other than stories. His statement: (like irregular recitations etc.) Al-Nahr said: In my view there is a difference: The one who is capable of Arabic reciting Persian is not Quran at all because in the custom of the Law it is turned to Arabic, so if he recites a story he becomes a speaker of people's speech, unlike irregular recitation, for it is Quran except that there is doubt about its being Quran, so it does not invalidate even if it is a story. They related agreement on its non-invalidity. The most appropriate is what is in al-Muhit: interpreting Shams al-A'imma's statement as when he confines himself to it. That is, if he confines himself to irregular recitation, it invalidates due to abandoning the obligatory recitation, not because it is invalidating.
Source pages p. 536

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding reciting the Quran in Persian (or any non-Arabic language) in prayer. The author explains that if a person is unable to recite Arabic, there is consensus that Persian recitation is valid. For one who is capable, the correct position is that it is invalid, though Abu Hanifa initially held it valid based on the Quranic verse 'ولو جعلناه قرآناً أعجمياً' which implies that a non-Arabic Quran is still called Quran. However, he retracted and agreed with Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) that it is impermissible. The proof is that the term 'al-Quran' in the verse 'فاقرءوا ما تيسر من القرآن' is understood in the Shariah to refer to the Arabic Quran. The author then discusses the reconciliation between conflicting reports in al-Hidayah and Fatawa Qadikhan, concluding that if the Persian recitation consists of dhikr or tasbih it does not invalidate, but if it includes stories, commands, or prohibitions it does. The passage also clarifies a common confusion: the retraction of Abu Hanifa occurred in the issue of recitation, not in the issue of commencing prayer (which is a separate matter). The weight is on the fatwa of the Sahibayn for the incapable, and the ruling of Abu Hanifa for the capable (i.e., invalidity). Finally, the author distinguishes between Persian recitation (which is not Quran at all) and irregular recitations (which are Quran but with doubt), explaining that the latter do not invalidate the prayer unless one confines oneself to them.

Key Terms
القراءة بالفارسية (al-qira'ah bil-farisiya): Reciting the Quran in Persian translation or non-Arabic language instead of the original Arabic in prayer.
العاجز عن العربية (al-'ajiz an al-'arabiya): A person who cannot recite Arabic due to inability (e.g., non-Arab or unable to learn).
القراءة الشاذة (al-qira'ah al-shadhdhah): Recitations of the Quran that have not reached the level of tawatur (mutawatir) and are considered irregular or non-canonical.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for a person capable of Arabic who recites the Quran in Persian during prayer?
A) The prayer is valid because Persian is also Quran.
B) The prayer is invalid because reciting Persian when capable of Arabic invalidates the prayer.
C) The prayer is valid if the Persian recitation contains dhikr or tasbih.
D) The prayer is valid but requires sajdah al-sahw.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that reciting the Quran in Persian is valid in prayer only for those incapable of Arabic; for those capable, it invalidates the prayer, based on the Shariah custom that 'al-Quran' refers specifically to the Arabic revelation.

Tasmiya for Slaughter: The Condition of Dhikr
Ruling on tasmiya for slaughter: condition is dhikr, any language valid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the condition for valid slaughter is dhikr of Allah in any language.

Core Idea
For slaughter, any dhikr of Allah in any language fulfills the condition by consensus.

This lesson clarifies the straightforward ruling on saying the name of Allah during slaughter. The condition is simply mentioning Allah, and it is achieved in any language, as agreed upon by Hanafi scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its condition
The act is slaughter (dhabh), and the condition is tasmiya (saying Allah's name).
Tasmiya is wajib.
2
Recognize the nature of the condition
The condition is dhikr (remembrance) of Allah, not a specific formula.
3
Note the language scope
Dhikr is achieved in any language, so Arabic is not required.
By agreement (ittifaq).
4
Apply the ruling
Any phrase that clearly mentions Allah suffices, e.g., 'Bismillah' in any language.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أو ذبح وسمى بها) اتفاقاً لأن الشرط فيه الذكر وهو حاصل بأي لسان كان قوله (لا باللهم اغفر لي) أي لا يكون شارعاً في الصلاة ولا مسمياً على الذبيحة بقوله اللهم اغفر لي لأنه ليس بثناء خالص بل مشوب بحاجته قيد به لأنه لو قال اللهم اختلفوا فيه والصحيح الجواز كذا في المحيط. وأشار إلى أنه لو قال اللهم أرزقني أو قال استغفر الله أو أعوذ بالله أو لا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله أو ما شاء الله فإنه لا يكون شارعاً كما يصير في المنية، ولو قال الله الرحمن الرحيم ففي المبتغى والمجتبى يجوز، وفي الذخيرة لا يجوز معللاً بأن التسمية للتبرك فكأنه قال بارك لي في هذا الأمر، وفي شرح المنية هو الأشبه قال في النهر وفي السراج هو الأصح.
His statement: (or slaughtered and mentioned the name upon it) by agreement, because the condition is dhikr, and it is achieved in any language. His statement: (not by 'Allahumma ighfir li') meaning he does not become a starter in prayer nor a namer on the slaughtered animal by saying 'Allahumma ighfir li' because it is not pure praise but mixed with need. He restricted it because if he said 'Allahumma', they differed, and the correct is permissibility, as in al-Muhit. And he indicated that if he said 'Allahumma arzuqni' or said 'Astaghfirullah' or 'A'udhu billah' or 'La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' or 'Ma sha' Allah', then he does not become a starter (in prayer) as it becomes in al-Munya. And if he said 'Allah al-Rahman al-Rahim', then in al-Mubtagha and al-Mujtaba it is permissible, and in al-Dhakhira it is not permissible, reasoned that the tasmiya is for blessing, as if he said 'Bless me in this matter'. In Sharh al-Munya, it is more appropriate (ashbah). In al-Nahr and al-Siraj, it is the most correct (asahh).
Source pages p. 537

Commentary
This passage covers two rulings: First, for slaughtering an animal, saying any name of Allah (including 'Bismillah') is valid by agreement, as the condition is simply dhikr of Allah in any language. Second, for commencing prayer, saying 'Bismillah' is disputed. According to al-Mubtagha and al-Mujtaba, it is permissible; according to al-Dhakhira, it is not, because 'Bismillah' is considered a blessing (tabarruk), akin to saying 'Bless me in this matter', which is not pure praise but a request. The author notes that the view of permissibility is considered 'ashbah' (more appropriate) in Sharh al-Munya, and 'asahh' (most correct) in al-Nahr and al-Siraj. Therefore, the mufta bihi is that saying 'Bismillah' to commence prayer is valid according to the more correct view, though there is some disagreement. The passage also clarifies that other phrases like 'Allahumma arzuqni' (supplication) or 'Astaghfirullah' (seeking forgiveness) do not count as commencement because they are requests or supplications, not praise.

Key Terms
التسمية (al-tasmiya): The act of saying the name of Allah, especially 'Bismillah', for slaughter or for commencing an act.
الذبح (al-dhabh): Slaughtering an animal for consumption; requires saying the name of Allah (tasmiya) as a condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is true regarding saying the name of Allah during slaughter?
A) Only Arabic is allowed.
B) Any language is valid because the condition is dhikr.
C) It is recommended but not obligatory.
D) It must be said loudly.

Key Takeaway
For slaughter, any dhikr of Allah in any language fulfills the condition, by agreement.

Saying 'Bismillah' to Commence Prayer: The Correct Hanafi View
Ruling on 'Bismillah' for prayer commencement: intra-Hanafi dispute resolved by tarjih.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on saying 'Bismillah' to commence prayer and state the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Saying 'Bismillah' to commence prayer is valid because it is praise, not a request, per the more correct view.

This lesson addresses a nuanced issue: whether saying 'Bismillah' can serve as the opening phrase for prayer. Some Hanafi scholars argue it is invalid because it is a blessing request, but the later authoritative view considers it valid as praise. The passage also clarifies that other supplications are clearly invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed act
The act is commencing prayer (shuru') with the phrase 'Bismillah' (or 'Allah al-Rahman al-Rahim').
2
Note the two Hanafi positions
al-Mubtagha and al-Mujtaba say it is valid; al-Dhakhira says it is invalid.
Both are Hanafi authorities.
3
Understand the reasoning for invalidity
al-Dhakhira argues that tasmiya is for tabarruk (blessing), like saying 'Barik li', which is a request not suitable for commencement.
4
Recognize the tarjih
Sharh al-Munya calls it 'ashbah' (more appropriate), and al-Nahr and al-Siraj call it 'asahh' (most correct) to permit it.
Thus the mufta bihi is validity.
5
Distinguish from other invalid phrases
Supplications like 'Allahumma arzuqni' or 'Astaghfirullah' are not valid because they are pure requests, not praise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

His statement: (or slaughtered and mentioned the name upon it) by agreement, because the condition is dhikr, and it is achieved in any language. Commentary
This passage covers two rulings: First, for slaughtering an animal, saying any name of Allah (including 'Bismillah') is valid by agreement, as the condition is simply dhikr of Allah in any language. Second, for commencing prayer, saying 'Bismillah' is disputed. According to al-Mubtagha and al-Mujtaba, it is permissible; according to al-Dhakhira, it is not, because 'Bismillah' is considered a blessing (tabarruk), akin to saying 'Bless me in this matter', which is not pure praise but a request. The author notes that the view of permissibility is considered 'ashbah' (more appropriate) in Sharh al-Munya, and 'asahh' (most correct) in al-Nahr and al-Siraj. Therefore, the mufta bihi is that saying 'Bismillah' to commence prayer is valid according to the more correct view, though there is some disagreement. The passage also clarifies that other phrases like 'Allahumma arzuqni' (supplication) or 'Astaghfirullah' (seeking forgiveness) do not count as commencement because they are requests or supplications, not praise.

Key Terms
التسمية (al-tasmiya): The act of saying the name of Allah, especially 'Bismillah', for slaughter or for commencing an act.
اللهم (Allahumma): A supplicatory form of 'Allah', often used in du'a.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the more correct (asahh) view in the Hanafi school, which of the following is valid for commencing prayer?
A) 'Allahumma arzuqni'
B) 'Astaghfirullah'
C) 'Bismillah'
D) 'La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah'

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi permits saying 'Bismillah' to open the prayer because it is praise, not a request.

Salah — Prayer

The Manner and Timing of Hand Placement in Prayer
Expanding ruling of hand placement with manner, time, and intra-Hanafi dispute on qawmah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the preferred Hanafi manner of hand placement and identify the standing positions where placement is sunnah.

Core Idea
Hand placement is sunnah only in stable standings with prescribed dhikr; its manner combines grasping and placing to harmonize divergent hadiths.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author expands on the ruling of hand placement (wad') in prayer. While the base text of Kanz al-Daqa'iq simply states that the right hand is placed on the left under the navel, the commentary clarifies two critical aspects: the precise manner (kayfiyyah) and the exact timing (waqt). Both were left unspecified in Zahir al-Riwayah, leading to scholarly discussion. You will learn the preferred Hanafi position on how to place hands and in which positions it is considered sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the act of hand placement (wad') is and its legal classification. Is it fard, wajib, sunnah, or something else?
The passage states it is a sunnah, but confirm the category: sunnah muakkadah.
2
Analyze the manner of placement
The author mentions that the manner was not specified in Zahir al-Riwayah. Look for the preferred method among later scholars: combining grasping the wrist and placing the hand.
The chosen view is to take the wrist with the thumb and little finger, placing the rest.
3
Determine the time of placement
According to Zahir al-Riwayah, placement is done after the takbir during any standing that has stability (qarar) and prescribed dhikr (thana', qunut, etc.).
Note the condition: 'qiyam lahu qarar'.
4
Identify exceptions
The passage explicitly says it is not sunnah for the one praying sitting. Also, the qawmah is later discussed as an exception.
The general rule is limited to prolonged standings.
5
Compare with other schools
The Shafi'i school places hands in all standings including sitting and the qawmah. This shows the Hanafi particularization.
This cross-madhhab comparison helps understand the distinct Hanafi criterion.

And he places his right hand on his left under his navel, opening (with du'a) and seeking refuge silently for recitation, so the one who is preceded (masbuq) does not perform it. And the apparent statement of the commentator is to prefer it, and in Sharh al-Munyah it is the more appropriate, and it is preferable to give weight to permissibility because it is pure remembrance, as evidence by the basmalah on the slaughtered animal with the condition of pure remembrance therein due to His saying 'So mention the name of Allah upon them when lined up' [22:36] meaning purely. His statement (and he places his right on his left under his navel as we have previously mentioned, and he did not mention the manner of placement because it was not mentioned in Zahir al-Riwayah. And there is a difference of opinion on it, and the chosen view is that he takes the wrist with the little finger and thumb because taking necessitates placement and not vice versa, and this is because reports differed: some mention placement and some mention taking, so combining them acting on both evidences is better. And the author also did not mention the time of placement; so in Zahir al-Riwayah its time is when he finishes the takbir, and it is a sunnah of a standing that has stability (qiyam lahu qarar) in which there is prescribed dhikr, so he places during the praise (thana'), and in qunut, and the takbirs of the funeral prayer, and it was said it is sunnah only during recitation, so he does not place in these places. And they all agree that it is not sunnah for the one who prays sitting. Fatawa al-Marghinani that it is the correct one, then he said: so the preponderant regarding basmalah is non-acceptance, and the more preponderant i.e., in al-Bahr is acceptance. The author's statement 'and he places his right on his left' – said in al-Nahr: meaning palm on palm, and it is said on the wrist. Al-Ayni said it, and his statement admits both possibilities, and in it is an indication of explaining the manner; so what is in al-Bahr that he did not explain it due to its absence in Zahir al-Riwayah is subject to consideration. And from the second he grasps the left wrist with the right hand, and al-Hindawani chose it. And Muhammad said: he places them such that the wrist is in the middle of the palm. Al-Sarakhsi said: many scholars considered it good to take the wrist with the thumb and little finger and place the rest so that it combines between the two reported (narrations) of taking and placing in the sunnah, and it is the chosen view. End quote. In Mi'raj al-Dirayah after attributing this statement to al-Mujtaba, al-Zahirah, and al-Mabsut with the addition 'so as to act upon both hadiths and schools out of precaution', he said: and it was said this is outside the schools and hadiths, so acting upon it is not precaution. End quote. His statement: 'so it is a sunnah of a standing that has stability' – al-Ramli said: it is explicit that it is not sunnah for the one who prays sitting, and I have not seen anyone draw attention to this, and people are heedless of it. And if it is not sunnah for him, how should he place? Apparently he places his hands on his thighs and spreads his fingers as he does in the first and second sitting. Then I saw in Sharh al-Wiqayah called Tawfiq al-Inayah in explaining his statement 'and he places his right' etc., the picture of the issue: the praying person places his right palm on his left palm and forms a ring with the little finger and thumb on the wrist in the state of standing. End quote. So his statement 'in the state of standing' implies that he does not do that in the state of sitting – consider. And I saw in the books of the Shafi'is that he does in sitting as he does in standing. End quote. I said: his student Sheikh Alauddin al-Haskafi mentioned something similar and said: I have not seen it. Then he said: then I saw in Majma' al-Anhur that what is meant by 'standing' is more general because the sitting person does likewise. His statement: 'and they all agree' etc. – said in al-Nahr: there is consideration regarding the consensus. It was mentioned in al-Siraj from al-Nasafi, al-Hakim, al-Jurjani, and al-Fadli that he leans in the qawmah (standing after ruku'), the funeral prayer, and the extra takbirs of the Eid; it is appropriate for what the commentator narrated from some that it is sunnah for every standing. And Shaykh al-Islam narrated in one place that according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) he holds (i.e., places hands) in the qawmah that is between ruku' and sujud because in that standing there is prescribed dhikr, i.e., tasmi' (sami'a Allahu liman hamidah) or tahmid. And he singled out the two's statement because according to Muhammad it is sunnah during recitation, and according to the two it is Zahir al-Riwayah as in al-Siraj. And this reasoning with regard to the person led by the imam and the imam himself is precluded because it is not sunnah to place in the standing that intervenes between ruku' and sujud because it has no stability and no recitation in it. By this, what is in Fath al-Qadir is refuted: that the letting go in the qawmah according to the mentioned criterion requires that there is no prescribed dhikr in it; but this is only complete if it is said that tahmid and tasmi' are not sunnah in it but rather in the very transition to it, but this is contrary to the apparent texts, and the reality is that rarely does tasmi' occur except in the standing while combining between them. End quote. Because you know that their statement is only about qiyam that has stability. And in al-Qunyah: if he leaves tasmi' until he stands up straight, he does not do it, just as if he did not say the takbir while bending until he ruku' or sujud, he abandons it. And one should memorize this and observe each thing in its place. End quote. And it is explicit that the qawmah has no prescribed dhikr. And it is mentioned in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli that Shaykh al-Islam mentioned in Sharh Kitab al-Salah that he lets go (i.e., does not place hands) in the qawmah between ruku' and sujud according to the two's statement just as is the view of Muhammad. And in another place he mentioned that according to the two's statement one should hold (place hands) because in this standing there is prescribed dhikr, i.e., tasmi' or tahmid; and upon this the author of al-Multaqat relied. End quote. And it supports what the researcher examined earlier. And upon this, that tasmi' or tahmid is only sunnah in the state of transition; yes, for the one praying alone it is based on that he combines them (tasmi' and tahmid), as he says 'Rabbana laka al-hamd' when he stands upright, according to the apparent answer which is correct as in al-Qunyah. And we do not admit that this standing has absolutely no stability because of their statement that the one praying a supererogatory prayer, even if it is sunnah, it is sunnah for him to perform supplications like 'Fill the heavens and the earth...' after tahmid, and 'Allahumma ighfir li warhamni' between the two prostrations. And know that al-Hadadi restricted the letting go (of hands) in what has no prescribed dhikr to when the standing is not prolonged; but if it is prolonged he holds (places hands). And in al-Khulasa: likewise he lets go in Zahir al-Riwayah in every standing that has no dhikr and is not long; and this implies that the previous criterion should be increased with 'or is long' – and Allah is the granter of success. End quote. Sheikh Isma'il said after that: the commentary of Miskin narrated the restriction with 'long'. Al-Birjandi said: placement of the hand in the mentioned manner is sunnah in every standing in which dhikr is prescribed, whether the dhikr is obligatory, obligatory (wajib), or sunnah; and what is meant by 'prescribed' is legislated. And in Sharh Ibn Malik: so he places in the mentioned states according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) because what is narrated from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them) regarding the sunnah of placement is general in the states of standing, but the qawmah from ruku' is particularized from those states due to its lack of extension, so what remains besides it remains on the original. And similar is in Ghurar al-Adhkar and al-Manba'. And in the first two also in explaining the statement of Muhammad: because the legislation of placement is to prevent the blood from gathering in the fingertips, and that only occurs in the state where prolongation is sunnah, i.e., the state of recitation. End quote. And apparently this extension and prolongation is what is meant by the statement of al-Bahr 'has stability (luhu qarar)' – end of his words. Then he objected to al-Nahr regarding its transmission from al-Fadli about leaning that it is not correct; rather, what is in al-Siraj from him is that he lets go in the mentioned (situations). So the correct is not to mention him together with al-Nasafi and those after him. End quote. This is his objection to the reasoning in the statement of Shaykh al-Islam 'because in this standing there is prescribed dhikr' etc., and his interpretation of it for the one praying alone is not apparent because tasmi' and tahmid are remembrance with 'or' which denotes one of two things, and the one praying alone performs them both according to what he mentioned, so his submission (i.e., that it is only for the mufrid) is not correct even for the mufrid. Rather, the apparent is that it agrees with what was discussed in Fath al-Qadir as the author of al-Bahr said. So the statement of Shaykh al-Islam 'i.e., tasmi'' – meaning if it were
Source pages p. 538

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the ruling of placing hands during prayer. It opens by clarifying the manner of placement: the right hand is placed on the left under the navel. The author notes that the manner (kayfiyyah) is not specified in Zahir al-Riwayah, and there is a difference of opinion. The preferred view among later scholars is to grasp the left wrist with the thumb and little finger, while placing the remaining fingers on the forearm. This combines the two narrations (some mention 'placement', some mention 'grasping') and is chosen by al-Sarakhsi and many others. As for the time of placement, the passage explains that in Zahir al-Riwayah it is sunnah to place hands immediately after the takbir, and continues until the end of the standing position in which prescribed dhikr occurs. Thus, placement is done during the opening supplication (thana'), during qunut, and during the takbirs of the funeral prayer. However, there is a view that it is only sunnah during recitation (qira'ah), so one would not place in those other positions. The passage then extensively discusses the specific case of the qawmah (standing after ruku' before sujud). There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to Imam Muhammad, placement in the qawmah is not sunnah because it is a brief standing without recitation and without prescribed dhikr (since tasmi' and tahmid are part of the transition, not the standing itself). According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two companions, Sahibayn), placement is sunnah in the qawmah because there is prescribed dhikr (tasmi' or tahmid). The passage weighs the evidence, quoting from various later authorities such as Shaykh al-Islam and al-Multaqat, and concludes that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the qawmah is a standing without stability (qarar) and without prescribed dhikr, so hands are not placed. The passage also clarifies that one who prays sitting does not place hands at all, as the sunnah is only for qiyam that has stability. Finally, there is a discussion of whether the qawmah can be considered prolonged (tawil) – if it is prolonged, placement becomes sunnah even according to the hesitant views. The overall ruling: the sunnah of placing hands applies in every standing position that has prescribed dhikr and is extended; brief stances like the qawmah are excluded.

Key Terms
وضع (wad'): Placement of the right hand on the left during prayer; a sunnah act with differing opinions on manner and timing.
قومة (qawmah): The brief standing after rising from ruku' before going into sujud; a position where hand placement is disputed.
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani; the most authoritative transmission of Hanafi rulings.
سنة قيام له قرار (sunnatu qiyamin lahu qarar): A sunnah that applies to a standing position that has stability (i.e., is not a brief transition) and contains prescribed dhikr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, in which of the following positions is hand placement NOT sunnah?
A) During the opening supplication (thana')
B) During the standing after ruku' (qawmah)
C) During qunut in Witr
D) During the takbirs of the funeral prayer

Key Takeaway
Hand placement is a sunnah muakkadah performed after takbir in every stable standing that contains prescribed dhikr; it is not sunnah in sitting or in the brief qawmah unless prolonged.
